**Total Duration:** 60 hours
**Sections:** 30 sections × 2 hours each
**Exam Pass Target:** >71%
**Format:** ~2 hours per section (mix of reading, practical work, and review)

---

## Study Plan Overview

This plan is designed to progressively build mastery from fundamentals to advanced enterprise concepts. Each section includes reading, practical exercises where applicable, and knowledge consolidation.

**Recommended Pace:** 2–3 sections per day over 10–15 days for intensive study, or 1–2 sections per day over 3–4 weeks for balanced learning.

---

## 🏗️ Week 1: Foundations & Core Concepts

### 🔧 Section 1: GitHub Actions Fundamentals & Tooling (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [01-GitHub-Actions-VS-Code-Extension.md](01-GitHub-Actions-VS-Code-Extension.md)
**Overview:**

- GitHub Actions platform capabilities and use cases
- GitHub Actions VS Code Extension installation and setup
- YAML schema validation and IntelliSense features
- Local workflow validation with act or extension tools
- Best practices for local development and testing

**Deliverables:**

- Install and configure the VS Code extension
- Validate a sample workflow locally
- Understand extension features and troubleshooting


<details>
<summary>🔧 Scenario 1-A: Install & Configure the VS Code GitHub Actions Extension</summary>


**Objective:** Install the GitHub Actions VS Code extension, verify YAML IntelliSense activates, and confirm schema validation catches errors.

**Prerequisites:** VS Code v1.60+; Git installed; a cloned or initialized Git repository open as a workspace folder.

**Context:** Without the extension, YAML typos in workflow files are invisible until the run fails on GitHub. The extension provides real-time schema validation and IntelliSense for all GitHub Actions keys, reducing push-and-pray debugging cycles.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Open VS Code → Extensions panel (`Ctrl+Shift+X`) → search `GitHub Actions` → verify publisher is **GitHub** → **Install**.
2. Create the workflows directory: `mkdir -p .github/workflows` (or `New-Item -ItemType Directory -Force .github\workflows` on Windows).
3. Create `.github/workflows/hello.yml` with this content:

```yaml
name: Hello World

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  greet:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Checkout code
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Print greeting
        run: echo "Hello, ${{ github.actor }}!"
```

4. Hover over `runs-on` → verify a tooltip describing the key appears.
5. Type `runs-on: invalid-runner-name` → verify a red squiggly warning appears.
6. Restore the valid value and confirm the warning disappears.
7. Inside the `steps:` block start typing `- uses: actions/` → verify IntelliSense suggests action names.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Extension appears in the Extensions panel as "GitHub Actions" by GitHub.
- [ ] Hovering YAML keys shows documentation tooltips.
- [ ] An invalid `runs-on` value produces a visible schema validation warning.
- [ ] IntelliSense completes action names when typing `uses:`.

**Expected Output:**

Hovering over `runs-on` shows: *"The type of machine to run the job on. The machine can be either a GitHub-hosted runner or a self-hosted runner."*

**Troubleshooting:**

- **IntelliSense not appearing** → Ensure the file is inside `.github/workflows/` with a `.yml` or `.yaml` extension. Opening a standalone file (no workspace folder) will not activate the schema.
- **No schema warnings** → Reload window (`Ctrl+Shift+P` → "Developer: Reload Window") after installing the extension.

**Time Estimate:** 10–15 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 4 (YAML Syntax) for YAML anchors and advanced structure; → Section 15 (Debugging) for interpreting workflow error messages.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>✅ Scenario 1-B: Validate a Workflow Locally with `act`</summary>


**Objective:** Install the `act` CLI and run a GitHub Actions workflow on your local machine without pushing to GitHub.

**Prerequisites:** Docker Desktop installed and running; Scenario 1-A complete (workflow file exists).

**Context:** `act` uses Docker to simulate the GitHub Actions runner environment locally. This shortens the feedback loop from "push → wait → fail → push again" to an immediate local test cycle. It is especially useful for catching logic errors and environment misconfigurations.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Install `act`:
   - **Windows (winget):** `winget install nektos.act`
   - **Windows (choco):** `choco install act-cli`
   - **macOS:** `brew install act`
   - **Linux:** `curl https://raw.githubusercontent.com/nektos/act/master/install.sh | sudo bash`
2. Verify installation: `act --version`
3. From the repository root run `act -l` to list detected workflows.
4. Run the push event locally: `act push`
5. Observe the Docker image pull (first run only) and step execution in the terminal.
6. Add `.actrc` in the repo root to avoid the image prompt on future runs:

```text
-P ubuntu-latest=catthehacker/ubuntu:act-latest
```

7. Run `act push --dry-run` to preview execution order without running steps.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `act --version` prints a version string.
- [ ] `act -l` lists the `Hello World` workflow.
- [ ] `act push` executes the `greet` job and prints the greeting.
- [ ] `act push --dry-run` prints the plan without executing Docker containers.

**Expected Output:**

```text
[Hello World/greet] 🐳 docker run image=catthehacker/ubuntu:act-latest
[Hello World/greet]   ✅  Success - Checkout code
[Hello World/greet]   ✅  Success - Print greeting
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **"Cannot connect to Docker daemon"** → Start Docker Desktop; verify `docker ps` works.
- **act pulls wrong image** → Add `.actrc` as shown above to specify the correct image tag.
- **Step output shows wrong actor** → `act` uses `nektos/act` as the actor by default; this is expected in local runs.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Pass a secret to `act`: `act push -s MY_SECRET=value`
- Test multiple events: `act pull_request` to simulate PR triggers.

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for enabling debug logging inside `act`; → Section 5 (Triggers) for simulating different event types locally.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔍 Scenario 1-C: Advanced Workflow Validation — Linting and Schema Enforcement</summary>


**Objective:** Set up automated workflow validation beyond the VS Code extension using actionlint, schema linters, and pre-commit hooks to catch errors before pushing to GitHub.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 1-A and 1-B complete; basic shell/bash knowledge.

**Context:** While the VS Code extension catches obvious errors, enterprise teams need consistent validation across all developers. Tools like `actionlint` provide deeper analysis: unused variables, missing outputs, unreachable steps, and deprecated syntax. Pre-commit hooks enforce validation automatically.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Install `actionlint` (requires Go ≥1.16):
   - **macOS/Linux:** `brew install actionlint`
   - **Windows:** Download from [rhysd/actionlint releases](https://github.com/rhysd/actionlint/releases) or use `scoop install actionlint`
   - Verify: `actionlint --version`

2. Run `actionlint` on your workflow:

   ```bash
   actionlint .github/workflows/hello.yml
   ```

3. Create an intentionally flawed workflow at `.github/workflows/flawed.yml`:

   ```yaml
   name: Flawed Workflow
   on: push
   jobs:
     test:
       runs-on: ubuntu-latest
       steps:
         - uses: actions/checkout@v4
         - name: Use undefined variable
           run: echo "Value is ${{ env.UNDEFINED_VAR }}"
         - name: Unreachable step
           if: false
           run: echo "Never runs"
   ```

4. Run `actionlint .github/workflows/flawed.yml` and observe the warnings.

5. Install `pre-commit` framework:
   - `pip install pre-commit` (or `brew install pre-commit` on macOS)

6. Create `.pre-commit-config.yaml` in repo root:

   ```yaml
   repos:
     - repo: https://github.com/rhysd/actionlint
       rev: v1.6.27
       hooks:
         - id: actionlint
   ```

7. Install the git hook: `pre-commit install`

8. Try committing `.github/workflows/flawed.yml` — the pre-commit hook will block it with validation errors.

9. Fix the flawed workflow and commit again successfully.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `actionlint --version` runs without error.
- [ ] Running actionlint on flawed.yml reports 2+ warnings.
- [ ] Pre-commit hook is installed and active (`git hook list` shows pre-commit).
- [ ] Committing flawed workflow is blocked; committing corrected workflow succeeds.

**Expected Output:**

```bash
.github/workflows/flawed.yml:7:15: "env.UNDEFINED_VAR" is not defined. available env variables are ["GITHUB_*", ...]
.github/workflows/flawed.yml:8:5: unreachable step detected. step cannot run because condition is always false
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **actionlint not found** → Add to PATH or use full path `/usr/local/bin/actionlint`
- **Pre-commit hook not blocking commits** → Verify hook is installed: `cat .git/hooks/pre-commit`
- **Hook runs too slowly** → Use `pre-commit run --all-files --hook-stage commit` to test specific hooks

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Add `yamllint` for YAML syntax validation
- Integrate with GitHub Actions to run actionlint on every workflow change (meta-workflow)
- Configure actionlint in strict mode: `actionlint -config-file .actionlintrc.yaml`

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 4 (YAML Syntax) for schema rules; → Section 15 (Debugging) for actionlint error interpretation.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🐛 Scenario 1-D: Troubleshooting Local Workflow Validation — Diagnosing and Fixing Common Issues</summary>


**Objective:** Diagnose and fix common problems when using the VS Code extension, `act`, and actionlint. Learn systematic troubleshooting methodology.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 1-C complete; exposure to typical validation failures.

**Context:** Real-world development involves misconfigurations: Docker not running, act using wrong image, extension not loading schemas, pre-commit hooks conflicting. Learning to diagnose these systematically saves hours of frustration.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Simulate Extension Loading Failure:**
   - Close VS Code completely
   - Delete VS Code cache: `rm -rf ~/.config/Code/CachedData/*` (Linux/macOS) or `rmdir "%APPDATA%\Code\CachedData" /s /q` (Windows)
   - Reopen VS Code and wait 30 seconds for extension initialization
   - If IntelliSense still doesn't appear, check Output panel: **View → Output → GitHub Actions**
   - Expected: Log shows "Schema loaded successfully"

2. **Simulate and Fix Docker Connection Error with act:**
   - Stop Docker Desktop or stop Docker daemon: `systemctl stop docker` (Linux)
   - Try running `act push` — observe error: "Cannot connect to Docker daemon"
   - Check Docker status: `docker ps` (fails as expected)
   - Restart Docker and verify: `docker ps` (shows running containers)
   - Retry `act push` — succeeds

3. **Fix act Image Mismatch:**
   - Run `act -l` and note the detected workflows
   - Run `act push 2>&1 | head -20` to see image being pulled
   - Delete `.actrc` if it exists: `rm .actrc`
   - Run `act push` again — note it prompts for image selection or uses default
   - Create `.actrc` with explicit image:

     ```bash
     -P ubuntu-latest=ghcr.io/catthehacker/ubuntu:act-latest
     ```

   - Run `act push` again — verify correct image is used

4. **Diagnose actionlint Configuration Issues:**
   - Create malformed `.actionlintrc.yaml`:

     ```yaml
     invalid: yaml: [structure
     ```

   - Run `actionlint .github/workflows/hello.yml` — observe error
   - Fix YAML syntax in `.actionlintrc.yaml` — retry

5. **Resolve Pre-commit Hook Bypass Issues:**
   - Verify hook is active: `ls -la .git/hooks/pre-commit`
   - Run pre-commit manually: `pre-commit run --all-files`
   - If blocked by actionlint errors, note them and create an issue or fix the workflow

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Extension Output panel shows schema initialization logs.
- [ ] Docker connectivity restored and `act` runs successfully.
- [ ] `.actrc` points to correct image; `act -l` confirms.
- [ ] actionlint produces clear error messages for invalid YAML configs.
- [ ] Pre-commit hook can be manually invoked and blocks invalid workflows.

**Expected Output:**

```bash
$ docker ps
Error response from daemon: Cannot connect to Docker daemon

$ systemctl start docker
$ docker ps
CONTAINER ID   IMAGE   COMMAND   STATUS   PORTS
[containers list]

$ act push
[Hello World/greet] 🐳 docker run image=ghcr.io/catthehacker/ubuntu:act-latest
[Hello World/greet]   ✅  Success - Checkout code
[Hello World/greet]   ✅  Success - Print greeting
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Extension logs not appearing** → Ensure Output panel is visible; check dropdown is set to "GitHub Actions"
- **Docker still not found** → Verify Docker installation: `which docker` (Unix) or `where docker` (Windows)
- **Pre-commit hook still not blocking** → Manually run `pre-commit run --all-files` to test

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Enable `act` debug logging: `act push --verbose`
- Test on a separate branch to avoid blocking main development
- Create a "validation dashboard" script that checks all three tools in sequence

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for advanced log inspection; → Section 5 (Triggers) for testing different event types locally.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏢 Scenario 1-E: Enterprise-Scale Setup — Shared IDE Configuration and Team Workflow Templates</summary>


**Objective:** Establish organizational standards for GitHub Actions local development: shared VS Code settings, standardized `.actrc` configuration, and reusable workflow templates enforced across the team.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 1-D complete; team/organization collaboration model.

**Context:** Solo developers can validate workflows individually, but teams need consistency. Shared IDE settings, pre-configured act environments, and enforced workflow standards reduce onboarding time and prevent misconfiguration-related bugs. This scenario models enterprise practices: committing configuration to version control, using DevContainers, and defining team standards.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Create Shared VS Code Workspace Settings:**
   - In repo root, create `.vscode/settings.json`:

     ```json
     {
       "[yaml]": {
         "editor.formatOnSave": true,
         "editor.defaultFormatter": "esbenp.prettier-vscode"
       },
       "yaml.schemas": {
         "https://json.schemastore.org/github-workflow.json": ".github/workflows/*.yml"
       },
       "editor.codeActionsOnSave": {
         "source.fixAll": "explicit"
       }
     }
     ```

2. **Create Shared Extensions Recommendation:**
   - Create `.vscode/extensions.json`:

     ```json
     {
       "recommendations": [
         "github.vscode-github-actions",
         "esbenp.prettier-vscode",
         "redhat.vscode-yaml",
         "ms-vscode.makefile-tools"
       ]
     }
     ```

3. **Commit Team `.actrc` Configuration:**
   - In repo root, create `.github/.actrc.template`:

     ```bash
     -P ubuntu-latest=ghcr.io/catthehacker/ubuntu:act-latest
     -P windows-latest=ghcr.io/catthehacker/windows:latest
     -P macos-latest=ghcr.io/catthehacker/macos:latest
     --artifact-server-path /tmp/artifacts
     ```

   - Add documentation: **SETUP.md** → "Copy `.github/.actrc.template` to repo root as `.actrc`"

4. **Create Enforced Workflow Template:**
   - Add `.github/workflows/TEMPLATE.yml` with required structure:

     ```yaml
     # Copy this template to create new workflows
     # Required sections: name, on, jobs with proper structure
     name: "[Workflow Name]"
     on: [push, pull_request]
     jobs:
       build:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - uses: actions/checkout@v4
           - name: "[Step description]"
             run: echo "Add your step here"
     ```

5. **Create Pre-commit Policy Enforcement:**
   - Extend `.pre-commit-config.yaml` to include filename validation:

     ```yaml
     repos:
       - repo: https://github.com/rhysd/actionlint
         rev: v1.6.27
         hooks:
           - id: actionlint
       - repo: local
         hooks:
           - id: check-workflow-template
             name: Check workflow template compliance
             entry: bash -c 'for f in .github/workflows/*.yml; do grep -q "jobs:" "$f" || exit 1; done'
             language: system
             files: ^\.github/workflows/
     ```

6. **Create Team Onboarding Guide (DEVELOPMENT.md):**

   ```markdown
   # Local Development Setup

   ## Prerequisites
   - VS Code with GitHub Actions extension
   - Docker Desktop
   - actionlint and pre-commit

   ## Setup Steps
   1. Clone repository
   2. Install pre-commit: `pip install pre-commit && pre-commit install`
   3. Copy `.github/.actrc.template` to `.actrc`
   4. Run `act -l` to verify workflows are detected
   5. VS Code will auto-load shared settings from `.vscode/settings.json`

   ## Validating Workflows
   - Pre-commit hook runs on every commit
   - Manual validation: `actionlint .github/workflows/*.yml`
   - Local simulation: `act push`
   ```

7. **Test Team Setup on Fresh Clone:**
   - In a temporary directory: `git clone <repo> test-clone && cd test-clone`
   - Follow the DEVELOPMENT.md steps
   - Verify all tools work correctly and shared settings load

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `.vscode/settings.json` exists and is committed to repo
- [ ] `.vscode/extensions.json` recommends GitHub Actions and yaml extensions
- [ ] `.github/.actrc.template` provides team-standard act configuration
- [ ] `TEMPLATE.yml` enforces consistent workflow structure
- [ ] Pre-commit policy includes actionlint and custom template checks
- [ ] Fresh clone successfully loads shared settings and passes all validations
- [ ] Team members can follow DEVELOPMENT.md and validate workflows locally

**Expected Output:**

When a new team member clones the repo:

```bash
$ git clone <repo>
$ cd <repo>
$ pre-commit install
pre-commit installed at .git/hooks/pre-commit

$ cp .github/.actrc.template .actrc
$ act -l
[workflows detected]

$ act push
[workflow runs successfully with shared configuration]
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Settings not loading** → Verify `.vscode/` directory is committed: `git ls-files .vscode/`
- **Extensions not recommended** → Restart VS Code to trigger recommendation prompt
- **Pre-commit policy too strict** → Adjust regex patterns to balance safety and flexibility
- **Team bypass validation** → Use branch protection rules (Section 23) to enforce pre-commit passes

**Time Estimate:** 30–40 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Add GitHub Actions workflow to validate all workflows on push: "meta-validation"
- Use DevContainers (`.devcontainer/devcontainer.json`) for complete standardized environment
- Integrate with GitHub Advanced Security for policy enforcement

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 17 (Reusable Workflows) for template distribution; → Section 22 (Enterprise Management) for org-wide policies; → Section 23 (Security) for branch protection and enforcement.

</details>

---

### 🔍 Section 2: Understanding GitHub Contexts - Part 1 (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [02-Contextual-Information.md](02-Contextual-Information.md) (first half)
**Overview:**

- What are contexts and why they matter in workflows
- The `github` context: repository info, ref, event data, actor
- The `env` context: environment variables at workflow/job/step level
- The `secrets` context: encrypted secret handling
- Context interpolation and expression syntax

**Practical Work:**

- Create a test workflow using `github.event_name` and `github.ref`
- Access repository owner and branch information
- Practice secret masking and context limitations


<details>
<summary>🔍 Scenario 2-A: Explore the `github` Context in a Workflow</summary>


**Objective:** Write a workflow that prints key `github` context values to understand what information is available at runtime, and observe how these values differ across trigger types.

**Prerequisites:** Section 1 complete; a GitHub repository where you can push commits and open pull requests.

**Context:** The `github` context is the richest context in GitHub Actions — it contains information about the triggering event, the repository, the actor, and more. Knowing which properties are available (and when) is essential for writing conditional logic and building robust workflows.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/explore-contexts.yml`:

```yaml
name: Explore Contexts

on:
  push:
  pull_request:
  workflow_dispatch:

jobs:
  show-github-context:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Print core github context values
        run: |
          echo "=== Repository Info ==="
          echo "Repo           : ${{ github.repository }}"
          echo "Owner          : ${{ github.repository_owner }}"
          echo "Default branch : ${{ github.event.repository.default_branch }}"

          echo "=== Trigger Info ==="
          echo "Event name     : ${{ github.event_name }}"
          echo "Ref            : ${{ github.ref }}"
          echo "Ref name       : ${{ github.ref_name }}"
          echo "Ref type       : ${{ github.ref_type }}"
          echo "SHA            : ${{ github.sha }}"

          echo "=== Actor Info ==="
          echo "Actor          : ${{ github.actor }}"
          echo "Triggering actor: ${{ github.triggering_actor }}"

          echo "=== PR-specific (only on pull_request events) ==="
          echo "Head ref       : ${{ github.head_ref }}"
          echo "Base ref       : ${{ github.base_ref }}"

      - name: Print full github context as JSON (for inspection)
        env:
          # Assign context to env var to safely print JSON
          GITHUB_CTX: ${{ toJSON(github) }}
        run: echo "$GITHUB_CTX"
```

2. Push to `main` and examine the "Trigger Info" output — note `ref` = `refs/heads/main`.
3. Open a pull request and inspect the same job — note `head_ref` and `base_ref` are now populated.
4. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` — note `event_name` = `workflow_dispatch` and `head_ref` is empty.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `github.repository` prints `owner/repo-name` format.
- [ ] `github.event_name` correctly reflects the trigger type for each run.
- [ ] `github.head_ref` is populated on `pull_request` events and empty on `push` events.
- [ ] The full JSON context dump completes without redaction errors.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`${{ github.head_ref }}` is empty on push** → This is correct behavior; `head_ref` only exists on PR events.
- **JSON dump shows redacted values for secrets** → Expected; the `github` context itself does not contain secrets, but `toJSON(secrets)` would be redacted.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔐 Scenario 2-B: Secrets Context — Masking and Limitations</summary>


**Objective:** Add a repository secret, use it in a workflow, and observe how GitHub automatically masks the value in logs to prevent accidental exposure.

**Prerequisites:** Repository admin access to add secrets; Scenario 2-A complete.

**Context:** Secrets are encrypted at rest and automatically masked in runner logs. Understanding the masking behavior — and its limits — is required exam knowledge. The `secrets` context is only available in certain workflow scopes and is not accessible in pull requests from forks by default.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Navigate to **Repository → Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions → New repository secret**.
   - Name: `DEMO_API_KEY`
   - Value: `super-secret-value-abc123`

2. Create `.github/workflows/secrets-demo.yml`:

```yaml
name: Secrets Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  secrets-test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Use secret safely (masked in logs)
        env:
          # Best practice: map secret to env var rather than inline in run:
          API_KEY: ${{ secrets.DEMO_API_KEY }}
        run: |
          echo "API key length: ${#API_KEY}"
          echo "Using key in command (value is masked): $API_KEY"
          # The value 'super-secret-value-abc123' will appear as *** in logs

      - name: Demonstrate accidental exposure is prevented
        env:
          API_KEY: ${{ secrets.DEMO_API_KEY }}
        run: |
          # Even if you try to echo the value, GitHub masks it
          VAL="$API_KEY"
          echo "Attempting to print: $VAL"

      - name: Secrets unavailable without mapping
        run: |
          # ${{ secrets.DEMO_API_KEY }} inline in run: works but is not best practice
          echo "Inline ref: ${{ secrets.DEMO_API_KEY }}"
```

3. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` and view the logs.
4. Observe that `super-secret-value-abc123` never appears — it is replaced with `***`.
5. Verify the length step prints the correct length (22 characters) — length is not masked.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Secret value is masked as `***` in all log lines.
- [ ] `${#API_KEY}` (length) prints correctly — masking does not prevent computation.
- [ ] No plain-text secret appears anywhere in the workflow log or annotation.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`secrets.DEMO_API_KEY` is empty** → Verify the secret name matches exactly (case-sensitive). Re-check under Settings → Secrets.
- **Secret not masked in log** → If the secret value is very short (< 3 characters), GitHub does not mask it to avoid masking common strings. Use realistic secret values in testing.
- **Secret unavailable in fork PR** → By design. Fork PRs do not have access to repository secrets by default. Use environment protection rules to enable this if necessary.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 7 (Environment Variables) for `GITHUB_ENV` and the difference between env vars and secrets; → Section 8 (Environment Protection) for per-environment secrets; → Section 23 (Security) for script injection via untrusted input.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🧩 Scenario 2-C: Advanced Context Interpolation — Nested Objects and Conditional Logic</summary>


**Objective:** Work with complex `github` context nested properties (event payload data), and implement multi-branch conditional logic using context values.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 2-B complete; comfort with YAML syntax.

**Context:** The `github` context often requires nested property access: `github.event.pull_request.title`, `github.event.repository.full_name`, etc. Additionally, real workflows need to make decisions based on these values using expressions with logical operators. Debugging broken expressions requires understanding how GitHub evaluates them.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/advanced-contexts.yml`:

```yaml
name: Advanced Context Usage

on:
  pull_request:
    types: [opened, synchronize, reopened]
  issues:
    types: [opened, edited]
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      debug_mode:
        description: 'Enable debug output'
        required: false
        default: 'false'

jobs:
  analyze-event:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Analyze PR context
        if: github.event_name == 'pull_request'
        run: |
          echo "=== PR Details ==="
          echo "PR Title       : ${{ github.event.pull_request.title }}"
          echo "PR Author      : ${{ github.event.pull_request.user.login }}"
          echo "PR Base Branch : ${{ github.event.pull_request.base.ref }}"
          echo "PR Head Branch : ${{ github.event.pull_request.head.ref }}"
          echo "PR Draft?      : ${{ github.event.pull_request.draft }}"
          echo "PR Labels      : ${{ join(github.event.pull_request.labels.*.name, ', ') }}"

      - name: Analyze Issue context
        if: github.event_name == 'issues'
        run: |
          echo "=== Issue Details ==="
          echo "Issue Number   : ${{ github.event.issue.number }}"
          echo "Issue Title    : ${{ github.event.issue.title }}"
          echo "Issue Author   : ${{ github.event.issue.user.login }}"
          echo "Issue State    : ${{ github.event.issue.state }}"

      - name: Complex conditional - Route based on trigger type and labels
        if: |
          (github.event_name == 'pull_request' && contains(github.event.pull_request.labels.*.name, 'bug')) ||
          (github.event_name == 'issues' && github.event.action == 'opened')
        run: echo "This should run on PR labeled 'bug' OR any new issue"

      - name: Use workflow dispatch input with context
        if: github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch' && github.event.inputs.debug_mode == 'true'
        run: echo "Debug mode enabled! Full context dump:"

      - name: Safe context access with defaults
        run: |
          TITLE="${{ github.event.pull_request.title || 'No title' }}"
          AUTHOR="${{ github.event.issue.user.login || 'Unknown' }}"
          echo "PR Title with default: $TITLE"
          echo "Issue author with default: $AUTHOR"
```

2. Push the workflow to your repository.

3. Trigger via different event types and observe the output:
   - Open a PR with the `bug` label → "Complex conditional" step should run
   - Create an issue → "Analyze Issue context" runs; "Complex conditional" runs (new issue)
   - Go to **Actions → Advanced Context Usage → Run workflow** → set `debug_mode=true` → "Use workflow dispatch input" runs

4. Modify the conditional on the "Complex conditional" step and test:

   ```yaml
   if: contains(github.event.pull_request.labels.*.name, 'enhancement')
   ```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] PR context shows correct branch names and author.
- [ ] Issue context correctly shows issue number and state.
- [ ] Complex conditional expression with `&&` / `||` operators evaluates correctly.
- [ ] The `join()` function correctly formats PR labels as comma-separated list.
- [ ] Workflow dispatch input conditionals work as expected.

**Expected Output (on PR with 'bug' label):**

```bash
=== PR Details ===
PR Title       : Fix authentication bug
PR Author      : teammate
PR Base Branch : main
PR Head Branch : fix/auth-bug
PR Draft?      : false
PR Labels      : bug, urgent
This should run on PR labeled 'bug' OR any new issue
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Nested property access returns empty** → Check event type; not all events populate all fields. Use `github.event_name` to guard access.
- **`contains()` returns false unexpectedly** → Label names may contain whitespace or special characters. Use `join()` and log the output to debug.
- **Complex conditional never evaluates to true** → Test each sub-expression individually using separate steps to identify which part fails.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Build a label-based router: create multiple jobs, each with conditionals for specific labels
- Implement auto-labeling: use GitHub CLI within a step to add labels based on context analysis
- Create a "debug context dump" action that logs the entire `github`, `env`, and `job` contexts as JSON

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 3 (Job & needs context) for multi-job orchestration; → Section 9 (Conditional Logic) for more complex `if:` expressions; → Section 16 (REST API) for comparing context-based decisions with API queries.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🐛 Scenario 2-D: Troubleshooting Context Mismatches — Diagnosing Hidden Context Issues</summary>


**Objective:** Identify and fix scenarios where context values don't match expectations, including permission issues, event payload mismatches, and scope problems.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 2-C complete; exposure to workflow failures.

**Context:** Subtle context problems cause silent failures: a conditional that should fire doesn't, an expected `secrets` value is `null`, or `github.event` is missing fields. Learning to diagnose these systematically is critical for real-world troubleshooting.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Scenario: PR labels context returns empty list**
   - Create a PR and add a label (`bug`).
   - Create `.github/workflows/diagnose-labels.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Diagnose Labels
     on: pull_request
     jobs:
       check-labels:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Print PR labels (should be non-empty)
             run: echo "Labels: ${{ github.event.pull_request.labels }}"

           - name: Check if empty
             run: |
               LABELS="${{ github.event.pull_request.labels }}"
               if [ -z "$LABELS" ]; then
                 echo "ERROR: Labels are empty! This may indicate wrong event type."
               fi
     ```

   - Push and create a PR. Labels should print as JSON array.
   - **Fix if empty:** Verify PR actually has labels applied; verify event type is `pull_request`.

2. **Scenario: Secrets context returns null**
   - Add a repository secret: `TEST_SECRET=value123`.
   - Create `.github/workflows/diagnose-secrets.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Diagnose Secrets
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       check-secret:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Try to access secret
             run: echo "Secret length: ${{ secrets.TEST_SECRET != '' && 'set' || 'empty' }}"

           - name: Verify in env
             env:
               MY_SECRET: ${{ secrets.TEST_SECRET }}
             run: |
               if [ -z "$MY_SECRET" ]; then
                 echo "ERROR: Secret not available in this job!"
                 echo "Checking permissions..."
               fi
     ```

   - Push and manually trigger. If secret is empty, check:
     - [ ] Secret name matches exactly (case-sensitive)
     - [ ] Job doesn't have `permissions` block that restricts access
     - [ ] Workflow run is from a fork (fork PRs can't access secrets by default)

3. **Scenario: `github.event.pull_request` is null on wrong event**
   - Create `.github/workflows/diagnose-event.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Diagnose Event
     on:
       pull_request:
       push:
     jobs:
       check-event:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Print event type and PR availability
             run: |
               echo "Event: ${{ github.event_name }}"
               echo "PR: ${{ github.event.pull_request.number || 'NULL' }}"

               if [ "${{ github.event_name }}" = "push" ]; then
                 echo "On push: PR context is not available"
               fi
     ```

   - Push a commit (event type = `push`) and create a PR (event type = `pull_request`).
   - Observe: PR number is only available on `pull_request` events.
   - **Fix:** Guard context access with `if: github.event_name == 'pull_request'`.

4. **Scenario: Context differs between job and workflow level**
   - Create `.github/workflows/diagnose-scope.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Diagnose Scope
     env:
       WORKFLOW_VAR: from-workflow
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       job1:
         env:
           JOB_VAR: from-job
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Print scope
             env:
               STEP_VAR: from-step
             run: |
               echo "Workflow var: $WORKFLOW_VAR"
               echo "Job var: $JOB_VAR"
               echo "Step var: $STEP_VAR"
               # WORKFLOW_VAR and JOB_VAR visible here; step-level overrides all
     ```

   - Push and observe all three variables print correctly.
   - Modify step to remove `STEP_VAR` — `JOB_VAR` takes precedence.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Label context returns correct label array when PR has labels.
- [ ] Secret context is available; if empty, you can identify the cause (name mismatch, wrong event, etc.).
- [ ] Event-specific context (e.g., `github.event.pull_request`) is only accessed on correct event types.
- [ ] Environment variable scope (workflow > job > step) is understood and predictable.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Still can't access expected context** → Run `act push` or `act pull_request` locally with verbose logging to simulate the exact event.
- **Secret available locally but not in GitHub** → Verify secret is committed in `.github/workflows/` and not in `.gitignore`.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a "context validator" action that checks for common misconfigurations and reports them
- Build a workflow that tests all supported event types and reports which context fields are available

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for log inspection; → Section 8 (Secrets) for secret availability in different contexts.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏢 Scenario 2-E: Enterprise Secret Management — Rotation, Organizational Secrets, and Protected Context Handling</summary>


**Objective:** Implement enterprise-grade secret management: using organizational secrets, automating secret rotation workflows, and ensuring secrets are accessed only by authorized workflows.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 2-D complete; organization admin access.

**Context:** Large organizations must manage dozens of secrets across many repositories. GitHub supports organization-level secrets, environment secrets, and private secrets with restricted access. This scenario covers designing a secure, scalable secret management strategy.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Create Organization-Level Secret (Org Admin):**
   - Navigate to **Organization → Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions**.
   - Create `ORG_API_KEY` with value `org-secret-value-xyz`.
   - Set access to: "Private repositories" or "Selected repositories" (add your test repo).

2. **Create Environment Secret (Repo Admin):**
   - In your repository, go to **Settings → Environments → Create environment** named `production`.
   - Add environment secret: `PROD_DATABASE_URL = db.prod.internal`.
   - Set "Deployment branches" to only allow `main`.

3. **Create a Workflow Using Organization + Environment Secrets:**

```yaml
name: Secret Rotation Demo

on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      environment:
        description: 'Target environment'
        required: true
        default: 'production'
        type: choice
        options:
          - staging
          - production

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: ${{ github.event.inputs.environment }}
    steps:
      - name: Authenticate with org API key
        run: |
          echo "Authenticating with organization secret..."
          # In real scenario, use secret for API calls
          KEY_LENGTH=$(echo -n "${{ secrets.ORG_API_KEY }}" | wc -c)
          echo "API key is $KEY_LENGTH chars (value masked in logs)"

      - name: Access environment-specific secret
        run: |
          echo "Connecting to database..."
          # Real scenario: mysql -h ${{ secrets.PROD_DATABASE_URL }} ...
          echo "Database URL length: $(echo -n '${{ secrets.PROD_DATABASE_URL }}' | wc -c) chars"

      - name: Verify secret is masked
        run: |
          # Attempt to print the secret - GitHub auto-masks it
          echo "Secret attempt: ${{ secrets.ORG_API_KEY }}"
          # Output will show *** instead of actual value
```

4. **Implement Secret Rotation Automation:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/rotate-secrets.yml` (manually triggered):

```yaml
name: Rotate Secrets

on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      secret_name:
        description: 'Secret to rotate'
        required: true
        type: choice
        options:
          - ORG_API_KEY
          - PROD_DATABASE_URL

jobs:
  rotate:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Generate new secret value
        id: generate
        run: |
          NEW_VALUE=$(openssl rand -base64 32)
          echo "old_value_placeholder=***" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "new_value=$NEW_VALUE" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "rotation_timestamp=$(date -u +'%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ')" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Update secret (requires GitHub CLI + proper permissions)
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
        run: |
          # In real scenario, update via GitHub API or third-party secret manager
          echo "Secret rotation logged:"
          echo "  Secret: ${{ github.event.inputs.secret_name }}"
          echo "  Timestamp: ${{ steps.generate.outputs.rotation_timestamp }}"
          echo "  Status: PENDING (awaits manual update in Settings)"

      - name: Send notification
        run: echo "Secret rotation initiated. Update via Settings → Secrets within 5 minutes."
```

5. **Implement Secret Access Audit (via Workflow Logs):**
   - Create `.github/workflows/audit-secrets.yml`:

```yaml
name: Secret Access Audit

on:
  workflow_run:
    workflows: [Secret Rotation Demo, Deploy]
    types: [completed]

jobs:
  audit:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Log access attempt
        run: |
          echo "Workflow: ${{ github.event.workflow_run.name }}"
          echo "Conclusion: ${{ github.event.workflow_run.conclusion }}"
          echo "Secrets used: ORG_API_KEY, PROD_DATABASE_URL"
          echo "Timestamp: $(date -u)"
          # In real scenario, send to centralized audit log
```

6. **Test the Workflow:**
   - Trigger `Secret Rotation Demo` with `production` environment.
   - Verify it runs only on `main` branch (deployment branch restriction).
   - Verify secrets are masked in logs.
   - Run `Rotate Secrets` to simulate rotation (outputs will show placeholders).

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Organization secret is accessible to all authorized repositories.
- [ ] Environment secret is accessible only in the specified environment.
- [ ] Deployment branch restriction prevents `production` environment access from non-`main` branches.
- [ ] All secret values are masked in workflow logs.
- [ ] Rotation workflow provides audit trail (timestamps, secret names).
- [ ] Fresh checkout can access both org and environment secrets without additional auth.

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Authenticating with organization secret...
API key is 24 chars (value masked in logs)

Connecting to database...
Database URL length: 18 chars

Secret attempt: *** (masked by GitHub)

Secret rotation logged:
  Secret: ORG_API_KEY
  Timestamp: 2024-04-19T14:23:45Z
  Status: PENDING (awaits manual update in Settings)
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Organization secret not accessible** → Verify repository is in the "Selected repositories" list for the secret.
- **Environment deployment restriction not blocking** → Ensure you're pushing from a non-`main` branch; restriction only applies when workflow specifies `environment: production`.
- **Manual secret update tedious at scale** → In production, integrate with AWS Secrets Manager, HashiCorp Vault, or GitHub's native secret scanning APIs.

**Time Estimate:** 30–40 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Implement Vault integration using third-party actions for automatic secret retrieval
- Build a secret audit dashboard that tracks which workflows access which secrets
- Create a "secret expiration" workflow that alerts when secrets are old and need rotation
- Integrate GitHub Advanced Security to scan workflows for hardcoded secrets

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 8 (Environment Protection) for deployment approval workflows; → Section 23 (Security) for least-privilege GITHUB_TOKEN and secret scanning; → Section 22 (Enterprise Management) for organization-wide policies.

</details>
