### 🔍 Section 3: Understanding GitHub Contexts - Part 2 (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [02-Contextual-Information.md](02-Contextual-Information.md) (second half) + [03-Context-Availability-Reference.md](03-Context-Availability-Reference.md)
**Overview:**

- The `job`, `runner`, `steps`, and `matrix` contexts
- The `inputs` context for workflow_dispatch and workflow_call
- The `needs` context for inter-job communication
- The `strategy` context for matrix configurations
- Static vs runtime evaluation of expressions

**Practical Work:**

- Use matrix context to access axis values
- Pass data between jobs using needs context
- Implement conditional expressions with context data
- Test context availability at different workflow scopes


<details>
<summary>📡 Scenario 3-A: Pass Data Between Jobs Using the `needs` Context</summary>


**Objective:** Create a two-job workflow where the `deploy` job consumes structured outputs produced by the `build` job via the `needs` context.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–2 complete; a GitHub repository where you can push and trigger Actions.

**Context:** Real CI/CD pipelines frequently need to hand data from one job to the next — a build number, a generated version string, or an artifact path. The `GITHUB_OUTPUT` file and the `needs.<job>.outputs` context are the canonical mechanism. Using the deprecated `set-output` command will fail on current runners.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/job-outputs.yml`:

```yaml
name: Job Outputs Demo

on:
  workflow_dispatch: # trigger manually from Actions tab

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      # Expose step outputs as job outputs
      version: ${{ steps.set-version.outputs.version }}
      artifact-name: ${{ steps.set-name.outputs.name }}
    steps:
      - name: Generate version string
        id: set-version
        # Write key=value pairs to $GITHUB_OUTPUT to expose step outputs
        run: echo "version=1.0.${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Generate artifact name
        id: set-name
        run: echo "name=app-${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: build  # declares dependency; also makes build outputs accessible
    steps:
      - name: Consume build outputs
        run: |
          echo "Deploying version : ${{ needs.build.outputs.version }}"
          echo "Artifact name     : ${{ needs.build.outputs.artifact-name }}"
          echo "Triggered by      : ${{ github.actor }}"
```

2. Push the file and navigate to **Actions → Job Outputs Demo → Run workflow**.
3. In the run detail, click the `build` job → expand the "Generate version string" step → note the `version` output value.
4. Click the `deploy` job and verify the values in the "Consume build outputs" step match exactly.
5. Confirm the dependency arrow: the `deploy` job box appears only after `build` finishes.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `build` job completes and its outputs appear in the Actions run summary.
- [ ] `deploy` job does not start until `build` finishes successfully.
- [ ] `deploy` logs print the correct version and artifact name from `build`.
- [ ] `needs.build.outputs.version` value matches `1.0.<run_number>` format.

**Expected Output (deploy job logs):**

```text
Deploying version : 1.0.42
Artifact name     : app-42
Triggered by      : your-username
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`needs.build.outputs.version` is empty** → Verify the step writing to `$GITHUB_OUTPUT` has an `id:` field. Without `id:`, you cannot reference that step's output at the job level.
- **`deploy` job is skipped** → If `build` fails, `deploy` is skipped by default. Check `build` logs for errors.
- **`>> $GITHUB_OUTPUT` vs `> $GITHUB_OUTPUT`** → Always append (`>>`); a single `>` overwrites the file and deletes previous outputs from the same job.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Add a third `notify` job that needs `deploy` and prints `needs.deploy.outputs.*`.
- Store a JSON string in an output and parse it with `fromJSON()` in the consuming job.

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 9 (Conditional Logic) for using `needs.build.outputs.version` inside an `if:` expression; → Section 14 (Inter-Job Communication) for matrix output aggregation patterns.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔀 Scenario 3-B: Implement Conditional Steps Using the `if:` Expression</summary>


**Objective:** Use `if:` expressions with `github` context values so that individual steps execute only in appropriate trigger scenarios.

**Prerequisites:** Section 2 (github context) completed; basic workflow structure understood.

**Context:** Without `if:` guards, every step runs regardless of trigger type, branch, or actor. Adding conditions prevents accidental deployments on PRs, avoids redundant notifications on scheduled runs, and blocks manual overrides on protected branches.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/conditional-steps.yml`:

```yaml
name: Conditional Steps Demo

on:
  push:
    branches: [main, develop]
  pull_request:
  workflow_dispatch:

jobs:
  demo:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Always runs — print trigger info
        run: |
          echo "Event     : ${{ github.event_name }}"
          echo "Ref       : ${{ github.ref }}"
          echo "Head ref  : ${{ github.head_ref }}"

      - name: Only on push to main
        # Evaluates at runtime; no quotes needed around the expression
        if: github.event_name == 'push' && github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
        run: echo "✅ Production push detected — would trigger deploy"

      - name: Only on pull_request events
        if: github.event_name == 'pull_request'
        run: echo "📋 PR from '${{ github.head_ref }}' into '${{ github.base_ref }}'"

      - name: Only on workflow_dispatch
        if: github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch'
        run: echo "🖱️ Manually triggered by ${{ github.actor }}"

      - name: Skip on forks — avoid leaking secrets
        if: github.repository_owner == github.event.repository.owner.login
        run: echo "Running in the origin repo — safe to use secrets"
```

2. Push to `develop` → verify only the "Always runs" step and none of the branch-specific steps execute.
3. Push to `main` → verify the "Only on push to main" step executes.
4. Open a PR → verify the pull_request step executes.
5. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` → verify the manual step executes.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Correct steps fire on each trigger type; incorrect ones show as **Skipped** (grey) in the UI.
- [ ] No step shows as **Failed** due to a condition syntax error.
- [ ] The "Skip on forks" step logic is understood and could be applied to protect secrets.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **All steps run regardless of condition** → Check for typos in the `if:` value. An expression syntax error causes the condition to evaluate as `true` (permissive default).
- **`github.head_ref` is empty on push** → `head_ref` is only populated on `pull_request` events. Use `github.ref` for branch name on push events.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 9 (Jobs & Steps) for `success()`, `failure()`, and `cancelled()` status functions in `if:` expressions; → Section 5 (Trigger Filters) for combining trigger conditions with `if:` guards.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🧠 Scenario 3-C: Advanced Conditional Logic — Nested Conditions, Status Checks, and Multi-Output Routing</summary>


**Objective:** Master complex conditional expressions using GitHub's built-in functions (`success()`, `failure()`, `cancelled()`, `always()`) and multi-branch routing based on step outputs and job status.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 3-B complete; familiarity with basic `if:` expressions.

**Context:** Real workflows need sophisticated routing: run cleanup on failure, skip on cancellation, or branch logic based on step outputs. Mastering these patterns enables resilient, self-healing workflows.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/advanced-conditionals.yml`:

```yaml
name: Advanced Conditionals

on:
  push:
  pull_request:
  workflow_dispatch:

jobs:
  build-and-test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Build application
        id: build
        run: |
          echo "🔨 Building..."
          # Simulate successful build
          echo "build_output=success" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "build_version=1.0.0" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Run tests
        id: tests
        # Fail the tests to demonstrate failure handling
        run: |
          echo "🧪 Testing..."
          # Comment out the next line to make tests pass
          exit 1  # Simulate test failure

      - name: Report test results (runs only if tests pass)
        if: success()
        run: echo "✅ All tests passed!"

      - name: Collect failure info (runs only if any step failed)
        if: failure()
        run: |
          echo "❌ Build failed. Collecting debug info..."
          echo "Build output: ${{ steps.build.outputs.build_output }}"

      - name: Cleanup (always runs, even on cancellation)
        if: always()
        run: echo "🧹 Cleanup step (always runs)"

      - name: Determine next action based on status
        if: always()
        run: |
          if [ "${{ job.status }}" = "success" ]; then
            echo "Job succeeded — would proceed to deployment"
          elif [ "${{ job.status }}" = "failure" ]; then
            echo "Job failed — would trigger rollback"
          fi

  deploy-on-success:
    # This entire job only runs if build-and-test succeeded
    if: success()
    needs: build-and-test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Deploy to production
        run: echo "🚀 Deploying version ${{ needs.build-and-test.outputs.build_version }}"

  notify-on-failure:
    # This job only runs if build-and-test failed
    if: failure()
    needs: build-and-test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Send failure notification
        run: echo "📧 Sent failure alert to team"
```

2. Push the workflow and trigger manually. Observe:
   - Build step succeeds → outputs `build_version`
   - Tests fail → "Report test results" is **Skipped**
   - Cleanup always runs
   - Deploy job is **Skipped** (because `success()` is false)
   - Notify job runs (because `failure()` is true)

3. Comment out `exit 1` to make tests pass, and re-trigger:
   - Cleanup runs (always)
   - Deploy job now runs
   - Notify job is **Skipped**

4. Add another job that uses `cancelled()`:

```yaml
  handle-cancellation:
    if: cancelled()
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Log cancellation
        run: echo "⚠️ Workflow was cancelled by user"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Step-level `if: success()` correctly skips when previous steps fail.
- [ ] Step-level `if: failure()` correctly activates when previous steps fail.
- [ ] `if: always()` runs regardless of previous step status.
- [ ] Job-level `if: success()` prevents deploy job from running when build fails.
- [ ] Job-level `if: failure()` activates notification job on build failure.
- [ ] Cancelling the workflow activates the `handle-cancellation` job.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`success()` behaves unexpectedly** → Remember: `success()` checks if all previous steps succeeded, not just the prior step. For single-step checks, use explicit conditions.
- **Step output not visible in dependent step** → Ensure output is set via `id:` field and referenced as `${{ steps.STEPID.outputs.KEY }}`.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a conditional matrix: apply different conditions to different matrix combinations
- Implement automatic retry logic: use a custom action that retries on specific failure patterns
- Build a "health check" job that runs after critical steps and can trigger rollback workflows

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 9 (Job Dependencies & needs) for coordinating multi-job workflows; → Section 15 (Debugging) for inspecting job status in logs.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🐛 Scenario 3-D: Troubleshooting Conditional Failures — Why Conditions Don't Fire and How to Debug Them</summary>


**Objective:** Diagnose and fix scenarios where conditions silently fail, misfire, or evaluate unexpectedly.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 3-C complete; exposure to workflow runs.

**Context:** Silent failures in conditionals cause entire sections of workflows to be skipped without error messages. Learning systematic debugging techniques prevents days of frustration.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Scenario: Condition syntax error causes unexpected permissive behavior**
   - Create `.github/workflows/debug-conditional.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Debug Conditional
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Set output
             id: check
             run: echo "status=ready" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

           - name: Intentional syntax error (typo in function name)
             if: succes()  # Typo: missing final 's'
             run: echo "This should run but won't"
     ```

   - Push and trigger. The step is **Skipped** (not failed).
   - **Fix:** Change `succes()` to `success()`. Step now runs.
   - **Lesson:** GitHub doesn't error on typos; it defaults to `if: false`.

2. **Scenario: Using wrong output reference syntax**
   - Create `.github/workflows/debug-outputs.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Debug Outputs
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Set output
             id: check
             run: echo "status=ready" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

           - name: Wrong reference (should fail)
             if: steps.check.output.status == 'ready'  # Wrong: .output instead of .outputs
             run: echo "This won't run because reference syntax is wrong"

           - name: Correct reference
             if: steps.check.outputs.status == 'ready'  # Correct: .outputs (plural)
             run: echo "This will run"
     ```

   - First step with wrong reference is **Skipped**. Second step runs.
   - **Fix:** Always use `.outputs` (plural).

3. **Scenario: Condition references non-existent step**
   - Create `.github/workflows/debug-step-id.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Debug Step ID
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: No ID assigned
             run: echo "no_id_here=value" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

           - name: Reference missing step ID
             if: steps.check.outputs.status == 'ready'  # Step ID 'check' doesn't exist
             run: echo "This step is skipped due to failed condition evaluation"

           - name: Correct reference
             id: check
             run: echo "status=ready" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
     ```

   - Push and observe: Condition evaluates to false; step skipped.
   - **Fix:** Ensure every step you reference in `if:` has an `id:` field.

4. **Scenario: Complex condition is hard to debug; need step-by-step validation**
   - Create `.github/workflows/debug-complex-condition.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Debug Complex
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Check condition components
             run: |
               echo "Event: ${{ github.event_name }}"
               echo "Ref: ${{ github.ref }}"
               echo "Actor: ${{ github.actor }}"
               echo "Repository: ${{ github.repository }}"

           - name: Break complex condition into steps
             run: |
               COND1=${{ github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch' }}
               COND2=${{ github.ref == 'refs/heads/main' }}
               COND3=${{ github.actor == 'pbaletkeman' }}
               echo "Condition 1 (event): $COND1"
               echo "Condition 2 (ref): $COND2"
               echo "Condition 3 (actor): $COND3"
     ```

   - Run this to understand which part of a complex condition is false.

5. **Scenario: Job-level `if:` condition references outputs that don't exist yet**
   - Create `.github/workflows/debug-job-condition.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Debug Job Condition
     on: workflow_dispatch
     jobs:
       build:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         outputs:
           version: ${{ steps.get-version.outputs.version }}
         steps:
           - name: Get version
             id: get-version
             run: echo "version=1.0.0" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

       deploy:
         # This condition evaluates BEFORE build job runs, so it can't access build's outputs
         if: needs.build.outputs.version == '1.0.0'
         needs: build
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Deploy
             run: echo "Deploying version ${{ needs.build.outputs.version }}"
     ```

   - The deploy job won't run if the condition is wrong. Fix: ensure `build` job declares outputs with exact syntax.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Can identify and fix syntax errors in conditions (typos in function names).
- [ ] Understand `.outputs` (plural) vs `.output` (wrong) reference syntax.
- [ ] Know how to reference step outputs using `steps.STEPID.outputs.KEY` format.
- [ ] Can break down complex conditions into sub-expressions to debug them.
- [ ] Understand the difference between step-level and job-level condition evaluation timing.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Still can't see why condition fails** → Add explicit `run:` steps that print each condition component separately, then use those values in `if:`.
- **Job outputs not available to downstream job** → Ensure upstream job has `outputs:` section mapping step output to job output.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a "condition validator" action that tests conditions before the workflow runs
- Implement conditional logging: only log detailed output when debug mode is enabled

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for using `runner.debug` to enable verbose output; → Section 9 (Job Dependencies) for understanding `needs:` and job-level conditions.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏢 Scenario 3-E: Enterprise-Scale Conditional Routing — Multi-Environment Deployments and Self-Healing Workflows</summary>


**Objective:** Design enterprise-grade workflows that intelligently route deployments across multiple environments based on branch, approval status, and health checks, with automatic rollback on failure.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 3-D complete; understanding of job dependencies and outputs.

**Context:** Large organizations need safe, auditable deployment pipelines that prevent errors, enable team approval, and support automatic recovery. This scenario builds a production-grade workflow.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Create a Multi-Environment Deployment Workflow:**

```yaml
name: Enterprise Multi-Environment Deployment

on:
  push:
    branches:
      - main
      - staging
      - develop
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      target_env:
        description: 'Target environment (dev/staging/prod)'
        required: true
        type: choice
        options:
          - dev
          - staging
          - prod

jobs:
  determine-environment:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      target_env: ${{ steps.set-env.outputs.target_env }}
      approval_required: ${{ steps.set-env.outputs.approval_required }}
    steps:
      - name: Determine target environment from branch
        id: set-env
        run: |
          if [ "${{ github.event_name }}" = "workflow_dispatch" ]; then
            TARGET="${{ github.event.inputs.target_env }}"
            APPROVAL="false"
          elif [ "${{ github.ref }}" = "refs/heads/main" ]; then
            TARGET="prod"
            APPROVAL="true"  # Production requires approval
          elif [ "${{ github.ref }}" = "refs/heads/staging" ]; then
            TARGET="staging"
            APPROVAL="false"
          else
            TARGET="dev"
            APPROVAL="false"
          fi
          echo "target_env=$TARGET" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "approval_required=$APPROVAL" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      build_tag: ${{ steps.build.outputs.image_tag }}
    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Build container image
        id: build
        run: |
          IMAGE_TAG="ghcr.io/myorg/app:${{ github.sha }}"
          echo "image_tag=$IMAGE_TAG" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "🐳 Would build: $IMAGE_TAG"

  test:
    needs: build
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Run test suite
        run: |
          echo "🧪 Running tests on ${{ needs.build.outputs.build_tag }}"
          # Simulate test pass/fail randomly
          [ $((RANDOM % 2)) -eq 0 ] && exit 0 || exit 1

  approve-production:
    # Only required for production deployments
    if: |
      needs.determine-environment.outputs.approval_required == 'true' &&
      needs.test.result == 'success'
    needs: [determine-environment, test]
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment:
      name: ${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}-approval
    steps:
      - name: Wait for manual approval
        run: echo "⏳ Waiting for production approval (via GitHub Environment)"

  deploy:
    if: needs.test.result == 'success'
    needs: [determine-environment, build, test, approve-production]
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment:
      name: ${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}
      url: https://${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}.myapp.com
    steps:
      - name: Deploy to ${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}
        run: |
          echo "🚀 Deploying ${{ needs.build.outputs.build_tag }} to ${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}"

      - name: Wait for rollout (simulate)
        run: sleep 10 && echo "✅ Deployment complete"

      - name: Health check
        id: health
        run: |
          echo "🏥 Running health checks..."
          # Simulate health check pass/fail
          [ $((RANDOM % 2)) -eq 0 ] && exit 0 || exit 1

  rollback:
    # Only runs if deploy fails
    if: failure() && needs.deploy.result == 'failure'
    needs: [determine-environment, deploy]
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Initiate rollback
        run: |
          echo "⚠️ Deployment failed! Rolling back ${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}"
          echo "Using previous stable version..."

      - name: Notify team
        run: echo "📧 Sent rollback notification to on-call team"

  notify:
    if: always()
    needs: [determine-environment, deploy]
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Send deployment summary
        run: |
          STATUS="${{ needs.deploy.result }}"
          ENV="${{ needs.determine-environment.outputs.target_env }}"
          echo "📊 Deployment Summary:"
          echo "  Environment: $ENV"
          echo "  Status: $STATUS"
          echo "  Timestamp: $(date -u)"
```

2. **Create Environment Protection Rules (via Settings):**
   - Navigate to **Settings → Environments → prod-approval** (or via UI create it).
   - Enable "Required reviewers": add team members.
   - Set "Deployment branches and tags" to `main` only.
   - This enforces approval before the `approve-production` job completes.

3. **Trigger the Workflow:**
   - Push to `main` → workflow waits for approval before deploying to production.
   - Push to `staging` → workflow deploys to staging without approval.
   - Push to `develop` → workflow deploys to dev.
   - Manually trigger → choose target environment.

4. **Monitor and Handle Failures:**
   - If tests fail, deploy is **Skipped**.
   - If deploy fails health check, rollback job runs.
   - Notify job always summarizes outcome.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Workflow correctly routes to dev/staging/prod based on branch.
- [ ] Production deployments require manual approval (via environment protection rule).
- [ ] Tests must pass before deployment; deploy is skipped on test failure.
- [ ] Rollback job only runs on deployment failure.
- [ ] Health check determines deployment success.
- [ ] Notification job always runs regardless of outcome.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Approve job never completes** → Verify environment protection rule is configured in Settings; GitHub won't enforce approvals without the rule.
- **Deploy job always skipped** → Check `needs.test.result == 'success'` syntax; ensure test job has `id:` if needed.
- **Rollback logic doesn't trigger** → Test job must succeed for deploy to run; if test fails, entire downstream chain is skipped.

**Time Estimate:** 35–45 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Implement canary deployments: deploy to 10% of production first, then full rollout
- Add feature flag toggles: use context to enable/disable features per environment
- Integrate with incident management: auto-page on-call team if rollback is triggered
- Build approval analytics: track approval times and approval rates per environment

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 8 (Environment Protection) for manual approval setup; → Section 15 (Debugging) for understanding job results in complex workflows; → Section 22 (Enterprise Runners) for organizational deployment policies.

</details>

---

### 📝 Section 4: YAML Syntax & Workflow File Structure (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [04-Workflow-File-Structure.md](04-Workflow-File-Structure.md)
**Overview:**

- GitHub Actions workflow file anatomy
- Top-level keys: name, on, env, jobs, defaults, concurrency
- YAML anchors (&), aliases (*), and merge operators (<<)
- Proper indentation and YAML nesting
- Workflow file naming and placement (.github/workflows/)
- Schema validation and common YAML errors

**Practical Work:**

- Create a workflow file from scratch with proper structure
- Implement YAML anchors to reduce duplication
- Fix syntax errors in sample workflows
- Use schema validation to catch mistakes early


<details>
<summary>🏗️ Scenario 4-A: Build a Workflow from Scratch with Correct Structure</summary>


**Objective:** Author a complete, valid workflow file from memory, correctly using every top-level key and understanding the relationship between `on`, `env`, `defaults`, `concurrency`, and `jobs`.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–3 complete; VS Code with GitHub Actions extension installed.

**Context:** The GH-200 exam tests whether you know the exact YAML structure of a workflow file — valid key names, nesting levels, and which keys are optional vs required. Writing one from scratch without autocomplete is the best way to internalize the schema.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Without using IntelliSense, write `.github/workflows/full-structure.yml` from scratch:

```yaml
name: Full Structure Demo

# Top-level trigger configuration
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:
  workflow_dispatch:

# Workflow-level environment variables (available to all jobs)
env:
  NODE_VERSION: '20'
  BUILD_ENV: production

# Default shell and working directory for all run steps
defaults:
  run:
    shell: bash
    working-directory: ./src

# Prevent concurrent runs of the same workflow on the same branch
concurrency:
  group: ${{ github.workflow }}-${{ github.ref }}
  cancel-in-progress: true

jobs:
  build:
    name: Build Application
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest

    # Job-level env overrides workflow-level env
    env:
      BUILD_ENV: development  # overrides workflow-level BUILD_ENV for this job

    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Node.js
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: ${{ env.NODE_VERSION }}

      - name: Install and build
        # working-directory defaults to ./src from the defaults block
        run: |
          echo "Building in $(pwd)"
          echo "Environment: $BUILD_ENV"

  test:
    name: Run Tests
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: build  # runs after build completes

    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Run tests
        # Step-level env overrides all higher scopes
        env:
          BUILD_ENV: test
        run: echo "Test env: $BUILD_ENV"
```

2. Validate with the VS Code extension — confirm no red squiggles.
3. Push and verify the `test` job waits for `build` to finish in the Actions UI.
4. Inspect the Actions run and confirm `concurrency` prevents a second run if you push twice quickly.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] File has correct top-level keys: `name`, `on`, `env`, `defaults`, `concurrency`, `jobs`.
- [ ] `defaults.run` applies to all `run:` steps unless overridden.
- [ ] `env` precedence: step > job > workflow — confirmed by log output.
- [ ] `concurrency` cancels an in-progress run when a new push arrives.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`defaults.run.working-directory` causes "no such directory" error** → The `src/` directory must exist. Remove the `working-directory` setting or create the directory in a prior step.
- **`concurrency` not cancelling** → The `group` expression must be identical for the cancellation to apply. Verify `${{ github.ref }}` resolves consistently between runs.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔧 Scenario 4-B: YAML Anchors and Fixing Common Syntax Errors</summary>


**Objective:** Use YAML anchors and merge keys to eliminate step duplication, then practice identifying and fixing the five most common GitHub Actions YAML errors.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 4-A complete; basic understanding of YAML data types.

**Context:** YAML anchors (`&`) and aliases (`*`) let you define a block once and reference it multiple times. This is useful for repeated `env:` blocks or common steps across jobs. Knowing how to spot indentation errors, wrong key names, and type mismatches is essential for both the exam and real-world debugging.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/yaml-anchors.yml` demonstrating anchor usage:

```yaml
name: YAML Anchors Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

# Define a reusable environment block with an anchor
.common-env: &common-env
  NODE_ENV: production
  LOG_LEVEL: info
  TIMEOUT: '30'

jobs:
  job-a:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    env:
      <<: *common-env  # merge all keys from common-env anchor
      EXTRA_VAR: job-a-only
    steps:
      - run: env | grep -E 'NODE_ENV|LOG_LEVEL|TIMEOUT|EXTRA_VAR'

  job-b:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    env:
      <<: *common-env  # same anchor, different job
      EXTRA_VAR: job-b-only
    steps:
      - run: env | grep -E 'NODE_ENV|LOG_LEVEL|TIMEOUT|EXTRA_VAR'
```

2. Push and verify both jobs show identical values for `NODE_ENV`, `LOG_LEVEL`, and `TIMEOUT` but different `EXTRA_VAR` values.

3. Now practice fixing these intentionally broken YAML snippets. For each, identify the error before reading the fix:

**Error 1 — Wrong indentation:**

```yaml
# BROKEN
jobs:
  build:
  runs-on: ubuntu-latest  # ❌ should be indented under build:
```

Fix: indent `runs-on:` two more spaces under `build:`.

**Error 2 — Missing required key:**

```yaml
# BROKEN
jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Run tests
        # ❌ missing 'run:' or 'uses:' — a step must have one of them
```

Fix: add `run: pytest` or `uses: actions/...`.

**Error 3 — Incorrect boolean type:**

```yaml
# BROKEN
- name: Continue on error
  run: false-command
  continue-on-error: True  # ❌ YAML True ≠ GitHub Actions boolean true
```

Fix: use lowercase `true` (YAML boolean, not string).

**Error 4 — Expression in wrong context:**

```yaml
# BROKEN
on:
  push:
    branches: [${{ github.ref }}]  # ❌ expressions not evaluated in on: block
```

Fix: expressions are only evaluated at runtime inside `jobs:`; use a literal branch name.

**Error 5 — Duplicate key:**

```yaml
# BROKEN
jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    runs-on: windows-latest  # ❌ duplicate key; last value silently wins
```

Fix: remove the duplicate `runs-on:` line.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Anchors workflow runs without errors; both jobs show identical shared env vars.
- [ ] All 5 broken snippets identified and corrected before viewing fixes.
- [ ] VS Code extension flags at least Errors 1 and 2 with visible warnings.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for reading YAML parse errors in workflow run logs; → Section 4 (YAML Structure) self-referential — this is the deepest dive into the topic.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>♻️ Scenario 4-C: Multi-File Workflow Composition and DRY Principles — Reusable Workflow Components</summary>


**Objective:** Organize complex workflows using composition patterns: splitting large workflows into smaller reusable units, using defaults, and eliminating duplication.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 4-B complete; comfort with YAML anchors and aliases.

**Context:** Large workflows become unmaintainable as they grow. Professional teams break workflows into logical components using GitHub's reusable workflow feature combined with YAML composition patterns and defaults blocks.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Create a Shared Defaults Workflow:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/defaults-base.yml`:

     ```yaml
     # This is not a callable reusable workflow, but a documentation of standard defaults
     # Teams use this as a template for consistency

     name: Defaults Template
     on: [push, pull_request]

     env:
       # Organization-wide defaults
       NODE_VERSION: '20'
       CACHE_KEY_PREFIX: ci-cache
       ARTIFACT_RETENTION_DAYS: 5

     defaults:
       run:
         shell: bash
         working-directory: ./src

     jobs:
       build:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Checkout
             uses: actions/checkout@v4

           - name: Setup Node
             uses: actions/setup-node@v4
             with:
               node-version: ${{ env.NODE_VERSION }}
     ```

2. **Create Reusable Workflow for Common Tasks:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/reusable-build.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Reusable Build Workflow

     on:
       workflow_call:
         inputs:
           build-flags:
             description: 'Build command flags'
             required: false
             type: string
             default: '--production'
         outputs:
           artifact-path:
             description: 'Path to build artifact'
             value: ${{ jobs.build.outputs.artifact }}

     jobs:
       build:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         outputs:
           artifact: ./dist/app.zip
         steps:
           - name: Checkout
             uses: actions/checkout@v4

           - name: Build
             run: |
               npm install
               npm run build ${{ inputs.build-flags }}

           - name: Upload artifact
             uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
             with:
               name: build-artifact
               path: dist/
     ```

3. **Create Reusable Workflow for Testing:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/reusable-test.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Reusable Test Workflow

     on:
       workflow_call:
         inputs:
           test-type:
             description: 'Type of tests (unit|integration|all)'
             required: false
             type: string
             default: 'all'

     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Checkout
             uses: actions/checkout@v4

           - name: Setup
             uses: actions/setup-node@v4
             with:
               node-version: '20'
               cache: npm

           - name: Run tests
             run: npm test -- --type=${{ inputs.test-type }}
     ```

4. **Compose Main Workflow Using Reusable Components:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/main-composed.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Main Composed Workflow
     on:
       push:
         branches: [main]
       pull_request:

     jobs:
       # Reuse the test workflow
       run-tests:
         uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-test.yml
         with:
           test-type: unit

       # Only build if tests pass
       build-app:
         needs: run-tests
         uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-build.yml
         with:
           build-flags: '--production --minify'

       # Downstream job
       verify-artifact:
         needs: build-app
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Verify artifact
             run: echo "Artifact at: ${{ needs.build-app.outputs.artifact-path }}"
     ```

5. **Test the Composed Workflow:**
   - Push to `main` → workflow runs composed structure
   - Modify reusable workflow input → main workflow inherits changes
   - Verify job dependencies and output passing work as expected

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Reusable workflows are callable and parameterized.
- [ ] Main workflow composes multiple reusable workflows using `uses:` and `with:`.
- [ ] Outputs from reusable workflows are accessible to downstream jobs.
- [ ] Modifications to reusable workflow are inherited by all callers.
- [ ] Job dependencies are maintained correctly across reusable boundaries.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Reusable workflow not found** → Ensure workflow file is in `.github/workflows/` directory.
- **Output not available** → Ensure reusable workflow declares `outputs:` at job level and job level.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a library of 5+ reusable workflows covering all standard tasks
- Implement workflow versioning: use git tags to pin reusable workflow versions
- Build a workflow discovery system: document all reusable workflows in a catalog

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 17 (Reusable Workflows) for detailed cross-repo workflow sharing; → Section 25 (Performance) for composition patterns that improve workflow performance.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔄 Scenario 4-D: Migrating Legacy Workflow to Modern YAML Syntax and Validating Structure</summary>


**Objective:** Take an outdated or poorly-structured workflow and modernize it using current best practices, then validate it with tooling.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 4-C complete; exposure to YAML syntax rules.

**Context:** Older workflows often lack structure, use deprecated features, or have suboptimal patterns. Learning to refactor them teaches best practices while preserving functionality.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Start with a Legacy Workflow (Anti-Patterns):**
   - Create `.github/workflows/legacy-broken.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Old Workflow
     on: [push]
     jobs:
       job1:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - uses: actions/checkout@v2  # Outdated version
           - run: |
               echo "Step 1"
               npm install
               npm test
               npm run build
               # No separation of concerns

           - run: |
               echo "Uploading..."
               # Hard-coded paths; not maintainable
               ls -la /home/runner/work/repo/repo/dist/

       job2:
         needs: job1  # But no outputs defined
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - run: echo "Deploy"
           # No artifact retrieval
     ```

2. **Identify Anti-Patterns:**
   - ✗ Outdated action versions (`@v2`)
   - ✗ Multiple commands in single `run:` step (no separation)
   - ✗ Hard-coded paths instead of `env:` or `$GITHUB_WORKSPACE`
   - ✗ Job dependencies without output passing
   - ✗ No error handling or conditional steps
   - ✗ Missing artifact upload/download

3. **Refactor to Modern Syntax:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/modern-refactored.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Refactored Workflow

     # Modern best practices
     on:
       push:
         branches: [main]
       pull_request:

     env:
       NODE_VERSION: '20'
       ARTIFACT_DIR: dist

     defaults:
       run:
         shell: bash

     jobs:
       build:
         name: Build & Test
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         outputs:
           build-status: ${{ job.status }}
           artifact-size: ${{ steps.build.outputs.size }}
         steps:
           - name: Checkout repository
             uses: actions/checkout@v4  # Updated version

           - name: Setup Node.js
             uses: actions/setup-node@v4
             with:
               node-version: ${{ env.NODE_VERSION }}
               cache: npm

           - name: Install dependencies
             run: npm ci  # Better than npm install for CI

           - name: Run tests
             run: npm test -- --coverage

           - name: Build application
             id: build
             run: |
               npm run build
               SIZE=$(du -sh ${{ env.ARTIFACT_DIR }} | cut -f1)
               echo "size=$SIZE" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

           - name: Upload artifact
             uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
             with:
               name: build-${{ github.sha }}
               path: ${{ env.ARTIFACT_DIR }}
               retention-days: 5

       deploy:
         name: Deploy to Production
         needs: build
         if: success() && github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         environment:
           name: production
           url: https://myapp.com
         steps:
           - name: Download artifact
             uses: actions/download-artifact@v3
             with:
               name: build-${{ github.sha }}
               path: ${{ env.ARTIFACT_DIR }}

           - name: Deploy
             run: |
               echo "Deploying ${{ env.ARTIFACT_DIR }}"
               ls -la ${{ env.ARTIFACT_DIR }}
     ```

4. **Validate Refactored Workflow:**
   - Use `actionlint` locally to check for issues:

     ```bash
     actionlint modern-refactored.yml
     ```

   - Use VS Code extension to verify no syntax errors
   - Run `act` locally to simulate execution:

     ```bash
     act push -j build
     ```

5. **Compare Both Workflows:**
   - Document improvements made (versions, structure, artifact handling, etc.)
   - Test modern workflow to verify it produces same result as legacy

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] All action versions are updated to v4 or latest stable.
- [ ] Steps are logically separated (one task per step).
- [ ] Artifact upload/download is properly implemented.
- [ ] Job outputs are defined and used by downstream jobs.
- [ ] Conditional logic (`if:`) is used appropriately.
- [ ] Refactored workflow passes `actionlint` validation.
- [ ] Local `act` simulation succeeds without errors.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Build artifact not found** → Ensure artifact upload path matches build output path.
- **Downstream job doesn't receive artifact** → Verify artifact name matches exactly between upload and download.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a "workflow modernization checklist" for teams upgrading workflows
- Automate detection of outdated action versions across repos
- Build a script that converts legacy workflows to modern syntax automatically

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for using `act` to test workflows locally; → Section 12 (Artifacts) for proper artifact handling patterns.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>⚙️ Scenario 4-E: Programmatically Generate Workflow YAML from Schema and Validation Automation</summary>


**Objective:** Build a system to generate workflow files from a schema definition, enabling consistency, validation, and rapid workflow creation.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 4-D complete; comfort with JSON/YAML schema concepts.

**Context:** Organizations managing 100+ workflows benefit from programmatic generation: consistency is enforced at creation time, and updates can be rolled out automatically. This scenario teaches infrastructure-as-code thinking for CI/CD.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Define a Workflow Schema (JSON Schema):**
   - Create `workflow-schema.json`:

     ```json
     {
       "$schema": "http://json-schema.org/draft-07/schema#",
       "title": "GitHub Actions Workflow Schema",
       "type": "object",
       "properties": {
         "name": {"type": "string", "description": "Workflow name"},
         "trigger": {
           "type": "string",
           "enum": ["push", "pull_request", "schedule", "workflow_dispatch"],
           "description": "Primary trigger type"
         },
         "node_version": {"type": "string", "default": "20"},
         "include_tests": {"type": "boolean", "default": true},
         "include_build": {"type": "boolean", "default": true},
         "include_deploy": {"type": "boolean", "default": false},
         "deploy_env": {"type": "string", "enum": ["staging", "production"]},
         "artifact_retention": {"type": "integer", "default": 5}
       },
       "required": ["name", "trigger"]
     }
     ```

2. **Create a Workflow Configuration File:**
   - Create `workflow-config.json`:

     ```json
     {
       "name": "Build, Test, Deploy",
       "trigger": "push",
       "node_version": "20",
       "include_tests": true,
       "include_build": true,
       "include_deploy": true,
       "deploy_env": "staging",
       "artifact_retention": 7
     }
     ```

3. **Create a Generator Script (Node.js):**
   - Create `generate-workflow.js`:

     ```javascript
     #!/usr/bin/env node

     const fs = require('fs');
     const path = require('path');
     const Ajv = require('ajv');

     // Load schema
     const schema = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('workflow-schema.json', 'utf8'));
     const config = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('workflow-config.json', 'utf8'));

     // Validate config against schema
     const ajv = new Ajv();
     const validate = ajv.compile(schema);
     const valid = validate(config);

     if (!valid) {
       console.error('Config validation failed:', validate.errors);
       process.exit(1);
     }

     // Generate workflow YAML
     const workflow = {
       name: config.name,
       on: {
         [config.trigger]: config.trigger === 'schedule' ?
           [{ cron: '0 0 * * *' }] :
           config.trigger === 'workflow_dispatch' ?
           {} :
           { branches: ['main'] }
       },
       env: {
         NODE_VERSION: config.node_version,
         ARTIFACT_RETENTION_DAYS: config.artifact_retention
       },
       jobs: {}
     };

     // Build job
     if (config.include_build) {
       workflow.jobs.build = {
         'runs-on': 'ubuntu-latest',
         steps: [
           { uses: 'actions/checkout@v4' },
           {
             uses: 'actions/setup-node@v4',
             with: {
               'node-version': '${{ env.NODE_VERSION }}',
               cache: 'npm'
             }
           },
           { run: 'npm ci' },
           {
             run: 'npm run build',
             if: config.include_tests ? 'success()' : 'always()'
           },
           {
             uses: 'actions/upload-artifact@v3',
             with: {
               name: 'build-${{ github.sha }}',
               path: 'dist/',
               'retention-days': config.artifact_retention
             }
           }
         ]
       };
     }

     // Test job
     if (config.include_tests) {
       workflow.jobs.test = {
         'runs-on': 'ubuntu-latest',
         steps: [
           { uses: 'actions/checkout@v4' },
           {
             uses: 'actions/setup-node@v4',
             with: {
               'node-version': '${{ env.NODE_VERSION }}',
               cache: 'npm'
             }
           },
           { run: 'npm ci' },
           { run: 'npm test' }
         ]
       };
     }

     // Deploy job
     if (config.include_deploy) {
       const build_needs = config.include_build ? 'build' : undefined;
       workflow.jobs.deploy = {
         'runs-on': 'ubuntu-latest',
         needs: build_needs,
         environment: {
           name: config.deploy_env,
           url: `https://${config.deploy_env}.myapp.com`
         },
         if: 'success()',
         steps: [
           ...(config.include_build ? [{
             uses: 'actions/download-artifact@v3',
             with: {
               name: 'build-${{ github.sha }}',
               path: 'dist/'
             }
           }] : []),
           {
             run: `echo "Deploying to ${config.deploy_env}"`
           }
         ]
       };
     }

     // Convert to YAML and write
     const yaml = require('js-yaml');
     const output = yaml.dump(workflow, { lineWidth: -1 });

     fs.writeFileSync(
       path.join('.github/workflows/generated-workflow.yml'),
       output
     );

     console.log('✅ Workflow generated successfully!');
     console.log(`📋 Output: .github/workflows/generated-workflow.yml`);
     ```

4. **Create Validation Script:**
   - Create `validate-workflow.js`:

     ```javascript
     #!/usr/bin/env node

     const fs = require('fs');
     const { spawnSync } = require('child_process');

     // Validate with actionlint
     const result = spawnSync('actionlint', [
       '.github/workflows/generated-workflow.yml'
     ], { encoding: 'utf8' });

     if (result.error || result.status !== 0) {
       console.error('Validation failed:');
       console.error(result.stderr || result.stdout);
       process.exit(1);
     }

     console.log('✅ Workflow validation passed!');
     ```

5. **Generate and Validate:**
   - Run:

     ```bash
     node generate-workflow.js
     node validate-workflow.js
     ```

   - Review generated `.github/workflows/generated-workflow.yml`
   - Modify `workflow-config.json` and regenerate to see changes

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Config file validates against schema.
- [ ] Generated workflow is valid YAML.
- [ ] `actionlint` validates generated workflow without errors.
- [ ] Changing config generates different workflow correctly.
- [ ] Generated workflow structure matches expected organization standards.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Schema validation fails** → Check config JSON against schema requirements.
- **Generated workflow has syntax errors** → Verify generator logic handles all config combinations.

**Time Estimate:** 30–40 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Extend schema to support matrix jobs, multiple triggers, and custom steps
- Integrate generator into CI/CD pipeline to auto-generate workflows on config change
- Create a web UI for non-technical users to configure and generate workflows
- Build a workflow template library with pre-configured generators

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 17 (Reusable Workflows) for template-based workflow creation; → Section 25 (Performance) for parameterized workflow optimization.

</details>

## ⚡ Week 2: Workflow Triggers & Events

### ⚡ Section 5: Workflow Trigger Events - Part 1 (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [05-Workflow-Trigger-Events.md](05-Workflow-Trigger-Events.md) (first half)
**Overview:**

- Repository events: `push`, `pull_request`, `pull_request_review`
- Scheduled events: `schedule` with cron syntax
- Manual trigger: `workflow_dispatch` and inputs validation
- Repository lifecycle events: create, delete, fork, public
- Status events: workflow_run, deployment, deployment_status

**Practical Work:**

- Configure workflows to trigger on push to specific branches
- Set up scheduled workflows with cron expressions
- Validate cron syntax for different time zones
- Create workflow_dispatch with typed inputs


<details>
<summary>⚡ Scenario 5-A: Configure Push Triggers with Branch and Path Filtering</summary>


**Objective:** Create a workflow that triggers only when relevant files are changed on relevant branches, preventing unnecessary CI runs on documentation-only commits.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–4 complete; repository has at least a `main` branch and some source files.

**Context:** In a monorepo or active open-source project, triggering every workflow on every push wastes CI minutes and creates noise. `paths` filters ensure the frontend pipeline only runs when frontend code changes, and `branches` filters prevent feature branches from triggering production deploy workflows.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create two directories to simulate a project structure:

   ```text
   src/app.js
   docs/README.md
   package.json
   ```

2. Create `.github/workflows/filtered-ci.yml`:

```yaml
name: Filtered CI

on:
  push:
    branches:
      - main
      - 'release/**'     # matches release/v1.0, release/v2.0, etc.
    paths:
      - 'src/**'         # any change under src/
      - 'package.json'   # root package manifest
      - '!src/**/*.md'   # exclude markdown inside src/ (negation)
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]
    paths:
      - 'src/**'

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Show what triggered this run
        run: |
          echo "Event  : ${{ github.event_name }}"
          echo "Branch : ${{ github.ref_name }}"
          echo "Actor  : ${{ github.actor }}"
```

3. Push a change to `src/app.js` on `main` → verify workflow triggers.
4. Push a change to `docs/README.md` on `main` → verify workflow is **not** triggered.
5. Push to a branch named `feature/login` → verify workflow is **not** triggered.
6. Create a branch `release/v1.0` and push a `src/` change → verify workflow triggers.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `src/` changes on `main` trigger the workflow.
- [ ] `docs/` or `README.md` changes on `main` do **not** trigger the workflow.
- [ ] Pushes to `feature/*` branches do **not** trigger the workflow.
- [ ] `release/v1.0` branch pushes with `src/` changes **do** trigger the workflow.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Workflow ignores path filter (runs on every push)** → Check YAML indentation; `paths:` must be indented under the event key (`push:`), not at the top `on:` level.
- **`release/**` pattern not matching** → The `**` glob in branch patterns matches any characters including `/`. Use it consistently; `release/*` only matches one level deep.
- **Negation `!src/**/*.md` not working** → Negation patterns only exclude files when at least one non-negated path pattern already matches.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Add a `paths-ignore:` list instead of negation patterns for clarity.
- Combine `tags` trigger for release tagging: `on: { push: { tags: ['v*'] } }`.

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 6 (Trigger Events Part 2) for `paths-ignore` vs negation and tag triggers; → Section 9 (Conditional Logic) for adding `if:` to individual jobs as a secondary filter.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🎮 Scenario 5-B: Create a `workflow_dispatch` with Typed and Validated Inputs</summary>


**Objective:** Build a manually-triggered workflow with `choice`, `boolean`, and `string` typed inputs, including server-side validation logic.

**Prerequisites:** Section 5-A complete; familiarity with `run:` steps and `if:` conditions.

**Context:** `workflow_dispatch` inputs replace fragile "magic branch names" or commit message conventions as a way to pass parameters to manual runs. Typed inputs render as a form in the GitHub UI, reducing human error and eliminating the need for documentation about what values are acceptable.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/manual-deploy.yml`:

```yaml
name: Manual Deploy

on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      environment:
        description: 'Target environment'
        required: true
        type: choice
        options:
          - development
          - staging
          - production
        default: development

      version:
        description: 'Version tag to deploy (e.g. 1.0.0)'
        required: true
        type: string

      dry-run:
        description: 'Preview changes without deploying'
        required: false
        type: boolean
        default: true

      send-notification:
        description: 'Notify Slack after deploy'
        required: false
        type: boolean
        default: false

jobs:
  validate:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Validate production requires explicit version
        # Prevent accidental production deploys with empty/default versions
        if: inputs.environment == 'production' && inputs.version == ''
        run: |
          echo "ERROR: A specific version is required for production deployments."
          exit 1

      - name: Print resolved inputs
        run: |
          echo "Environment       : ${{ inputs.environment }}"
          echo "Version           : ${{ inputs.version }}"
          echo "Dry run           : ${{ inputs.dry-run }}"
          echo "Send notification : ${{ inputs.send-notification }}"

  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: validate
    steps:
      - name: Simulate deployment
        run: |
          if [ "${{ inputs.dry-run }}" == "true" ]; then
            echo "DRY RUN: would deploy v${{ inputs.version }} → ${{ inputs.environment }}"
          else
            echo "DEPLOYING v${{ inputs.version }} → ${{ inputs.environment }}"
          fi

      - name: Notify (conditional)
        if: inputs.send-notification == true && inputs.dry-run == false
        run: echo "📢 Notification sent for ${{ inputs.environment }} deploy"
```

2. Push the file. Navigate to **Actions → Manual Deploy → Run workflow**.
3. Verify the form shows a **dropdown** for environment, **text fields** for version, and **checkboxes** for the boolean inputs.
4. Run with `dry-run: true` → confirm the simulation message appears.
5. Run with `environment: production` and an empty version → confirm the validate job fails with the error message.
6. Run with `environment: staging`, `version: 1.0.0`, `dry-run: false` → confirm deploy output appears.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Input form renders with a dropdown, text box, and checkboxes.
- [ ] Production + empty version produces a non-zero exit and fails the `validate` job.
- [ ] `deploy` job skips when `validate` fails (due to `needs: validate`).
- [ ] Dry-run and non-dry-run produce different output messages.
- [ ] Notification step skips when `dry-run: true`.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`inputs.environment` evaluates as empty inside a job** → Use `${{ inputs.environment }}` with the expression syntax; bare `inputs.environment` is not valid in `run:` scripts.
- **Boolean checkbox sends string `"true"/"false"`** → In shell scripts compare with `== "true"`, not `== true`. In `if:` expressions, compare with `inputs.dry-run == true` (without quotes).

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Add an `environment:` key to the `deploy` job to link it to a GitHub Environment for approval gates (see Section 8).
- Pass `inputs.version` to a reusable workflow via `workflow_call` (see Section 17).

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 6 (Trigger Events Part 2) for passing `workflow_dispatch` inputs to called workflows; → Section 8 (Environment Protection Rules) for adding required-reviewer gates on the `production` environment.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔀 Scenario 5-C: Complex Trigger Combinations — Paths, Branches, Tags, and Ignore Filters</summary>


**Objective:** Combine multiple trigger filters (branches, paths, tags, ignore patterns) to create sophisticated routing workflows that run only under specific conditions.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 5-B complete; understanding of YAML filter syntax.

**Context:** Real projects need nuanced triggering: run tests on all changes, but only deploy on tagged releases to main. Mastering filter combinations enables efficient, targeted automation.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/complex-triggers.yml`:

```yaml
name: Complex Trigger Combinations

on:
  push:
    # Run on main or version branches, but only if src/ or .github/ changed
    branches:
      - main
      - develop
      - 'release/v*'
    paths:
      - 'src/**'
      - '.github/workflows/**'
      - 'package.json'
    # But never run if only docs changed
    paths-ignore:
      - '*.md'
      - 'docs/**'

  pull_request:
    branches: [main, develop]
    paths:
      - 'src/**'
      - 'tests/**'
    paths-ignore:
      - 'docs/**'

  # Trigger on semantic version tags
  push:
    tags:
      - 'v[0-9]+.[0-9]+.[0-9]+'
      - 'v[0-9]+.[0-9]+.[0-9]+-rc*'

jobs:
  # Runs on all push/PR to src or .github
  lint:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - run: npm run lint

  # Runs only on version tags
  release:
    if: startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Create GitHub release
        run: echo "Release: ${{ github.ref }}"

  # Runs only on main + tag or version branch push
  deploy:
    if: |
      github.event_name == 'push' && (
        github.ref == 'refs/heads/main' ||
        startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/heads/release/') ||
        startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')
      )
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - run: echo "Deploying ${{ github.ref }}"
```

2. Test each trigger:
   - Push to `develop` with only docs changed → no run
   - Push to `develop` with src/ change → lint runs
   - Push to `release/v1.0` with src/ change → lint + deploy run
   - Create tag `v1.0.0` → all jobs run

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Push to non-target branch with no path changes = workflow skipped
- [ ] Push to target branch with relevant path = workflow runs
- [ ] Path-ignore correctly prevents runs
- [ ] Tag-based trigger fires only on matching tags
- [ ] Complex job conditionals combine branch + tag logic correctly

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a matrix of branches and tags, with different behavior for each
- Implement monorepo patterns: trigger different workflows based on which subdirectory changed

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 6 (Event Filters) for deeper dive into path matching; → Section 28 (Practice Assessment) for real-world multi-trigger scenarios.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🐛 Scenario 5-D: Troubleshooting Trigger Events — Why Workflows Don't Fire</summary>


**Objective:** Diagnose and fix workflows that don't trigger when expected using event inspection and testing.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 5-C complete; access to GitHub workflow run history.

**Context:** Silent trigger failures frustrate teams. A workflow that never runs is harder to debug than one that fails. Learning systematic diagnosis prevents hours of wasted time.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Scenario: Push filter expects multiple branches**
   - Create `.github/workflows/trigger-debug.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Trigger Debug
     on:
       push:
         branches:
           - main
           - staging
         paths:
           - 'src/**'
     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - run: echo "Workflow triggered"
     ```

   - Push to `develop` branch with src/ change → workflow does NOT run (expected: main/staging only)
   - Push to `main` with only README.md change → workflow does NOT run (expected: paths filter)
   - Push to `main` with src/ change → workflow DOES run ✓

2. **Scenario: Event type mismatch**
   - Create `.github/workflows/pull-request-only.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: PR Only
     on:
       pull_request:
         branches: [main]
         types: [opened, synchronize]
     jobs:
       pr-test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - run: echo "PR event only"
     ```

   - Comment on an existing PR → no run (event is `issue_comment`, not `pull_request`)
   - Push to main → no run (event is `push`, not `pull_request`)
   - Open new PR → runs ✓ (event type is `opened`)

3. **Scenario: Draft PR is skipped**
   - Create `.github/workflows/draft-debug.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Draft Check
     on:
       pull_request:
     jobs:
       check:
         if: ${{ !github.event.pull_request.draft }}
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - run: echo "Not a draft PR"
     ```

   - Open as draft → job skipped (if condition prevents it)
   - Convert to ready → runs ✓

4. **Scenario: Tag filter pattern doesn't match**
   - Create `.github/workflows/tag-debug.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Tag Debug
     on:
       push:
         tags:
           - 'v[0-9]+.[0-9]+.[0-9]+'  # Only matches semantic versions
     jobs:
       tag-job:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - run: echo "Tag: ${{ github.ref }}"
     ```

   - Create tag `release-1.0` → no run (pattern doesn't match)
   - Create tag `v1.0.0` → runs ✓

5. **Investigate Using GitHub UI:**
   - Go to **Actions → [Workflow] → [Run]**
   - Check "Trigger details" (button at top) for reason workflow ran or skipped
   - Log shows: "Triggered via push", "Skipped due to path filter", etc.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Can explain why each workflow did or didn't trigger
- [ ] Understand event types (push ≠ pull_request ≠ pull_request_target)
- [ ] Recognize path/branch/tag filter mismatches
- [ ] Use GitHub UI to inspect trigger reason
- [ ] Know when `draft: true` skips workflow due to conditions

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Trigger debug info not visible** → Go to **Actions → [Workflow] → Choose recent run → View trigger details**
- **Pattern matches locally but not GitHub** → Test regex with [regex101.com](https://regex101.com/)

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Create a diagnostic workflow that logs all triggering events and contexts
- Build a tool that predicts whether a workflow will trigger based on code changes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for reading GitHub Actions logs; → Section 3 (Conditionals) for job-level trigger guards.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏢 Scenario 5-E: Enterprise Multi-Trigger Orchestration — Cross-Repository Event Coordination</summary>


**Objective:** Build sophisticated, organization-scale workflows that coordinate across multiple repositories using webhook events and API-driven triggers.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 5-D complete; understanding of GitHub App webhooks.

**Context:** Large organizations have interdependent workflows: when Repo A builds, test suites in Repos B, C, and D should also run. This scenario teaches enterprise-scale automation patterns.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. **Create a Webhook-Triggered Workflow (Repo A):**
   - Create `.github/workflows/trigger-dependent-repos.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Trigger Dependent Tests
     on:
       push:
         branches: [main]
         paths:
           - 'src/**'
           - 'package.json'

     jobs:
       notify-downstream:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Trigger tests in Repo B
             run: |
               curl -X POST \
                 -H "Authorization: token ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}" \
                 -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
                 https://api.github.com/repos/YOUR_ORG/repo-b/dispatches \
                 -d '{"event_type":"upstream-build","client_payload":{"branch":"main","sha":"${{ github.sha }}"}}'

           - name: Trigger tests in Repo C
             run: |
               curl -X POST \
                 -H "Authorization: token ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}" \
                 -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
                 https://api.github.com/repos/YOUR_ORG/repo-c/dispatches \
                 -d '{"event_type":"upstream-build"}'
     ```

2. **Create Listener Workflows (Repos B & C):**
   - In Repo B, create `.github/workflows/run-on-upstream.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Run Tests on Upstream Build
     on:
       repository_dispatch:
         types: [upstream-build]

     jobs:
       test:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Checkout
             uses: actions/checkout@v4

           - name: Run tests (against main from Repo A)
             run: |
               echo "Testing compatibility with Repo A commit: ${{ github.event.client_payload.sha }}"
               npm test
     ```

3. **Implement Status Tracking:**
   - Create `.github/workflows/track-status.yml`:

     ```yaml
     name: Track Build Status
     on:
       workflow_run:
         workflows: ['Run Tests on Upstream Build']
         types: [completed]

     jobs:
       report:
         runs-on: ubuntu-latest
         steps:
           - name: Report status
             run: |
               if [ "${{ github.event.workflow_run.conclusion }}" = "success" ]; then
                 echo "✅ Downstream tests passed"
               else
                 echo "❌ Downstream tests failed"
               fi
     ```

4. **Test the Coordination:**
   - Push to Repo A main → triggers curl POST to Repos B & C
   - Repos B & C receive `repository_dispatch` event → run tests
   - `workflow_run` workflow in each captures completion

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Push to Repo A triggers repository_dispatch events in Repos B & C
- [ ] Client_payload passes context between workflows
- [ ] Downstream workflows can access upstream commit SHA and branch
- [ ] Status tracking captures success/failure of downstream runs

**Troubleshooting:**

- **repository_dispatch not triggering** → Verify GITHUB_TOKEN has appropriate scopes and cross-repo permissions
- **Client payload not visible** → Use `${{ github.event.client_payload.KEY }}` syntax to access

**Time Estimate:** 30–40 minutes

**Variations/Extensions:**

- Implement a retry mechanism: if Repo B tests fail, automatically retry
- Create a dashboard that shows status of all dependent runs
- Integrate with Slack to notify on downstream test failures

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 16 (REST API) for advanced event coordination; → Section 22 (Enterprise Management) for organization-scale workflow policies.

</details>
