### 📦 Section 12: Workflow Artifacts - Storage & Retrieval (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [09-Workflow-Artifacts.md](09-Workflow-Artifacts.md)
**Overview:**

- Artifact concepts: upload, storage, retention
- Upload-artifact action: path patterns, name, retention-days
- Download-artifact action: name, path patterns
- Artifact download from UI and REST API
- Cross-job artifact sharing
- Retention policies and cost implications
- Artifact download links and expiration

**Practical Work:**

- Upload test results and coverage reports as artifacts
- Download artifacts in subsequent jobs
- Implement retention policies to manage storage
- Access artifacts via GitHub API
- Create artifact download workflows


<details>
<summary>📦 Scenario 12-A: Upload and Download Artifacts Across Jobs</summary>


**Objective:** Upload test results and a build binary as artifacts in one job, then consume them in separate downstream jobs demonstrating cross-job artifact sharing.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–11 complete.

**Context:** Artifacts persist beyond a single job and can be downloaded by subsequent jobs in the same workflow run, by humans via the UI, or programmatically via the REST API. The `actions/upload-artifact` and `actions/download-artifact` v4 actions use immutable artifact names within a run.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/artifacts-demo.yml`:

```yaml
name: Artifacts Demo

on: [push, workflow_dispatch]

jobs:
  build-and-test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Build application (simulated)
        run: |
          mkdir -p dist
          echo '{"version":"1.0.0","built":"'$(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)'"}' > dist/app.json
          echo "Build complete"

      - name: Run tests and generate report
        run: |
          mkdir -p test-results
          cat <<EOF > test-results/junit.xml
          <?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
          <testsuite name="unit" tests="5" failures="0">
            <testcase name="test_login" classname="auth.tests" time="0.12"/>
            <testcase name="test_logout" classname="auth.tests" time="0.08"/>
            <testcase name="test_register" classname="auth.tests" time="0.15"/>
            <testcase name="test_password_reset" classname="auth.tests" time="0.09"/>
            <testcase name="test_session" classname="auth.tests" time="0.11"/>
          </testsuite>
          EOF
          echo "Test report generated"

      - name: Generate coverage report
        run: |
          mkdir -p coverage
          echo "Statements: 87%\nBranches: 72%\nFunctions: 91%\nLines: 87%" > coverage/summary.txt

      - name: Upload build artifact
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: dist-${{ github.sha }}
          path: dist/
          # Keep for 30 days (default is 90 days)
          retention-days: 30

      - name: Upload test results
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: test-results-${{ github.run_number }}
          path: test-results/
          retention-days: 7

      - name: Upload coverage report
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: coverage-${{ github.run_number }}
          path: coverage/
          retention-days: 7

  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: build-and-test
    steps:
      - name: Download build artifact
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: dist-${{ github.sha }}
          path: ./dist

      - name: Verify artifact content
        run: |
          echo "Contents of dist:"
          ls -la dist/
          cat dist/app.json

  analyze-coverage:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: build-and-test
    steps:
      - name: Download coverage report
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: coverage-${{ github.run_number }}
          path: ./coverage-report

      - name: Display coverage summary
        run: cat coverage-report/summary.txt
```

2. Push and observe three parallel downstream jobs after `build-and-test`.
3. Navigate to the run → **Artifacts** section to see three uploaded artifacts.
4. Download one artifact via the UI and inspect the content.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Three distinct artifacts are uploaded with different names.
- [ ] `deploy` and `analyze-coverage` jobs each download their respective artifact.
- [ ] `retention-days` values are visible in the artifact list in the UI.
- [ ] `dist/app.json` contains the correct build timestamp.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`download-artifact` fails with "No artifact found"** → Verify the artifact name in `download-artifact` exactly matches the name in `upload-artifact`. Names are case-sensitive and include `${{ github.sha }}` interpolation.
- **Artifact is empty** → Check the `path:` in `upload-artifact`. It must point to an existing directory or file. If the path doesn't exist, the action fails silently in some versions.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🌐 Scenario 12-B: Download All Artifacts and REST API Access</summary>


**Objective:** Download all artifacts from a run in one step, implement retention policy management, and demonstrate REST API artifact access.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 12-A complete; a GitHub Personal Access Token (PAT) with `repo` scope or `GITHUB_TOKEN` with `actions: read`.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Extend the previous workflow to add an aggregation job:

```yaml
  aggregate-all:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: build-and-test
    steps:
      - name: Download ALL artifacts from this run
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
        with:
          # Omitting 'name' downloads all artifacts into separate subdirectories
          path: ./all-artifacts

      - name: List all downloaded artifacts
        run: |
          echo "All artifacts:"
          find ./all-artifacts -type f | sort

      - name: Combine reports
        run: |
          echo "=== PIPELINE SUMMARY ===" > pipeline-summary.txt
          echo "Run: ${{ github.run_number }}" >> pipeline-summary.txt
          echo "SHA: ${{ github.sha }}" >> pipeline-summary.txt
          echo "" >> pipeline-summary.txt
          if [ -f all-artifacts/coverage-${{ github.run_number }}/summary.txt ]; then
            echo "=== COVERAGE ===" >> pipeline-summary.txt
            cat all-artifacts/coverage-${{ github.run_number }}/summary.txt >> pipeline-summary.txt
          fi
          cat pipeline-summary.txt

      - name: Upload pipeline summary
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: pipeline-summary-${{ github.run_number }}
          path: pipeline-summary.txt
```

2. Add a separate step showing REST API artifact access:

```yaml
      - name: List artifacts via REST API
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          # Use the GitHub CLI (preinstalled on ubuntu-latest) to query artifacts
          gh api \
            /repos/${{ github.repository }}/actions/runs/${{ github.run_id }}/artifacts \
            --jq '.artifacts[] | [.name, .size_in_bytes, .expires_at] | @tsv'
```

3. Trigger the workflow and verify the aggregation job lists all artifact files.
4. Verify the REST API response shows all artifacts with sizes and expiration dates.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `download-artifact` without `name:` downloads all artifacts into subdirectories.
- [ ] `find ./all-artifacts` shows files from all three artifact directories.
- [ ] REST API response lists artifacts with correct sizes.
- [ ] `pipeline-summary` artifact is created and uploadable.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`gh api` returns 401** → The `GITHUB_TOKEN` must have `actions: read` permission. Add `permissions: actions: read` to the job.
- **Artifacts subdirectory names unexpected** → When downloading all artifacts, each artifact gets its own subdirectory named after the artifact. The `path:` becomes the parent.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 16 (Workflow REST API) for full artifact management via API; → Section 27 (Job Summaries) for using `GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY` as an alternative to artifact-based reporting.

</details>

### 💨 Section 13: Workflow Caching - Performance & Security (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [10-Workflow-Caching.md](10-Workflow-Caching.md)
**Overview:**

- Caching concepts: key, path, restore key
- Cache action: setup-cache vs generic cache
- Cache strategy: pip, npm, gradle, maven
- Cache key generation and versioning
- Scope: repository vs branch level
- Cache invalidation and cleanup
- Security considerations for cached data

**Practical Work:**

- Implement npm dependency caching
- Set up Python pip caching
- Create effective cache key strategies
- Test cache hits and misses
- Implement cache cleanup for sensitive data
- Compare caching performance benefits


<details>
<summary>💨 Scenario 13-A: npm and Python Cache Strategies with Key Invalidation</summary>


**Objective:** Implement caching for npm and pip dependencies with correct key strategies that invalidate automatically when lock files change.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–12 complete; a repository with `package-lock.json` and/or `requirements.txt` (create them if needed).

**Context:** The cache `key` is a hash string that identifies whether a cache hit exists. Basing the key on the lock file hash (`hashFiles(...)`) ensures the cache is invalidated whenever dependencies change. The `restore-keys` fallback provides a partial cache restore when the exact key misses.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create sample dependency files (if they don't exist):

```bash
# Run locally or in a workflow step
echo '{"name":"demo","version":"1.0.0","dependencies":{"lodash":"^4.17.21"}}' > package.json
echo '{}' > package-lock.json  # simplified for demo
echo "requests==2.31.0" > requirements.txt
```

2. Create `.github/workflows/caching-demo.yml`:

```yaml
name: Caching Demo

on: [push, workflow_dispatch]

jobs:
  npm-with-cache:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Cache npm dependencies
        uses: actions/cache@v4
        id: npm-cache
        with:
          path: ~/.npm           # npm's global cache directory
          # Key includes runner OS and lockfile hash for correct invalidation
          key: ${{ runner.os }}-npm-${{ hashFiles('**/package-lock.json') }}
          # Fallback: use any existing npm cache for this OS (partial restore)
          restore-keys: |
            ${{ runner.os }}-npm-

      - name: Show cache hit/miss
        run: |
          echo "Cache hit: ${{ steps.npm-cache.outputs.cache-hit }}"
          # 'true' means exact key matched; 'false' means miss or restore-key match

      - name: Install npm dependencies
        # Even on cache hit, 'npm ci' is fast because it restores from ~/.npm
        run: npm ci --if-present

  python-with-cache:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.11'
          # setup-python has built-in cache support — preferred over manual cache
          cache: 'pip'

      - name: Install Python dependencies
        run: pip install -r requirements.txt

      - name: Verify installations
        run: pip list | grep requests

  manual-python-cache:
    # Shows manual cache approach for comparison with setup-python built-in
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.11'

      - name: Manual pip cache
        uses: actions/cache@v4
        with:
          # pip cache directory (varies by OS)
          path: ~/.cache/pip
          key: ${{ runner.os }}-pip-${{ hashFiles('**/requirements*.txt') }}
          restore-keys: |
            ${{ runner.os }}-pip-

      - run: pip install -r requirements.txt
```

3. Push twice and compare run times on the second push (cache hit expected).
4. Edit `requirements.txt` (add a new package), push again — observe cache miss and rebuild.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Second run shows `cache-hit: true` for npm job.
- [ ] After editing `requirements.txt`, cache misses and reinstalls dependencies.
- [ ] `setup-python` with `cache: 'pip'` is simpler and preferable to manual cache.
- [ ] `restore-keys` allows partial cache restore when exact key misses.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Cache never hits** → Verify the `path:` matches where the package manager stores its cache. `~/.npm` for npm, `~/.cache/pip` for pip on Linux. Use `echo $(pip cache dir)` to check.
- **`hashFiles` returns different values** → `hashFiles` is relative to the workspace root (`$GITHUB_WORKSPACE`). Verify the lock file path pattern is correct.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏎️ Scenario 13-B: Gradle/Maven Caching and Cache Size Management</summary>


**Objective:** Implement build tool caching for Java projects (Gradle and Maven), understand cache scope limitations, and practice cache busting.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 13-A complete; Java familiarity helpful but not required.

**Context:** Caches are scoped to the branch that created them. Pull requests can use the base branch's cache but cannot write back to it. Cache entries have a 7-day inactivity expiry and are evicted when the repository reaches 10 GB. Understanding scope prevents confusion when PRs don't benefit from feature branch caches.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/java-cache.yml`:

```yaml
name: Java Build Cache

on: [push, pull_request, workflow_dispatch]

jobs:
  gradle-build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-java@v4
        with:
          java-version: '21'
          distribution: 'temurin'
          # Built-in cache for Gradle — preferred approach
          cache: gradle

      - name: Make gradlew executable (if present)
        run: chmod +x gradlew 2>/dev/null || echo "No gradlew, using gradle"

      - name: Build with Gradle
        run: gradle --version  # Placeholder for: ./gradlew build

  maven-build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-java@v4
        with:
          java-version: '21'
          distribution: 'temurin'
          cache: maven  # Built-in Maven cache

      - name: Build with Maven
        run: mvn --version  # Placeholder for: mvn -B package

  manual-gradle-cache:
    # Manual cache example showing cache key structure
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-java@v4
        with:
          java-version: '21'
          distribution: 'temurin'

      - name: Cache Gradle packages
        uses: actions/cache@v4
        with:
          path: |
            ~/.gradle/caches
            ~/.gradle/wrapper
          # Version bump ('v1' suffix) to force cache bust when needed
          key: ${{ runner.os }}-gradle-v1-${{ hashFiles('**/*.gradle*', '**/gradle-wrapper.properties') }}
          restore-keys: |
            ${{ runner.os }}-gradle-v1-
            ${{ runner.os }}-gradle-

      - name: Build
        run: gradle --version
```

2. Trigger from a feature branch and observe that PRs can restore from the `main` branch cache.
3. Add `-v2` to the manual cache key to bust the cache (simulating a dependency conflict).

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `setup-java` with `cache: gradle` sets up caching automatically.
- [ ] Manual cache example shows correct `~/.gradle` path structure.
- [ ] Version suffix in key (`-v1`) can be incremented to force cache invalidation.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **PR doesn't use cache from main** → Caches from feature branches are not accessible to `main`, but `main`'s cache IS accessible to PRs. If the PR was pushed before main had a cache, there's nothing to restore.
- **Cache size growing unbounded** → Set retention-days on artifacts; for caches, the 7-day inactivity eviction handles it. Explicitly delete with `gh cache delete` for large stale caches.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 25 (Performance Optimization) for measuring cache impact on total workflow time; → Section 23 (Security) for avoiding sensitive data in caches.

</details>

---

2. Modify `pom.xml` → cache key changes → fresh download

**Objective:** Implement tiered caching for monorepo: shared cache, service-specific cache.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 13-D complete.

**Context:** Large monorepos need efficient caching: shared deps + service-specific. This scales builds.

1. Create shared layer cache for node_modules
2. Create service-specific layer for each service

### 📡 Section 14: Inter-Job Communication & Outputs (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [GitHub-Workflows-Guide.md](GitHub-Workflows-Guide.md) - Job Outputs section
**Overview:**

- Job outputs: defining and exporting step outputs
- Output interpolation in dependent jobs
- GITHUB_OUTPUT file for setting job outputs
- Artifact-based data passing for larger payloads
- Environment file sharing (GITHUB_ENV)
- Matrix job outputs and aggregation
- Output limits and best practices

**Practical Work:**

- Create workflows with job-to-job output passing
- Implement output aggregation from matrix jobs
- Use outputs in conditional job execution
- Pass complex data structures between jobs
- Test output limits and fallback strategies


<details>
<summary>📤 Scenario 14-A: Job Outputs and GITHUB_OUTPUT</summary>


**Objective:** Set step outputs using `GITHUB_OUTPUT`, consume them in subsequent steps, and pass job-level outputs to downstream jobs via `needs` context.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–13 complete.

**Context:** Step outputs written to `$GITHUB_OUTPUT` are available in subsequent steps via `${{ steps.<id>.outputs.<name> }}`. A job can expose step outputs as job outputs using the `outputs:` key at the job level. Downstream jobs access them via `${{ needs.<job>.outputs.<name> }}`.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/job-outputs.yml`:

```yaml
name: Job Outputs Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  prepare:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    # Declare what outputs this job exposes to downstream jobs
    outputs:
      version: ${{ steps.get-version.outputs.version }}
      environment: ${{ steps.determine-env.outputs.env }}
      should-deploy: ${{ steps.check-deploy.outputs.deploy }}

    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Get version from package.json (or generate one)
        id: get-version
        run: |
          # Try to read from package.json; fall back to git-based version
          if [ -f package.json ]; then
            VERSION=$(node -p "require('./package.json').version" 2>/dev/null || echo "1.0.0")
          else
            VERSION="1.0.${{ github.run_number }}"
          fi
          echo "version=${VERSION}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "Resolved version: ${VERSION}"

      - name: Determine deployment environment
        id: determine-env
        run: |
          BRANCH="${{ github.ref_name }}"
          if [[ "$BRANCH" == "main" ]]; then
            echo "env=production" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          elif [[ "$BRANCH" == "staging" ]]; then
            echo "env=staging" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          else
            echo "env=development" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          fi

      - name: Check if deployment is needed
        id: check-deploy
        run: |
          # Deploy only if version contains no '-dev' suffix
          VERSION="${{ steps.get-version.outputs.version }}"
          if [[ "$VERSION" != *"-dev"* ]]; then
            echo "deploy=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          else
            echo "deploy=false" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          fi

  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: prepare
    # Only deploy if the prepare job says to
    if: needs.prepare.outputs.should-deploy == 'true'
    steps:
      - name: Use outputs from prepare job
        run: |
          echo "Version    : ${{ needs.prepare.outputs.version }}"
          echo "Environment: ${{ needs.prepare.outputs.environment }}"
          echo "Deploying ${{ needs.prepare.outputs.version }} to ${{ needs.prepare.outputs.environment }}"

  notify:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: [prepare, deploy]
    if: always()
    steps:
      - run: |
          echo "Deploy result: ${{ needs.deploy.result }}"
          echo "Version      : ${{ needs.prepare.outputs.version }}"
```

2. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` from `main`.
3. Verify `deploy` job shows the correct version and environment.
4. Create a branch with a `-dev` version or ensure `should-deploy=false` to see the `deploy` job skipped.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `prepare` job outputs appear in `deploy` job via `needs.prepare.outputs`.
- [ ] `deploy` job is skipped when `should-deploy` is `false`.
- [ ] Multiple step outputs are aggregated into job-level outputs correctly.
- [ ] `notify` job runs regardless and shows correct `deploy` result.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Output is empty in downstream job** → Verify the job `outputs:` key maps the step output: `version: ${{ steps.get-version.outputs.version }}`. The mapping must exist at job level, not just step level.
- **`GITHUB_OUTPUT` not found** → This environment variable is automatically set; do not hardcode a path. Use `echo "key=value" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT`.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔄 Scenario 14-B: GITHUB_ENV and Environment Variable Sharing</summary>


**Objective:** Use `GITHUB_ENV` to set environment variables that persist across subsequent steps in the same job, and contrast with `GITHUB_OUTPUT` for inter-job sharing.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 14-A complete.

**Context:** `GITHUB_ENV` sets environment variables that are available in all subsequent steps of the same job. Unlike `GITHUB_OUTPUT`, these variables are NOT available in other jobs. For multi-line values, use the heredoc syntax. This file-based approach replaced the deprecated `::set-env::` workflow command.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/github-env-demo.yml`:

```yaml
name: GITHUB_ENV Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  env-sharing:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Set environment variables for subsequent steps
        run: |
          # Single-line variable
          echo "APP_VERSION=2.0.${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_ENV
          echo "BUILD_DATE=$(date -u +%Y-%m-%d)" >> $GITHUB_ENV

          # Multi-line variable using heredoc syntax
          echo "RELEASE_NOTES<<EOF" >> $GITHUB_ENV
          echo "Version 2.0.${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_ENV
          echo "Built on $(date -u +%Y-%m-%d)" >> $GITHUB_ENV
          echo "Commit: ${{ github.sha }}" >> $GITHUB_ENV
          echo "EOF" >> $GITHUB_ENV

      - name: Use environment variables in next step
        run: |
          # Variables set via GITHUB_ENV are available here
          echo "App version : $APP_VERSION"
          echo "Build date  : $BUILD_DATE"
          echo "Release notes:"
          echo "$RELEASE_NOTES"

      - name: Demonstrate GITHUB_PATH for PATH modifications
        run: |
          # Add a custom directory to PATH for subsequent steps
          echo "$HOME/.local/bin" >> $GITHUB_PATH
          mkdir -p "$HOME/.local/bin"
          echo '#!/bin/bash\necho "Custom tool v1.0"' > "$HOME/.local/bin/my-tool"
          chmod +x "$HOME/.local/bin/my-tool"

      - name: Use the custom PATH tool
        run: my-tool  # available because GITHUB_PATH was updated

  contrast-with-output:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Show scope difference
        run: |
          echo "GITHUB_ENV  = available in subsequent STEPS of the same JOB"
          echo "GITHUB_OUTPUT = available in downstream JOBS via needs context"
          echo "GITHUB_PATH = modifies PATH for subsequent steps in same job"
```

2. Trigger and verify the `APP_VERSION` and `BUILD_DATE` are available in the second step.
3. Verify the multi-line `RELEASE_NOTES` variable preserves newlines.
4. Verify `my-tool` is found after updating `GITHUB_PATH`.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `APP_VERSION` set in step 1 is readable in step 2 without explicit `env:`.
- [ ] Multi-line variable with heredoc syntax preserves all three lines.
- [ ] `my-tool` runs successfully after `GITHUB_PATH` update.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 10 (Matrix Strategies) for understanding why `GITHUB_ENV` doesn't persist across matrix job cells; → Section 27 (Job Summaries) for using `GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY` as another special environment file.

</details>

### 🐛 Section 15: Workflow Debugging & Troubleshooting (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [12-Workflow-Debugging.md](12-Workflow-Debugging.md), [19-Common-Failures-Troubleshooting.md](19-Common-Failures-Troubleshooting.md) (first half)
**Overview:**

- Debug logging: step context and secrets redaction
- Runner diagnostics information
- Log retention and access via UI/API
- Common failure patterns and causes
- Timeout and resource exhaustion issues
- YAML parsing and syntax errors
- Matrix job failure correlation

**Practical Work:**

- Enable debug logging in a workflow run

- Diagnose timeout issues
- Fix common YAML parsing errors

<details>
<summary>🔍 Scenario 15-A: Enable Debug Logging and Analyze Logs</summary>


**Objective:** Enable step-debug logging via repository secrets, interpret runner diagnostic logs, and build a diagnostic step that surfaces useful context when workflows fail.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–14 complete; repository admin access to add secrets.

**Context:** GitHub Actions provides two debug logging secrets: `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG` enables verbose step output (all `::debug::` messages), and `ACTIONS_RUNNER_DEBUG` logs runner-level infrastructure details. Both are enabled by setting the secret value to `true`. For one-off debugging without permanent secrets, re-run with the "Enable debug logging" checkbox.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Navigate to **Repository → Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions → New repository secret**.
2. Add: `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG` = `true`

3. Create `.github/workflows/debug-logging.yml`:

```yaml
name: Debug Logging Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  debug-demo:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Emit debug messages
        run: |
          # These appear only when ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG=true
          echo "::debug::This is a debug message — only visible with debug logging"
          echo "::notice::This is a notice — always visible in log annotations"
          echo "::warning::This is a warning — always visible"
          echo "Normal output — always visible"

      - name: Group log output
        run: |
          echo "::group::Detailed System Information"
          uname -a
          df -h
          free -m
          env | sort | grep -v SECRET | grep -v TOKEN
          echo "::endgroup::"
          echo "System info captured (collapsed in UI)"

      - name: Diagnostic context dump
        if: always()  # ensure this runs even on failure
        run: |
          echo "=== DIAGNOSTIC CONTEXT ==="
          echo "Workflow   : ${{ github.workflow }}"
          echo "Run ID     : ${{ github.run_id }}"
          echo "Run number : ${{ github.run_number }}"
          echo "Actor      : ${{ github.actor }}"
          echo "Branch     : ${{ github.ref_name }}"
          echo "SHA        : ${{ github.sha }}"
          echo "Event      : ${{ github.event_name }}"
          echo "Runner OS  : ${{ runner.os }}"
          echo "Runner arch: ${{ runner.arch }}"

      - name: Simulate a failure with useful error message
        run: |
          echo "::error file=src/app.js,line=42,col=8::Null pointer dereference — variable 'user' is undefined"
          exit 1

      - name: This step is skipped because previous failed
        run: echo "Never runs"
```

4. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` with debug logging enabled.
5. Compare the log verbosity with and without `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG=true`.
6. Observe the `::group::` collapsible section in the UI.
7. Note the `::error::` annotation linking to a file/line.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Debug messages appear in logs when `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG=true`.
- [ ] `::group::` creates a collapsible section in the UI.
- [ ] `::error::` creates a file annotation in the PR/commit view.
- [ ] Diagnostic context step runs even after the failure (`if: always()`).

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Debug messages not appearing** → Verify the secret name is exactly `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG` (case-sensitive) with value `true` (not `True` or `1`).
- **Annotations not appearing on PR** → Annotations are only visible on the commit/PR that triggered the workflow. They don't appear for `workflow_dispatch` triggered runs in the PR view.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔧 Scenario 15-B: Diagnosing YAML Syntax Errors and Timeout Issues</summary>


**Objective:** Intentionally introduce and fix common YAML errors, and configure `timeout-minutes` to handle runaway steps.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 15-A complete; VS Code with the GitHub Actions extension installed (Section 2).

**Context:** YAML is whitespace-sensitive. Common errors include incorrect indentation, wrong block scalar style (`|` vs `>`), and missing quotes around `on:` event names. Workflow YAML is validated at push time — the workflow will show as invalid before any runner picks it up. Timeouts prevent billing waste from hung processes.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create a workflow with intentional errors to study the error messages:

```yaml
# INTENTIONALLY BROKEN — study the error messages, then fix
name: YAML Error Study

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  broken-job:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
    - name: Bad indentation (steps should be 6 spaces or 3 x 2-space indent)
      run: echo "This fails due to the 4-space indent on steps"
    - name: Second step
       run: echo "Extra space before run causes mapping key error"
```

2. Push this file and observe the workflow error in the Actions tab before it runs.
3. Fix the indentation and push again.

4. Create a proper timeout demonstration:

```yaml
name: Timeout Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  job-with-timeout:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    timeout-minutes: 2  # entire job cancelled after 2 minutes
    steps:
      - name: Quick step
        timeout-minutes: 1  # individual step timeout
        run: echo "Fast step — completes in seconds"

      - name: Simulated hung process
        timeout-minutes: 1  # this step will time out
        continue-on-error: true  # allow job to continue despite timeout
        run: |
          echo "Starting potentially hung process..."
          sleep 120  # will be killed at 1-minute step timeout
          echo "This line never executes"

      - name: Cleanup after timeout
        if: always()
        run: echo "Cleanup runs regardless of timeout"
```

5. Push and observe the hung step being killed at 1 minute with exit code 124.
6. Verify the cleanup step still runs due to `if: always()`.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] YAML indentation errors produce clear validation messages in the Actions tab.
- [ ] VS Code highlights indentation errors with the GitHub Actions extension.
- [ ] The `sleep 120` step is killed at 1 minute with a timeout annotation.
- [ ] Cleanup step runs after the timeout.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Workflow shows as invalid but no error message** → Click on the workflow name in the Actions tab; invalid workflows show a banner with the specific YAML parse error.
- **`timeout-minutes` seems to be ignored** → Ensure `timeout-minutes` is at the correct level (job-level or step-level). Job-level timeout includes all steps; step-level timeout is per-step.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 2 (VS Code extension) for YAML schema validation that catches errors before pushing; → Section 26 (Troubleshooting) for production-level failure diagnosis techniques.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🌐 Scenario 16-A: Query and Manage Workflow Runs via REST API</summary>


**Objective:** Use the GitHub CLI and REST API to list workflow runs, retrieve job logs, cancel runs, and download artifacts programmatically.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–15 complete; GitHub CLI (`gh`) installed locally or used via runner; PAT with `repo` and `actions: read` scope or `GITHUB_TOKEN`.

**Context:** The GitHub Actions REST API provides endpoints for programmatic workflow management. The GitHub CLI (`gh`) wraps these endpoints with a friendly interface and is pre-installed on all GitHub-hosted runners. This is valuable for CI/CD automation, status dashboards, and integrating GitHub Actions into external tooling.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. On your local machine (or in a workflow step), authenticate:

```bash
gh auth login
# Or set GH_TOKEN environment variable
```

2. Create `.github/workflows/api-automation.yml`:

```yaml
name: REST API Automation Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  api-queries:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      actions: read   # required to query workflow runs
      contents: read

    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: List recent workflow runs
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          echo "=== Recent workflow runs ==="
          gh run list \
            --repo ${{ github.repository }} \
            --limit 5 \
            --json databaseId,displayTitle,status,conclusion,createdAt \
            --template '{{range .}}{{.databaseId}} | {{.status}} | {{.conclusion}} | {{.displayTitle}}\n{{end}}'

      - name: Get current run details
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          echo "=== Current run details ==="
          gh run view ${{ github.run_id }} \
            --repo ${{ github.repository }} \
            --json status,conclusion,jobs

      - name: List jobs in current run
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          echo "=== Jobs in this run ==="
          gh api \
            /repos/${{ github.repository }}/actions/runs/${{ github.run_id }}/jobs \
            --jq '.jobs[] | "\(.name): \(.status) — \(.conclusion // "in_progress")"'

      - name: List available workflows
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          echo "=== Workflows in this repo ==="
          gh workflow list \
            --repo ${{ github.repository }} \
            --all

      - name: Download artifacts from current run (if any exist)
        env:
          GH_TOKEN: ${{ github.token }}
        run: |
          echo "=== Artifacts in current run ==="
          ARTIFACTS=$(gh api \
            /repos/${{ github.repository }}/actions/runs/${{ github.run_id }}/artifacts \
            --jq '.total_count')
          echo "Total artifacts: $ARTIFACTS"
          if [ "$ARTIFACTS" -gt "0" ]; then
            gh run download ${{ github.run_id }} \
              --repo ${{ github.repository }} \
              --dir ./downloaded-artifacts
            ls -la ./downloaded-artifacts/
          fi
```

3. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` and review the output of each API query step.
4. Run the same `gh` commands locally against your repository to practice.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Recent workflow runs are listed with status and conclusion.
- [ ] Current run jobs are retrieved via REST API.
- [ ] All available workflows are listed.
- [ ] Artifact download works when artifacts exist.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`gh: error: unknown flag`** → Some `gh` flags vary by version. Use `gh run list --help` to see available options on the runner's installed version.
- **`actions: read` permission insufficient** → Some API endpoints require higher permissions. Check the specific endpoint's documentation for required scopes.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🚀 Scenario 16-B: Trigger Workflows and Manage Deployments via API</summary>


**Objective:** Trigger a `workflow_dispatch` event via the REST API, approve pending deployments programmatically, and cancel a running workflow.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 16-A complete; a workflow with `workflow_dispatch` inputs.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/api-triggered.yml`:

```yaml
name: API Triggered Workflow

on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      deploy-target:
        description: 'Deployment target'
        type: string
        default: 'staging'
      debug-mode:
        description: 'Enable debug mode'
        type: boolean
        default: false

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Show trigger parameters
        run: |
          echo "Deploy target: ${{ inputs.deploy-target }}"
          echo "Debug mode   : ${{ inputs.debug-mode }}"
          echo "Triggered by API or manual dispatch"
          sleep 30  # Long enough to demonstrate cancellation
```

2. Trigger the workflow via REST API using `gh`:

```bash
# Trigger with inputs
gh workflow run api-triggered.yml \
  --repo OWNER/REPO \
  --ref main \
  --field deploy-target=production \
  --field debug-mode=true

# Get the run ID of the just-triggered run
sleep 3
LATEST_RUN=$(gh run list \
  --workflow api-triggered.yml \
  --repo OWNER/REPO \
  --limit 1 \
  --json databaseId \
  --jq '.[0].databaseId')

echo "Triggered run ID: $LATEST_RUN"
```

3. Cancel the run programmatically before `sleep 30` completes:

```bash
# Cancel the running workflow
gh run cancel $LATEST_RUN --repo OWNER/REPO
echo "Run $LATEST_RUN cancelled"
```

4. Verify the run shows as "Cancelled" in the Actions UI.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `workflow_dispatch` inputs are passed correctly via the API.
- [ ] `sleep 30` step can be interrupted by a programmatic cancel.
- [ ] The UI shows the run as "Cancelled" after the API call.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 8 (Environments) for approving pending deployments via `POST /repos/{owner}/{repo}/actions/runs/{run_id}/pending_deployments`; → Section 17 (Reusable Workflows) for triggering reusable workflows via API.

</details>

## ♻️ Week 5: Reusable Workflows & Actions

### ♻️ Section 17: Reusable Workflows & Workflow Sharing (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [11-Workflow-Sharing.md](11-Workflow-Sharing.md)
**Overview:**

- Reusable workflow concept: workflow_call
- Input/output mapping for reusable workflows
- Secrets in reusable workflows
- Adding reusable workflows from same org/repo
- Public action repository workflows
- Versioning and tagging strategies
- Calling workflows from different repos/orgs

**Practical Work:**

- Create a reusable workflow for common tasks
- Call reusable workflows with various inputs
- Implement proper versioning with tags
- Pass secrets to reusable workflows
- Test reusable workflow output handling


<details>
<summary>♻️ Scenario 17-A: Create and Call a Reusable Workflow</summary>


**Objective:** Create a reusable `workflow_call` workflow with typed inputs, outputs, and secret inheritance, then call it from a caller workflow.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–16 complete; repository with at least one branch.

**Context:** Reusable workflows are called via `uses: owner/repo/.github/workflows/file.yml@ref`. They accept typed `inputs:` and `secrets:` declared in their `on.workflow_call:` block. Outputs from reusable workflows propagate back to the caller. They reduce duplication across team repositories.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/reusable-deploy.yml` (the reusable workflow):

```yaml
name: Reusable Deploy Workflow

# The workflow_call trigger makes this reusable
on:
  workflow_call:
    inputs:
      environment:
        description: 'Target deployment environment'
        type: string
        required: true
      version:
        description: 'Application version to deploy'
        type: string
        default: 'latest'
      dry-run:
        description: 'Perform a dry run without actual deployment'
        type: boolean
        default: false
    secrets:
      deploy-token:
        description: 'Token for deployment authentication'
        required: true
    outputs:
      deploy-url:
        description: 'URL of the deployed application'
        value: ${{ jobs.deploy.outputs.url }}

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      url: ${{ steps.do-deploy.outputs.deploy-url }}
    steps:
      - name: Validate inputs
        run: |
          echo "Environment: ${{ inputs.environment }}"
          echo "Version    : ${{ inputs.version }}"
          echo "Dry run    : ${{ inputs.dry-run }}"
          echo "Token set  : ${{ secrets.deploy-token != '' }}"

      - name: Perform deployment
        id: do-deploy
        run: |
          if [ "${{ inputs.dry-run }}" == "true" ]; then
            echo "DRY RUN — no actual deployment"
          else
            echo "Deploying ${{ inputs.version }} to ${{ inputs.environment }}"
          fi
          # Set the output URL
          URL="https://${{ inputs.environment }}.example.com"
          echo "deploy-url=${URL}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Post-deploy verification
        run: |
          echo "Deployment to ${{ inputs.environment }} complete"
          echo "Accessible at: https://${{ inputs.environment }}.example.com"
```

2. Create `.github/workflows/main-pipeline.yml` (the caller workflow):

```yaml
name: Main CI/CD Pipeline

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  workflow_dispatch:

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      version: ${{ steps.version.outputs.v }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - id: version
        run: echo "v=1.0.${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

  deploy-staging:
    needs: build
    # Call the reusable workflow — same repo, current branch
    uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-deploy.yml
    with:
      environment: staging
      version: ${{ needs.build.outputs.version }}
      dry-run: false
    secrets:
      deploy-token: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}

  deploy-production:
    needs: deploy-staging
    uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-deploy.yml
    with:
      environment: production
      version: ${{ needs.build.outputs.version }}
      dry-run: false
    secrets:
      deploy-token: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}

  summary:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    needs: [deploy-staging, deploy-production]
    if: always()
    steps:
      - run: |
          echo "Staging URL   : ${{ needs.deploy-staging.outputs.deploy-url }}"
          echo "Production URL: ${{ needs.deploy-production.outputs.deploy-url }}"
```

3. Push to `main` and observe both deploy jobs calling the same reusable workflow.
4. Verify the `deploy-url` output propagates from the reusable workflow back to the caller.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Reusable workflow runs as two separate jobs (staging and production).
- [ ] `deploy-url` output from reusable workflow appears in `summary` job.
- [ ] Secret `deploy-token` is accessible inside the reusable workflow.
- [ ] Input `dry-run: true` skips actual deployment.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`uses: ./.github/workflows/` fails** → The `./.github/workflows/` shorthand only works within the same repository. For cross-repo calls use `owner/repo/.github/workflows/file.yml@ref`.
- **Outputs from reusable workflow are empty** → The output must be declared in the reusable workflow's `on.workflow_call.outputs:` AND mapped in the job's `outputs:` key.

**Time Estimate:** 30–35 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔗 Scenario 17-B: Cross-Repository Reusable Workflows and Versioning</summary>


**Objective:** Call a reusable workflow from a different repository, understand `secrets: inherit`, and implement version pinning with tags.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 17-A complete; a second GitHub repository (or use a public repo).

**Context:** Reusable workflows can be called from any repository if the workflow file is in a public repo, or within the same organization for private repos. Versioning with tags (`@v1`, `@v1.2.3`) is critical for stability. `secrets: inherit` passes all caller secrets to the reusable workflow without explicitly mapping each one.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create a caller that uses `secrets: inherit`:

```yaml
name: Cross-Repo Reusable Workflow Call

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  call-shared-workflow:
    # Call from same repo but pinned to a specific tag
    uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-deploy.yml@main
    with:
      environment: development
      version: '1.0.0'
      dry-run: true
    # Pass ALL caller secrets to the reusable workflow
    # Avoid if you want explicit control over which secrets are shared
    secrets: inherit
```

2. Create a Git tag and push it:

```bash
git tag -a v1.0.0 -m "Release 1.0.0"
git push origin v1.0.0
```

3. Update the caller to pin to the tag:

```yaml
    uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable-deploy.yml@v1.0.0
```

4. Verify the tag-pinned call runs the exact version of the workflow at that tag.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `secrets: inherit` passes all secrets without explicit mapping.
- [ ] Tag-pinned call (`@v1.0.0`) uses the workflow file at that specific commit.
- [ ] Modifying the workflow on `main` does not affect tag-pinned callers.

**Time Estimate:** 20–25 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 18 (Custom Actions) for the parallel concept of action versioning with major version tags (`@v1`); → Section 22 (Enterprise) for organization-level starter workflows that call shared reusable workflows.

</details>

---

### 🧩 Section 18: Custom Actions - Types & Structure (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [15-Creating-Publishing-Actions.md](15-Creating-Publishing-Actions.md) (first half)
**Overview:**

- Action types: JavaScript, Docker, Composite
- Action metadata: action.yml structure
- Inputs and outputs definitions
- Branding and descriptions
- Running vs docker container execution
- Composite actions: combining existing actions
- Action composition patterns

**Practical Work:**

- Create a composite action combining multiple actions
- Build a JavaScript action with inputs/outputs
- Define action.yml metadata properly
- Test action with workflow
- Document action usage


<details>
<summary>🧩 Scenario 18-A: Build a Composite Action</summary>


**Objective:** Create a composite action that combines multiple steps into a reusable action, with typed inputs, outputs, and proper `action.yml` metadata.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–17 complete; understanding of YAML and shell scripting.

**Context:** Composite actions contain multiple `run` steps and can reference other actions. They are the simplest action type — no JavaScript or Docker required. They live in a directory within your repo (or a dedicated action repo) and are referenced via their path in workflows. Unlike reusable workflows, actions run as steps within a job.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create the action directory and `action.yml`:

```bash
mkdir -p .github/actions/setup-and-validate
```

2. Create `.github/actions/setup-and-validate/action.yml`:

```yaml
name: 'Setup and Validate'
description: 'Sets up Node.js, installs dependencies, and validates the project'
author: 'your-github-username'

branding:
  icon: 'check-circle'
  color: 'green'

inputs:
  node-version:
    description: 'Node.js version to use'
    required: false
    default: '20'
  working-directory:
    description: 'Directory containing package.json'
    required: false
    default: '.'
  run-tests:
    description: 'Whether to run tests after setup'
    required: false
    default: 'true'

outputs:
  node-version-installed:
    description: 'The actual Node.js version that was installed'
    value: ${{ steps.node-info.outputs.version }}
  validation-passed:
    description: 'Whether validation passed (true/false)'
    value: ${{ steps.validate.outputs.passed }}

runs:
  using: composite  # composite action type
  steps:
    - name: Setup Node.js
      uses: actions/setup-node@v4
      with:
        node-version: ${{ inputs.node-version }}

    - name: Capture installed Node version
      id: node-info
      shell: bash
      run: echo "version=$(node --version)" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

    - name: Install dependencies
      shell: bash
      working-directory: ${{ inputs.working-directory }}
      run: |
        if [ -f package-lock.json ]; then
          npm ci
        elif [ -f package.json ]; then
          npm install
        else
          echo "No package.json found — skipping install"
        fi

    - name: Validate project
      id: validate
      shell: bash
      working-directory: ${{ inputs.working-directory }}
      run: |
        # Run lint if available
        if npm run lint --if-present 2>/dev/null; then
          echo "passed=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
        else
          echo "passed=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT  # pass even without lint
        fi
        echo "Validation complete"

    - name: Run tests (if enabled)
      shell: bash
      if: inputs.run-tests == 'true'
      working-directory: ${{ inputs.working-directory }}
      run: npm test --if-present || echo "No tests defined"
```

3. Create `.github/workflows/use-composite-action.yml` to test it:

```yaml
name: Use Composite Action

on: [push, workflow_dispatch]

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup and validate
        id: setup
        # Reference the action by its relative path
        uses: ./.github/actions/setup-and-validate
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          run-tests: 'false'

      - name: Use action outputs
        run: |
          echo "Node installed: ${{ steps.setup.outputs.node-version-installed }}"
          echo "Validation    : ${{ steps.setup.outputs.validation-passed }}"
```

4. Push and verify the composite action runs all its steps as part of the `build` job.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Composite action steps appear as sub-steps in the job log.
- [ ] Outputs (`node-version-installed`, `validation-passed`) are readable in the calling workflow.
- [ ] `inputs.run-tests == 'false'` correctly skips the test step.
- [ ] Action branding metadata is defined in `action.yml`.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`uses: ./.github/actions/...` fails** → The path must point to a directory containing `action.yml`. Verify the directory structure. Also, the action must be checked out first (`uses: actions/checkout@v4` before the action reference).
- **`shell: bash` required in composite actions** → Unlike regular workflow steps, composite action steps must explicitly specify `shell:` for `run:` steps.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🟨 Scenario 18-B: JavaScript Action with Inputs and Outputs</summary>


**Objective:** Create a minimal JavaScript action that processes an input string, returns an output, and handles errors using `@actions/core`.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 18-A complete; Node.js installed locally; basic JavaScript knowledge.

**Context:** JavaScript actions run directly on the runner using Node.js. They use the `@actions/core` package for inputs/outputs, `@actions/github` for API access, and `@actions/exec` for subprocess execution. The `node_modules` must be committed or the code pre-bundled with `ncc`.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create the action directory:

```bash
mkdir -p .github/actions/string-transformer
cd .github/actions/string-transformer
npm init -y
npm install @actions/core
```

2. Create `.github/actions/string-transformer/action.yml`:

```yaml
name: 'String Transformer'
description: 'Transforms an input string to uppercase or lowercase'
inputs:
  input-string:
    description: 'The string to transform'
    required: true
  transform:
    description: 'Transformation: uppercase or lowercase'
    required: false
    default: 'uppercase'
outputs:
  result:
    description: 'The transformed string'
runs:
  using: node20
  main: index.js
```

3. Create `.github/actions/string-transformer/index.js`:

```javascript
const core = require('@actions/core');

try {
  const inputString = core.getInput('input-string', { required: true });
  const transform = core.getInput('transform');

  core.debug(`Processing: "${inputString}" with transform: ${transform}`);

  let result;
  if (transform === 'uppercase') {
    result = inputString.toUpperCase();
  } else if (transform === 'lowercase') {
    result = inputString.toLowerCase();
  } else {
    core.setFailed(`Unknown transform: ${transform}. Use 'uppercase' or 'lowercase'`);
    process.exit(1);
  }

  core.setOutput('result', result);
  core.info(`Transformed result: ${result}`);
} catch (error) {
  core.setFailed(error.message);
}
```

4. Commit `index.js`, `action.yml`, and `node_modules` (necessary for JS actions without `ncc`).

5. Test in a workflow:

```yaml
      - uses: ./.github/actions/string-transformer
        id: transform
        with:
          input-string: 'hello from github actions'
          transform: uppercase

      - run: echo "Result: ${{ steps.transform.outputs.result }}"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Action outputs `HELLO FROM GITHUB ACTIONS`.
- [ ] Invalid `transform` value causes `core.setFailed()` to mark the step red.
- [ ] `core.debug()` messages appear with `ACTIONS_STEP_DEBUG=true`.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 19 (Publishing Actions) for distributing this action to the Marketplace with versioned releases; → Section 24 (Security) for pinning third-party actions to commit SHAs.

</details>

---

**Context:** Production actions must handle edge cases and provide clear error messages.

2. Add try-catch for error handling

**Overview:**

- Public vs private action distribution

<details>
<summary>🏪 Scenario 19-A: Prepare an Action for Marketplace Publishing</summary>


**Objective:** Add all required metadata to `action.yml`, write comprehensive README documentation, and create a versioned release following the major-version-tag convention.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–18 complete; a completed composite or JavaScript action (from Section 18); the action must be in its own repository for Marketplace publishing.

**Context:** GitHub Marketplace listing requirements: `action.yml` must include `name`, `description`, `branding` (icon + color), and `author`. The repository must be public. The README appears on the Marketplace listing page. The convention for action releases is major version tags (`v1`, `v2`) that float to the latest minor/patch, allowing users to reference `@v1` without needing to track patch releases.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Ensure `action.yml` has all required fields:

```yaml
name: 'Setup and Validate'
description: 'Sets up Node.js, installs dependencies, validates, and optionally runs tests. Saves setup time by combining common CI steps.'
author: 'your-github-username'

branding:
  icon: 'check-circle'   # icon from feathericons.com
  color: 'green'          # blue, green, gray, orange, purple, red, yellow, or white

inputs:
  node-version:
    description: 'Node.js version to install (e.g., 18, 20, 22)'
    required: false
    default: '20'
  working-directory:
    description: 'Working directory containing package.json'
    required: false
    default: '.'
  run-tests:
    description: 'Set to "true" to run npm test after setup'
    required: false
    default: 'false'

outputs:
  node-version-installed:
    description: 'The exact Node.js version installed (e.g., v20.11.0)'
    value: ${{ steps.node-info.outputs.version }}

runs:
  using: composite
  steps:
    - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
      with:
        node-version: ${{ inputs.node-version }}
    - id: node-info
      shell: bash
      run: echo "version=$(node --version)" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
    - shell: bash
      run: npm ci
```

2. Create `README.md` with usage documentation:

```markdown
## Setup and Validate Action

Sets up Node.js, installs dependencies, validates, and optionally runs tests.

### Usage

    - uses: your-username/setup-and-validate-action@v1
      with:
        node-version: '20'
        run-tests: 'true'

### Inputs

| Input | Required | Default | Description |
|-------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `node-version` | No | `20` | Node.js version to install |
| `working-directory` | No | `.` | Directory containing package.json |
| `run-tests` | No | `false` | Run npm test after setup |

### Outputs

| Output | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `node-version-installed` | Exact Node.js version installed |

### Example

    jobs:
      build:
        runs-on: ubuntu-latest
        steps:
          - uses: actions/checkout@v4
          - id: setup
            uses: your-username/setup-and-validate-action@v1
          - run: echo "Node ${{ steps.setup.outputs.node-version-installed }}"
```

3. Create the action test workflow in the action's repository:

```yaml
name: Test Action

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Test action with defaults
        uses: ./  # test the action at the current repo root
        id: default-test

      - name: Verify output
        run: |
          VERSION="${{ steps.default-test.outputs.node-version-installed }}"
          echo "Installed: $VERSION"
          if [[ "$VERSION" =~ ^v[0-9]+ ]]; then
            echo "Output format is valid"
          else
            echo "Invalid output format: $VERSION"
            exit 1
          fi
```

4. Create the release and versioned tags:

```bash
# Create a full semantic version tag
git tag -a v1.0.0 -m "Initial release v1.0.0"
git push origin v1.0.0

# Create/move the floating major version tag
git tag -fa v1 -m "Update v1 to v1.0.0"
git push origin v1 --force
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] `action.yml` contains all required branding fields.
- [ ] README documents all inputs and outputs in a table.
- [ ] Self-test workflow passes using `uses: ./`.
- [ ] Both `v1.0.0` and `v1` tags exist and point to the same commit.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Marketplace listing not appearing** → Repository must be public and `action.yml` must be at the root of the repository (not in `.github/actions/`).
- **`git tag -fa` fails** → The `--force` flag requires the remote to allow force-push to tags. Use `git push origin :refs/tags/v1 && git push origin v1` as an alternative.

**Time Estimate:** 30–35 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🚀 Scenario 19-B: Automated Action Release Workflow</summary>


**Objective:** Create a workflow that automatically moves the major version tag on release publication, following GitHub's recommended action versioning pattern.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/release-action.yml`:

```yaml
name: Release Action

on:
  release:
    types: [published]

jobs:
  release:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: write  # required to create and update tags
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with:
          fetch-depth: 0  # fetch all history for tag operations

      - name: Extract major version
        id: version
        run: |
          TAG="${{ github.ref_name }}"  # e.g., v1.2.3
          MAJOR="${TAG%%.*}"            # extract v1
          echo "tag=${TAG}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "major=${MAJOR}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "Release tag : $TAG"
          echo "Major tag   : $MAJOR"

      - name: Update major version tag
        run: |
          MAJOR="${{ steps.version.outputs.major }}"
          TAG="${{ steps.version.outputs.tag }}"
          git tag -d $MAJOR 2>/dev/null || true
          git push origin :refs/tags/$MAJOR 2>/dev/null || true
          git tag $MAJOR
          git push origin $MAJOR
          echo "Major tag $MAJOR now points to $TAG"

      - name: Update CHANGELOG
        run: |
          echo "## ${{ steps.version.outputs.tag }} — $(date +%Y-%m-%d)" >> CHANGELOG.md
          echo "See release notes: ${{ github.event.release.html_url }}" >> CHANGELOG.md
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Creating a `v1.2.3` GitHub Release automatically moves `v1` to that commit.
- [ ] Old `v1` tag is deleted and recreated at the new release SHA.
- [ ] Workflow requires `contents: write` permission.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 18 (Custom Actions) for building the action being published; → Section 24 (Security) for why users should pin to full SHA instead of mutable major tags for security-critical workflows.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🏷️ Scenario 19-C: Version Management and Semantic Versioning for Actions</summary>


**Objective:** Implement semantic versioning for actions with major version tags and release branches.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 19-B complete.

**Context:** Version management prevents breaking users. Semantic versioning (major.minor.patch) enables safe updates.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Tag releases with semantic versions: v1.0.0, v1.1.0, v2.0.0
2. Maintain major version tag: v1 always points to latest v1.x
3. Create release branches for backports
4. Users pin to v1 for automatic updates within major version

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Semantic versioning implemented
- [ ] Major version tag tracks latest
- [ ] Users can upgrade safely

**Time Estimate:** 20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 18 (Actions) for versioning concepts.

</details>

### 🏃 Section 20: GitHub-Hosted Runners (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [16-Managing-Runners.md](16-Managing-Runners.md) (first half)
**Overview:**

- GitHub-hosted runner types (Ubuntu, Windows, macOS)
- Available runner images and preinstalled software
- Runner labels and selection
- Image updates and deprecations (Ubuntu 20.04, Windows Server 2025)

<details>
<summary>🏃 Scenario 20-A: Target Different Runner Types and Verify Environments</summary>


**Objective:** Create a matrix workflow that runs across all three GitHub-hosted OS types, verifies the preinstalled tools, and demonstrates runner-specific behavior.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–19 complete.

**Context:** GitHub provides `ubuntu-latest`, `windows-latest`, and `macos-latest` runners. Each has a different toolcache, different path conventions (`/` vs `\`), and different default shells (`bash` vs `pwsh`). Testing across runners catches cross-platform incompatibilities early.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/runner-matrix.yml`:

```yaml
name: Runner Type Matrix

on: [push, workflow_dispatch]

jobs:
  explore-runners:
    strategy:
      fail-fast: false
      matrix:
        os: [ubuntu-latest, windows-latest, macos-latest]
    runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: OS information
        run: |
          echo "Runner OS    : ${{ runner.os }}"
          echo "Runner arch  : ${{ runner.arch }}"
          echo "Runner name  : ${{ runner.name }}"
          echo "Temp dir     : ${{ runner.temp }}"
          echo "Tool cache   : ${{ runner.tool_cache }}"

      - name: Check common tools (bash-compatible)
        if: runner.os != 'Windows'
        run: |
          echo "=== Node.js ==="
          node --version
          npm --version
          echo "=== Python ==="
          python3 --version
          echo "=== Docker ==="
          docker --version || echo "Docker not available on macOS"
          echo "=== Git ==="
          git --version

      - name: Check common tools (PowerShell)
        if: runner.os == 'Windows'
        shell: pwsh
        run: |
          Write-Host "=== Node.js ==="
          node --version
          npm --version
          Write-Host "=== Python ==="
          python --version
          Write-Host "=== Git ==="
          git --version

      - name: Cross-platform file operations
        run: |
          echo "Creating test file"
          mkdir -p test-output
          echo "Hello from ${{ runner.os }}" > test-output/runner-info.txt
          cat test-output/runner-info.txt

      - name: Upload runner info artifact
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: runner-info-${{ matrix.os }}
          path: test-output/

  compare-results:
    needs: explore-runners
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Download all artifacts
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
        with:
          pattern: runner-info-*
          merge-multiple: false

      - name: Compare outputs
        run: |
          echo "=== Runner Outputs ==="
          for dir in runner-info-*/; do
            echo "--- $dir ---"
            cat "${dir}runner-info.txt"
          done
```

2. Push and observe the three parallel jobs in the Actions UI.
3. Review that the artifact content differs per OS.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] All three OS types run in parallel.
- [ ] Windows uses `shell: pwsh` syntax.
- [ ] Per-OS artifacts contain OS-specific content.
- [ ] `runner.os`, `runner.arch`, and `runner.tool_cache` are populated correctly.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **`docker --version` fails on macOS** → macOS runners don't include Docker by default. Use `ubuntu-latest` for Docker-dependent steps.
- **Path separator issues on Windows** → Use `${{ runner.temp }}` instead of hardcoded paths, and use forward slashes `/` in most contexts.

**Time Estimate:** 25–30 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>📌 Scenario 20-B: Runner Image Pinning and Toolcache Inspection</summary>


**Objective:** Pin to a specific runner image, inspect the toolcache, and simulate a runner image migration from `ubuntu-20.04` to `ubuntu-22.04`.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create `.github/workflows/runner-pinning.yml`:

```yaml
name: Runner Pinning Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  pinned-runner:
    runs-on: ubuntu-22.04  # pin to specific image version
    steps:
      - name: Verify runner image
        run: |
          echo "=== OS Version ==="
          cat /etc/os-release | grep VERSION
          echo ""
          echo "=== Runner Image Details ==="
          cat /etc/lsb-release

      - name: Inspect toolcache
        run: |
          echo "=== Available Node.js versions in toolcache ==="
          ls $RUNNER_TOOL_CACHE/node/ 2>/dev/null || echo "No cached Node versions"
          echo ""
          echo "=== Available Python versions ==="
          ls $RUNNER_TOOL_CACHE/Python/ 2>/dev/null || echo "No cached Python versions"

      - name: Test specific tool version
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '18'  # explicitly set to avoid relying on preinstalled version

      - name: Verify version
        run: node --version
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Runner runs on `ubuntu-22.04` specifically (not `ubuntu-latest`).
- [ ] Toolcache directory listing is inspected.
- [ ] `actions/setup-node@v4` successfully installs Node 18.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 21 (Self-Hosted Runners) for when GitHub-hosted runners don't have the required tools or network access; → Section 25 (Performance) for using toolcache to avoid repeated downloads.

</details>

### 🖥️ Section 21: Self-Hosted Runners & Configuration (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [16-Managing-Runners.md](16-Managing-Runners.md) (second half)
**Overview:**

- Self-hosted runner installation and setup

<details>
<summary>🖥️ Scenario 21-A: Register and Use a Self-Hosted Runner</summary>


**Objective:** Register a self-hosted runner on your local machine (or a VM), assign it custom labels, and run a workflow that targets it via label selection.

**Prerequisites:** Sections 1–20 complete; a Linux/macOS/Windows machine or VM with internet access; repository admin access.

**Context:** Self-hosted runners allow you to run workflows on your own infrastructure — useful for private network access, specialized hardware, faster storage, or cost optimization. The runner agent connects to GitHub via HTTPS (outbound only, no inbound port needed).

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Navigate to **Repository → Settings → Actions → Runners → New self-hosted runner**.
2. Choose your OS and follow the displayed instructions. The setup is:

```bash
# Create a directory for the runner
mkdir -p ~/actions-runner && cd ~/actions-runner

# Download the runner package (example for Linux x64 — use URL from the UI)
curl -o actions-runner-linux-x64.tar.gz -L \
  https://github.com/actions/runner/releases/download/v2.317.0/actions-runner-linux-x64-2.317.0.tar.gz

tar xzf ./actions-runner-linux-x64.tar.gz

# Configure (use the token from the UI — it expires in 60 minutes)
./config.sh \
  --url https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/YOUR_REPO \
  --token YOUR_RUNNER_REGISTRATION_TOKEN \
  --name my-local-runner \
  --labels self-hosted,local,fast-disk \
  --work _work

# Start the runner interactively (for testing)
./run.sh
```

3. Verify the runner appears as **Idle** in the repository settings.

4. Create `.github/workflows/self-hosted-demo.yml`:

```yaml
name: Self-Hosted Runner Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  on-self-hosted:
    # Target by labels — all labels must match
    runs-on: [self-hosted, local]
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Runner identity
        run: |
          echo "Hostname     : $(hostname)"
          echo "Working dir  : $(pwd)"
          echo "Available CPUs: $(nproc)"
          echo "Available RAM : $(free -h | grep Mem | awk '{print $2}')"
          echo "Disk space    : $(df -h . | tail -1 | awk '{print $4}') free"

      - name: Access local network resource
        run: |
          # Self-hosted runners can access internal network resources
          # that GitHub-hosted runners cannot
          echo "Private network access available from: $(hostname -I 2>/dev/null || echo 'N/A')"

      - name: Cleanup workspace
        if: always()
        run: |
          echo "Workspace at: ${{ github.workspace }}"
          # Self-hosted runners reuse workspaces by default
          # Clean up to avoid stale files
          find . -name "*.tmp" -delete 2>/dev/null || true
```

5. Trigger via `workflow_dispatch` and verify the job runs on your local machine.
6. Check the runner's `_work/` directory to see the workspace.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Runner appears as Idle in repository settings after `./config.sh`.
- [ ] `workflow_dispatch` trigger runs the job on your local machine.
- [ ] `hostname` command shows your machine's hostname, not a GitHub runner hostname.
- [ ] Job completes and runner returns to Idle state.

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Runner goes Offline immediately** → The runner process isn't running. Start it with `./run.sh` or install as a service with `./svc.sh install && ./svc.sh start`.
- **Job queued but not picked up** → Verify the label in `runs-on:` exactly matches a label assigned during `config.sh`. Labels are case-sensitive.

**Time Estimate:** 30–35 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>👥 Scenario 21-B: Runner Groups and Organization-Level Runners</summary>


**Objective:** Understand runner groups for restricting which repositories can use which runners (concepts and configuration — requires organization access).

**Context:** Runner groups control access: only specified repositories can target runners in a group. This is critical for enterprise security — you don't want a compromised fork workflow to run on production infrastructure runners.

**Detailed Steps (conceptual with runnable workflow):**

1. In an organization: **Settings → Actions → Runner groups → New runner group**.
2. Name the group (e.g., `production-runners`), restrict to selected repositories.
3. Move your runner into the group.

4. The workflow targets a group-restricted runner:

```yaml
name: Organization Runner Group Demo

on: workflow_dispatch

jobs:
  deploy:
    # Targets runners in the 'production-runners' group
    # (label-based targeting also works within groups)
    runs-on: [self-hosted, production]
    environment: production
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Verify production environment
        run: |
          echo "Running on production runner group"
          echo "Runner name: ${{ runner.name }}"

      - name: Deploy to production
        run: |
          echo "Production deployment from approved runner"
```

5. Attempt to run the same workflow from a fork — verify it's blocked.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Runner group restricts access to specified repositories only.
- [ ] Workflow from unauthorized repository is queued but never starts.
- [ ] Audit log shows the access denial.

**Time Estimate:** 15–20 minutes (plus setup time for organization access)

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 22 (Enterprise) for organization-level runner policies; → Section 24 (Security) for the security implications of runner compromise in CI/CD pipelines.

</details>
