<details>
<summary>📝 Scenario 28-A: Comprehensive Multi-Feature Workflow Assessment</summary>


**Objective:** Build a single production-grade workflow that integrates at minimum 8 GitHub Actions features covered in the study plan, demonstrating mastery of their interaction.

**Prerequisites:** All Sections 1–27 complete.

**Context:** The GH-200 exam frequently tests scenario-based questions where multiple features interact. This capstone scenario requires you to design a workflow integrating: matrix strategy, reusable workflows, environment protection, caching, job summaries, secrets, artifact publishing, and conditional execution — mirroring real exam scenario complexity.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Design the workflow architecture before writing YAML:
   - `strategy.matrix` to test on multiple Node.js versions
   - `needs:` to sequence build → test → deploy
   - `cache` to share node_modules across jobs
   - `environment: production` with approval gate
   - `GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY` for consolidated test + deploy reporting
   - `permissions:` scoped to minimum required per job

2. Implement `.github/workflows/capstone.yml`:

```yaml
name: Capstone Assessment Workflow

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  workflow_dispatch:

# Minimal default permissions — jobs opt in as needed
permissions: {}

jobs:
  # ── Job 1: Matrix build + test ──────────────────────────────
  test:
    strategy:
      fail-fast: false
      matrix:
        node: [18, 20]
        os: [ubuntu-latest, windows-latest]
        exclude:
          - os: windows-latest
            node: 18
    runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}
    permissions:
      contents: read
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: ${{ matrix.node }}

      - name: Cache node_modules
        uses: actions/cache@v4
        with:
          path: ~/.npm
          key: ${{ runner.os }}-node${{ matrix.node }}-${{ hashFiles('**/package-lock.json') }}
          restore-keys: ${{ runner.os }}-node${{ matrix.node }}-

      - name: Install and test
        id: test
        run: |
          echo "Testing on ${{ matrix.os }} / Node ${{ matrix.node }}"
          echo "passed=10" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "failed=0" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
        shell: bash

      - name: Test summary
        if: always()
        run: |
          cat >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY << EOF
          ### ${{ matrix.os }} / Node ${{ matrix.node }}
          - Passed: ${{ steps.test.outputs.passed }}
          - Failed: ${{ steps.test.outputs.failed }}
          EOF
        shell: bash

  # ── Job 2: Build artifact ────────────────────────────────────
  build:
    needs: test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: read
    outputs:
      artifact-name: ${{ steps.build.outputs.name }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - id: build
        run: |
          mkdir -p dist
          echo "Build ${{ github.run_number }}" > dist/app.js
          echo "name=app-v1.0.${{ github.run_number }}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: ${{ steps.build.outputs.name }}
          path: dist/
          retention-days: 7
          if-no-files-found: error

  # ── Job 3: Deploy to production (protected environment) ─────
  deploy:
    needs: build
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: production
    concurrency:
      group: deploy-production
      cancel-in-progress: false  # never cancel in-flight production deploys
    permissions:
      contents: read
      id-token: write  # for OIDC
    steps:
      - uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
        with:
          name: ${{ needs.build.outputs.artifact-name }}
          path: dist/

      - name: Deploy
        env:
          DEPLOY_ENV: production
        run: echo "Deploying $(cat dist/app.js) to $DEPLOY_ENV"

      - name: Deployment summary
        if: always()
        run: |
          cat >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY << EOF
          ## 🚀 Deployment
          - Artifact: ${{ needs.build.outputs.artifact-name }}
          - Status: ${{ job.status }}
          - Actor: ${{ github.actor }}
          EOF
```

3. Run the workflow and verify in the Actions UI:
   - Dependency graph shows test → build → deploy
   - Matrix excludes `windows/node18`
   - Production deploy shows "Waiting for approval" (if environment configured)
   - Summary tab shows per-matrix test results + deployment status

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Matrix produces 3 combinations (ubuntu/18, ubuntu/20, windows/20) — 1 excluded.
- [ ] Build job only runs after all test matrix cells pass.
- [ ] Deploy job waits for approval (if environment configured with protection rules).
- [ ] Artifact is downloaded in deploy job via `needs.build.outputs.artifact-name`.
- [ ] Summary tab displays formatted reports from all jobs.
- [ ] `concurrency:` prevents parallel production deployments.

**Time Estimate:** 45–60 minutes

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>📋 Scenario 28-B: Practice Exam Question Gauntlet (10 Scenarios)</summary>


**Objective:** Work through 10 targeted scenario questions spanning key exam domains without YAML code — pure conceptual recall.

**Questions:**

1. A workflow uses `on: pull_request` targeting a forked repository. The workflow calls `secrets.MY_SECRET`. What value does the step receive? *(Answer: empty string — fork PRs don't have access to secrets by default)*

2. You need a workflow to run at 9:00 AM UTC every weekday. Write the cron expression. *(Answer: `0 9 * * 1-5`)*

3. A reusable workflow requires a `with.environment` input. The calling workflow doesn't pass it. What happens? *(Answer: If the input has `required: true`, the workflow fails with a validation error at parse time)*

4. You want `job-b` to run only if `job-a` failed. What syntax do you use? *(Answer: `needs: [job-a]` + `if: failure()`)*

5. What is the maximum retention period for GitHub Actions artifacts on a public repository? *(Answer: 90 days)*

6. A matrix job has `fail-fast: false` and `continue-on-error: true`. One cell fails. What happens to the workflow run conclusion? *(Answer: The workflow succeeds — `continue-on-error: true` means the job failure doesn't fail the workflow)*

7. You write `${{ github.event.pull_request.title }}` directly in a `run:` step's shell command. What security risk does this introduce? *(Answer: Script injection — an attacker can craft a PR title with shell metacharacters)*

8. A composite action wants to run a JavaScript file. Is this supported? *(Answer: No — composite actions support only `run:` steps and `uses:` steps calling other actions, not direct JavaScript execution. Use a JavaScript action for that.)*

9. What permission does a job need to call `gh pr comment`? *(Answer: `pull-requests: write`)*

10. An `on: schedule` workflow runs at midnight but your job takes 25 minutes. Your next scheduled run is at 12:01 AM. What happens? *(Answer: GitHub Actions queues the run — concurrent scheduled runs are allowed, they don't cancel each other)*

**Time Estimate:** 20–30 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → All sections — this is a comprehensive review assessment.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>☁️ Scenario 28-C: Advanced IaC Patterns with GitHub Actions Orchestration</summary>


**Objective:** Orchestrate complex Infrastructure as Code deployments using GitHub Actions with Terraform/CloudFormation.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 28-B complete.

**Context:** Enterprise infrastructure requires coordinated multi-region, multi-account deployments with state management.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create modular Terraform configurations
2. Build workflow that plans infrastructure across multiple environments
3. Implement approval gates before apply
4. Handle state file management (locking, versioning)
5. Validate and apply infrastructure changes

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: IaC Orchestration - Multi-Region Deploy
on:
  push:
    paths:
      - 'infrastructure/**'
      - '.github/workflows/iac*.yml'
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      action:
        type: choice
        options: [plan, apply, destroy]
jobs:
  terraform-plan:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    strategy:
      matrix:
        environment: [dev, staging, prod]
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Terraform
        uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2
        with:
          terraform_version: 1.6.0

      - name: Initialize Terraform - ${{ matrix.environment }}
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}
          terraform init -backend=true

      - name: Validate configuration
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}
          terraform validate

      - name: Plan infrastructure changes
        id: plan
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}
          terraform plan -out=tfplan -lock=true

      - name: Save plan artifact
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
        with:
          name: tfplan-${{ matrix.environment }}
          path: infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}/tfplan

      - name: Comment PR with plan summary
        if: github.event_name == 'pull_request'
        uses: actions/github-script@v7
        with:
          script: |
            const fs = require('fs');
            const planOutput = 'Plan summary: ${{ steps.plan.outputs.stdout }}';
            github.rest.issues.createComment({
              issue_number: context.issue.number,
              owner: context.repo.owner,
              repo: context.repo.repo,
              body: '```\n' + planOutput + '\n```'
            });

  terraform-apply:
    needs: terraform-plan
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: production-approval
    strategy:
      matrix:
        environment: [dev, staging, prod]
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Download plan artifact
        uses: actions/download-artifact@v3
        with:
          name: tfplan-${{ matrix.environment }}
          path: infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}/

      - name: Apply infrastructure - ${{ matrix.environment }}
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}
          terraform apply -auto-approve tfplan

      - name: Export outputs
        id: outputs
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/${{ matrix.environment }}
          terraform output -json > outputs.json
          echo "Outputs saved"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Terraform plans generate for all environments
- [ ] Configuration validation succeeds
- [ ] Approval gate enforces review before production
- [ ] Apply only executes after approval
- [ ] State files locked during operations

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Terraform initialized
Validation passed
Plan: 5 to add, 2 to change, 1 to destroy
Applied successfully
Outputs saved
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **State lock conflict:** Check for concurrent runs; increase lock timeout
- **Approval not enforcing:** Verify environment protection rules
- **Plan artifact missing:** Ensure upload happens before apply job

**Time Estimate:** 35–40 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 8 (Secrets) for sensitive variables; → Section 22 (Enterprise) for multi-account governance.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔄 Scenario 28-D: Drift Detection and Auto-Remediation Workflows</summary>


**Objective:** Detect infrastructure drift from intended state and automatically remediate divergences.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 28-C complete.

**Context:** Infrastructure drift causes configuration inconsistencies. Automated detection and remediation maintains compliance.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Schedule drift detection workflow
2. Compare current infrastructure against desired state
3. Identify divergences (removed resources, modified configs)
4. Log drift events with severity
5. Trigger auto-remediation for non-critical drift
6. Notify team for manual review of critical drift

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Infrastructure Drift Detection
on:
  schedule:
    - cron: '0 */12 * * *'  # Every 12 hours
  workflow_dispatch:
jobs:
  detect-drift:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Refresh state
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/prod
          terraform init
          terraform refresh

      - name: Check for drift
        id: drift
        continue-on-error: true
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/prod
          DRIFT_OUTPUT=$(terraform plan -json 2>&1)
          if echo "$DRIFT_OUTPUT" | grep -q 'to change\|to destroy'; then
            echo "drift_detected=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
            echo "Changes detected in infrastructure"
          else
            echo "drift_detected=false" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          fi

      - name: Save drift report
        if: steps.drift.outputs.drift_detected == 'true'
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/prod
          terraform plan > drift-report.txt
          cat drift-report.txt

      - name: Upload drift report
        if: steps.drift.outputs.drift_detected == 'true'
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
        with:
          name: drift-report
          path: infrastructure/prod/drift-report.txt

  remediate-drift:
    needs: detect-drift
    if: failure() == false
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Classify drift severity
        id: severity
        run: |
          # Heuristic: count changes to classify severity
          echo "severity=medium" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          echo "auto_remediate=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Auto-remediate non-critical drift
        if: steps.severity.outputs.auto_remediate == 'true'
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/prod
          terraform apply -auto-approve
          echo "Drift remediated automatically"

      - name: Notify team of remediation
        run: |
          echo "Drift remediation completed"
          echo "Resources resynchronized to desired state"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Drift detection runs on schedule
- [ ] All resource types checked
- [ ] Drift report generated and saved
- [ ] Auto-remediation executes for allowed changes
- [ ] Team notified of significant drift

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Checking for drift...
Changes detected in infrastructure
Drift remediation completed
Resources resynchronized to desired state
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **False positives:** Adjust plan parsing to exclude cosmetic changes
- **Remediation blocked:** Check IAM permissions and approval rules
- **Schedule doesn't run:** Verify cron syntax and workflow enabled

**Time Estimate:** 30–35 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 5 (Triggers) for scheduled workflows; → Section 15 (Debugging) for drift analysis.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🌍 Scenario 28-E: Multi-Environment Orchestration with IaC</summary>


**Objective:** Coordinate infrastructure deployments across dev → staging → prod with validation gates and rollback capability.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 28-D complete.

**Context:** Enterprise deployments require careful orchestration across environments with safety checks and rollback procedures.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Define environment progression (dev → staging → prod)
2. Create approval gates between environments
3. Implement smoke tests to validate each environment
4. Set up automatic rollback on test failure
5. Track deployment history for audit

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Multi-Environment IaC Orchestration
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
    paths:
      - 'infrastructure/**'
jobs:
  deploy-dev:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: development
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Deploy to dev
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/dev
          terraform init
          terraform apply -auto-approve

      - name: Run dev smoke tests
        run: |
          echo "Testing dev environment..."
          curl -f http://dev-api.internal/health || exit 1
          echo "Dev environment healthy"

  deploy-staging:
    needs: deploy-dev
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: staging-approval
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Deploy to staging
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/staging
          terraform init
          terraform apply -auto-approve

      - name: Run staging smoke tests
        id: tests
        continue-on-error: true
        run: |
          echo "Testing staging environment..."
          sleep 2
          echo "Staging tests passed"

      - name: Rollback if tests fail
        if: steps.tests.outcome == 'failure'
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/staging
          echo "Tests failed, initiating rollback..."
          terraform destroy -auto-approve
          exit 1

  deploy-prod:
    needs: deploy-staging
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment: production-approval
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v2

      - name: Final pre-prod validation
        run: |
          echo "Running pre-deployment checks..."
          echo "✓ Security scan passed"
          echo "✓ Configuration validated"
          echo "✓ Dependencies verified"

      - name: Deploy to production
        run: |
          cd infrastructure/prod
          terraform init
          terraform apply -auto-approve

      - name: Run prod smoke tests
        run: |
          echo "Testing production environment..."
          curl -f https://api.example.com/health || exit 1
          echo "Production environment healthy"

      - name: Update deployment tracking
        run: |
          echo "Deployment completed and verified"
          echo "Deployment timestamp: $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)"
          echo "Deployed by: ${{ github.actor }}"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Each environment deploys in sequence
- [ ] Approval gates enforce manual review
- [ ] Smoke tests validate each environment
- [ ] Rollback executes on test failure
- [ ] Deployment history tracked
- [ ] Prod deployment only proceeds after staging validation

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Deploying to dev...
Dev environment healthy
Deploying to staging...
Staging tests passed
Deploying to production...
Production environment healthy
Deployment completed and verified
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Approval not enforcing:** Check environment protection rules
- **Smoke tests failing:** Review test logic and environment configuration
- **Rollback incomplete:** Verify destroy permissions and state management
- **Deployment stuck:** Check for manual approvals pending

**Time Estimate:** 40–45 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 8 (Secrets) for environment-specific credentials; → Section 22 (Enterprise) for approval workflows.

</details>

### 📋 Section 29: Mock Exam - Full Practice Test (2 hrs)

**Topics:** [question-prompt.md](question-prompt.md) - Generate practice questions

- Full 100-question practice exam
- Covers all 5 exam domains

- Complete mock exam in 2 hours
- Identify weak knowledge areas
- Review explanations for all incorrect answers
- Track improvement from earlier assessments


<details>
<summary>⏱️ Scenario 29-A: Timed Mock Exam Protocol (2 Hours)</summary>


**Objective:** Simulate actual exam conditions — time-boxed, no notes, and score yourself honestly to produce an actionable weakness report.

**Prerequisites:** All Sections 1–28 complete.

**Context:** The GH-200 exam is 100 questions in 2 hours (average 72 seconds per question). Questions fall into 5 domains: Author and Maintain Workflows (~50%), Consume Workflows (~15%), Author and Maintain Actions (~20%), Manage GitHub Actions (environments, runners, billing) (~15%). The pass mark is 71%.

**Exam Protocol:**

1. **Set a 2-hour countdown timer** before starting.
2. Open `question-prompt.md` and generate a 100-question practice set.
3. Answer each question by writing your answer (A/B/C/D or True/False) in a separate document — do not look anything up.
4. Mark flagged/uncertain questions with a `?` to review if time allows.
5. After 2 hours, stop regardless of progress.

**Scoring Template:**

```markdown
## Mock Exam Score Sheet — Attempt [N]

**Date:** [YYYY-MM-DD]
**Time taken:** [X hours Y minutes]
**Target score:** 71+

| Domain                              | Questions | Correct | Score |
|-------------------------------------|-----------|---------|-------|
| Author & Maintain Workflows         | ~50       |         | %     |
| Consume Workflows                   | ~15       |         | %     |
| Author & Maintain Actions           | ~20       |         | %     |
| Manage GitHub Actions               | ~15       |         | %     |
| **TOTAL**                           | **100**   |         | **%** |

## Missed Questions Analysis

| # | Topic | Why Missed | Action |
|---|-------|-----------|--------|
|   |       |           |        |

## Weak Areas (< 70% in domain)
-
-

## Next Steps
- [ ] Review sections:
- [ ] Rebuild workflow for:
- [ ] Re-quiz on:
```

5. After scoring, identify any domain scoring below 70% — those are your priority review areas before the next mock or the actual exam.

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Exam completed in exactly 2 hours (no overtime).
- [ ] Score sheet filled in with per-domain breakdown.
- [ ] Missed question analysis completed for all wrong answers.
- [ ] Specific sections identified for targeted review.
- [ ] Score is >71% (or specific sections identified if not).

**Troubleshooting / Common Exam Pitfalls:**

| Pitfall | Correct Understanding |
|---------|----------------------|
| Confusing `on: workflow_call` with `on: workflow_dispatch` | `workflow_call` = called by another workflow; `workflow_dispatch` = manual trigger |
| `GITHUB_TOKEN` scope for fork PRs | Fork PRs get `pull-requests: read` only, not write |
| `needs:` context vs `steps:` context | `needs.JOB.outputs.KEY` uses job outputs; `steps.STEP.outputs.KEY` uses step outputs within same job |
| Default shell on Windows | PowerShell, not bash — add `shell: bash` for cross-platform scripts |
| Artifact retention defaults | Default: 90 days (public repos), configurable 1–90 days |

**Time Estimate:** 2 hours exam + 30 minutes scoring and analysis

</details>

<summary>🎯 Scenario 29-B: Weak Area Drill — Targeted Workflow Reconstruction</summary>


**Objective:** For each domain you scored below 70% in Scenario 29-A, write one workflow from memory without referencing notes, then verify it against documentation.

**Drill Template (repeat per weak area):**

1. **Pick the lowest-scoring domain topic** (e.g., "reusable workflow secrets passing").
2. **Set a 15-minute timer.**
3. **Write the workflow YAML from memory** targeting that specific feature.
4. **Verify** by checking the relevant study plan section and comparing.
5. **Note any errors** in your scoring sheet under "Why Missed."

**Example Drill — Reusable Workflow with Secrets:**

```yaml
# Caller — write this from memory, then verify
name: Caller
on: push
jobs:
  call:
    uses: ./.github/workflows/reusable.yml
    secrets:
      API_KEY: ${{ secrets.API_KEY }}

# Called — write this from memory, then verify
name: Reusable
on:
  workflow_call:
    secrets:
      API_KEY:
        required: true
jobs:
  use-secret:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - run: echo "Key length ${#API_KEY}"
        env:
          API_KEY: ${{ secrets.API_KEY }}
```

**Time Estimate:** 15 minutes per weak area × number of weak areas

<details>
<summary>🚀 Scenario 29-C: Blue-Green and Canary Deployments</summary>


**Objective:** Implement blue-green and canary deployment strategies to minimize downtime and risk.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 29-B complete.

**Context:** Advanced deployment patterns reduce risk by allowing quick rollback and gradual traffic shifting.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Set up blue (current) and green (new) environments
2. Deploy new version to green environment
3. Run smoke tests on green
4. Implement traffic shifting strategy (immediate for blue-green, gradual for canary)
5. Monitor error rates and metrics during deployment
6. Rollback if issues detected

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Blue-Green Deployment
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      deployment_strategy:
        type: choice
        options: [blue-green, canary]
jobs:
  deploy-green:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Build application
        run: |
          echo "Building application v${{ github.run_number }}..."
          mkdir -p build
          echo "app-v${{ github.run_number }}" > build/version.txt

      - name: Deploy to green environment
        run: |
          echo "Deploying to green environment..."
          echo "Green URL: https://green.example.com"
          echo "Version: $(cat build/version.txt)"

      - name: Run green smoke tests
        id: green-tests
        continue-on-error: true
        run: |
          echo "Running smoke tests on green..."
          sleep 2
          echo "✓ Health check passed"
          echo "✓ Critical paths tested"
          echo "✓ Database connectivity verified"
          echo "green_healthy=true" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Shift traffic strategy
        if: steps.green-tests.outputs.green_healthy == 'true'
        run: |
          STRATEGY=${{ github.event.inputs.deployment_strategy }}
          if [ "$STRATEGY" = "blue-green" ]; then
            echo "Executing immediate blue-green cutover..."
            echo "100% traffic → green environment"
            echo "Blue environment available for rollback"
          elif [ "$STRATEGY" = "canary" ]; then
            echo "Executing canary deployment..."
            echo "5% traffic → green environment"
            echo "95% traffic → blue environment (current)"
          fi

      - name: Monitor deployment
        if: steps.green-tests.outputs.green_healthy == 'true'
        run: |
          echo "Monitoring deployment metrics..."
          for i in {1..30}; do
            echo "[Check $i/30] Error rate: 0.02%, P95 latency: 145ms"
            sleep 1
          done
          echo "Deployment stable"

  rollback:
    needs: deploy-green
    if: failure()
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Initiate rollback
        run: |
          echo "Deployment failed, initiating rollback..."
          echo "Reverting 100% traffic to blue environment"
          echo "Green environment stopped"
          echo "Rollback completed at $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Green environment deploys successfully
- [ ] Smoke tests pass on green
- [ ] Traffic shifts according to strategy
- [ ] Metrics monitored during deployment
- [ ] Rollback executes immediately if issues detected

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Deploying to green environment...
Running smoke tests on green...
Executing immediate blue-green cutover...
100% traffic → green environment
Monitoring deployment metrics...
Deployment stable
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Green deployment fails:** Review build logs and environment configuration
- **Smoke tests fail:** Debug application health checks
- **Traffic shift incomplete:** Check load balancer configuration
- **Rollback too slow:** Optimize rollback procedure

**Time Estimate:** 35–40 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 20 (Runners) for deployment infrastructure; → Section 25 (Performance) for monitoring during deployment.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🔄 Scenario 29-D: Rollback Automation and Failure Recovery</summary>


**Objective:** Build automated rollback procedures that execute when deployment health checks fail.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 29-C complete.

**Context:** Automatic rollback minimizes MTTR (Mean Time To Recovery) when deployments cause issues.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Deploy new version
2. Run comprehensive health checks
3. Monitor error rates and performance metrics
4. If metrics exceed thresholds, trigger automatic rollback
5. Verify rollback success
6. Notify team

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Deployment with Automatic Rollback
on: push
jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Deploy new version
        id: deploy
        run: |
          echo "Deploying version ${{ github.sha }}..."
          echo "Deployment URL: https://app.example.com"
          echo "deployed_version=${{ github.sha }}" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

  health-check:
    needs: deploy
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Run comprehensive health checks
        id: health
        continue-on-error: true
        run: |
          echo "Running post-deployment health checks..."
          ERROR_RATE=$(( RANDOM % 5 ))
          P95_LATENCY=$(( 100 + RANDOM % 100 ))

          echo "Error rate: ${ERROR_RATE}%"
          echo "P95 latency: ${P95_LATENCY}ms"

          ERROR_THRESHOLD=2
          LATENCY_THRESHOLD=150

          if [ $ERROR_RATE -gt $ERROR_THRESHOLD ]; then
            echo "health_status=unhealthy" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
            exit 1
          elif [ $P95_LATENCY -gt $LATENCY_THRESHOLD ]; then
            echo "health_status=unhealthy" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
            exit 1
          else
            echo "health_status=healthy" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
          fi

  rollback:
    needs: [deploy, health-check]
    if: failure()
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Detect failure reason
        run: |
          echo "Deployment health check failed"
          echo "Initiating automatic rollback..."

      - name: Rollback to previous version
        run: |
          echo "Rolling back to previous stable version..."
          echo "Previous version: ${{ github.event.before }}"

      - name: Verify rollback
        run: |
          echo "Verifying rollback..."
          sleep 3
          echo "✓ Rollback successful"
          echo "✓ Health checks passing"
          echo "✓ Service stable"

      - name: Notify team
        uses: actions/github-script@v7
        with:
          script: |
            github.rest.issues.createComment({
              issue_number: context.issue.number,
              owner: context.repo.owner,
              repo: context.repo.repo,
              body: '🚨 Automatic rollback executed due to health check failure'
            });
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Health checks execute after deployment
- [ ] Metrics compared against thresholds
- [ ] Rollback triggers automatically on threshold breach
- [ ] Rollback completes within 5 minutes
- [ ] Team notified of rollback
- [ ] Post-rollback health checks verify stability

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Running post-deployment health checks...
Error rate: 3%
Health check failed
Initiating automatic rollback...
Rolling back to previous stable version...
Rollback successful
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Thresholds too sensitive:** Adjust error rate and latency limits
- **Rollback hangs:** Check deployment tool configuration
- **Notifications not sent:** Verify notification channel setup
- **Previous version unavailable:** Maintain versioned deployment artifacts

**Time Estimate:** 30–35 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 15 (Debugging) for metrics collection; → Section 26 (Troubleshooting) for failure analysis.

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>🚩 Scenario 29-E: Progressive Delivery and Feature Flags</summary>


**Objective:** Deploy new features behind feature flags to enable progressive rollout and easy rollback.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 29-D complete.

**Context:** Feature flags decouple deployment from release, allowing safe progressive rollout and instant rollback.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Create feature flag configuration
2. Deploy code with feature behind flag (disabled by default)
3. Gradually enable flag for increasing user percentages
4. Monitor metrics at each rollout stage
5. Complete rollout or rollback based on metrics

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Progressive Feature Rollout
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      feature_name:
        description: 'Feature flag to rollout'
        default: 'new_checkout_flow'
jobs:
  deploy-with-flag:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Create feature flag configuration
        run: |
          cat > feature-flags.json <<'EOF'
          {
            "new_checkout_flow": {
              "enabled": false,
              "rollout_percentage": 0,
              "created_at": "$(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)"
            }
          }
          EOF
          cat feature-flags.json

      - name: Deploy code with feature (disabled)
        run: |
          echo "Deploying new feature code..."
          echo "Feature: ${{ github.event.inputs.feature_name }}"
          echo "Rollout: 0% (disabled)"
          echo "Deployment complete"

  rollout-stage-1:
    needs: deploy-with-flag
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Enable feature for 5% users
        run: |
          echo "Enabling ${{ github.event.inputs.feature_name }} for 5% of users..."
          echo "Rollout percentage: 5%"
          echo "Estimated users affected: ~500"

      - name: Monitor metrics (5 minutes)
        run: |
          echo "Monitoring metrics for 5 minutes..."
          for i in {1..5}; do
            echo "[Minute $i] Error rate: 0.1%, Conversion: 2.1%, Load: 42%"
            sleep 5
          done
          echo "Metrics stable at 5% rollout"

  rollout-stage-2:
    needs: rollout-stage-1
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Enable feature for 25% users
        run: |
          echo "Expanding to 25% of users..."
          echo "Rollout percentage: 25%"
          echo "Estimated users affected: ~2,500"

      - name: Monitor metrics (5 minutes)
        run: |
          echo "Monitoring metrics for 5 minutes..."
          for i in {1..5}; do
            echo "[Minute $i] Error rate: 0.1%, Conversion: 2.1%, Load: 58%"
            sleep 5
          done
          echo "Metrics stable at 25% rollout"

  rollout-stage-3:
    needs: rollout-stage-2
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Enable feature for 100% users
        run: |
          echo "Rolling out to 100% of users..."
          echo "Rollout percentage: 100%"
          echo "Feature fully released"

      - name: Final monitoring (10 minutes)
        run: |
          echo "Final monitoring of full rollout..."
          for i in {1..10}; do
            echo "[Minute $i] Error rate: 0.1%, Conversion: 2.2%, Load: 78%"
            sleep 5
          done
          echo "Rollout complete and stable"

  emergency-rollback:
    needs: rollout-stage-3
    if: failure()
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Disable feature immediately
        run: |
          echo "Emergency: Disabling feature flag..."
          echo "Feature: ${{ github.event.inputs.feature_name }}"
          echo "Rollout percentage: 0%"
          echo "Feature disabled"

      - name: Verify rollback
        run: |
          echo "Verifying rollback..."
          echo "✓ Feature disabled for all users"
          echo "✓ Error rate returned to normal"
          echo "✓ Service stable"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Feature deployed with flag disabled
- [ ] Gradual rollout through stages (5% → 25% → 100%)
- [ ] Metrics monitored at each stage
- [ ] Rollout continues only if metrics healthy
- [ ] Emergency rollback available at any stage
- [ ] Full rollout completes without errors

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Enabling new_checkout_flow for 5% of users...
Metrics stable at 5% rollout
Expanding to 25% of users...
Metrics stable at 25% rollout
Rolling out to 100% of users...
Rollout complete and stable
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Metrics not available:** Verify monitoring system integration
- **Rollout takes too long:** Consider increasing stage percentages
- **Feature flag not updating:** Check flag management service (LaunchDarkly, etc.)
- **Rollback doesn't disable feature:** Verify flag update permissions

**Time Estimate:** 40–45 minutes

**Cross-Section Connections:** → Section 7 (Environment Configuration) for feature flag variables; → Section 25 (Performance) for metrics monitoring.

</details>

<details>
<summary>📖 Scenario 30-A: Personal Quick Reference Guide Construction</summary>


**Objective:** Build a one-page (or single-screen) cheat sheet of the most frequently-tested GitHub Actions facts, syntax patterns, and gotchas — in your own words.

**Prerequisites:** All Sections 1–29 complete; Section 29 weak area analysis in hand.

**Context:** Research consistently shows that the act of constructing a reference guide (not just reading one) consolidates memory better than passive review. This scenario is about the construction process, not the output document.

**Quick Reference Template:**

```markdown
# GitHub Actions GH-200 Quick Reference

## Trigger Syntax (on:)
| Event              | Key Options                        |
|--------------------|------------------------------------|
| push               | branches, tags, paths              |
| pull_request       | types, branches, paths             |
| schedule           | cron: '0 9 * * 1-5' (Mon–Fri 9AM) |
| workflow_dispatch  | inputs: (string/bool/choice/env)   |
| workflow_call      | inputs: + secrets: (required/optional) |
| workflow_run       | workflows: ['Name'], types: [completed] |

## Context Reference
| Context          | Example Use                               |
|------------------|-------------------------------------------|
| github.sha       | Current commit SHA                        |
| github.ref       | refs/heads/main                           |
| github.event_name| push, pull_request, workflow_dispatch     |
| github.actor     | Username who triggered the run            |
| needs.JOB.outputs.KEY | Cross-job output passing           |
| steps.STEP.outputs.KEY | Same-job step output             |
| secrets.NAME     | Secret value (empty in fork PRs)          |
| vars.NAME        | Repository/org/environment variable       |
| env.NAME         | Workflow/job/step environment variable    |

## Job Control
- needs: [job-a, job-b]          # run after both complete
- if: failure()                   # run only if a needed job failed
- if: always()                    # run regardless of status
- continue-on-error: true         # don't fail workflow if this job fails
- timeout-minutes: 30             # default: 360 (6 hours)

## Special Files (Environment Files)
| File                | Purpose                          |
|---------------------|----------------------------------|
| $GITHUB_OUTPUT      | Set step outputs (key=value)     |
| $GITHUB_ENV         | Set env vars for subsequent steps|
| $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY| Append markdown to job summary   |
| $GITHUB_PATH        | Prepend directories to PATH      |

## Permissions
- Default: read for most + write for contents on workflow triggers
- Set permissions: {} to lock down, then grant per-job
- Fork PRs: pull-requests is read-only regardless of settings
- id-token: write — required for OIDC

## Action Types
| Type       | Defined by        | Runs on  |
|------------|-------------------|----------|
| JavaScript | action.yml + JS   | Runner   |
| Docker     | action.yml + Dockerfile | Container |
| Composite  | action.yml (steps:) | Runner  |

## Common Gotchas
1. `env:` at workflow level ≠ available in `on:` or `defaults:`
2. `needs:` context only in jobs that list those as dependencies
3. Fork PRs: secrets empty, pull-requests write blocked
4. Cron: based on UTC, not local time
5. `workflow_run`: triggered by another workflow's run, not its content
6. Composite actions: cannot use `env:` at action level (only at step level)
7. Matrix `include`: adds a new cell, doesn't modify existing ones
8. `cancel-in-progress: false` recommended for production deployments
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Quick reference covers all 5 exam domains.
- [ ] Every entry is written from memory first, then verified.
- [ ] Gotchas section includes at least 5 items from your personal weak areas.
- [ ] Reference fits on 1–2 pages when printed.

**Time Estimate:** 45–60 minutes

</details>

<details>
<summary>🎯 Scenario 30-B: Exam Day Protocol and Final Readiness Verification</summary>


**Objective:** Confirm technical readiness with a final 20-question speed drill, and establish an exam day strategy.

**20-Question Speed Drill (2 minutes each — 40 minutes total):**

Answer these without referencing any material:

1. Minimum cron schedule frequency in GitHub Actions? *(Every 5 minutes)*
2. Which `on:` event triggers a workflow when called by another workflow? *(`workflow_call`)*
3. How do you pass an output from step `build` to the next step in the same job? *(`${{ steps.build.outputs.KEY }}`)*
4. What's the maximum number of jobs in a matrix? *(256)*
5. Which permission allows `gh pr comment`? *(`pull-requests: write`)*
6. What syntax runs a job regardless of other jobs' failure? *(`if: always()`)*
7. How do you prevent a cron workflow from running if the previous run is still active? *(concurrency with `cancel-in-progress: true`)*
8. What file type defines a JavaScript action? *(`action.yml` in the root of the action repo)*
9. Default artifact retention for private repos? *(90 days)*
10. How do environment variables set in `$GITHUB_ENV` differ from `env:` in the step? *(`$GITHUB_ENV` persists to all subsequent steps; `env:` in step is step-scoped only)*
11. Which action type supports running shell scripts without a `Dockerfile`? *(Composite)*
12. What happens to `${{ secrets.MY_SECRET }}` in a fork PR workflow? *(Returns empty string)*
13. How do you declare a reusable workflow's required input? *(`inputs: NAME: required: true` under `on: workflow_call:`)*
14. What's the correct way to reference a reusable workflow in the same repository? *(`uses: ./.github/workflows/name.yml`)*
15. Which context provides the SHA of the commit that triggered the workflow? *(`github.sha`)*
16. How do you limit parallel matrix jobs to 3 at a time? *(`max-parallel: 3` under `strategy:`)*
17. What does `fail-fast: false` do in a matrix strategy? *(Allows all matrix cells to complete even if one fails)*
18. Which event type should you use to trigger a workflow after another workflow completes? *(`on: workflow_run`)*
19. What permission does OIDC token generation require? *(`id-token: write`)*
20. How do you pin an action to an immutable reference? *(Use commit SHA: `uses: owner/action@SHA # v1.2.3`)*

**Exam Day Checklist:**

- [ ] Exam environment loaded and tested (browser, stable internet)
- [ ] Quick reference guide printed or on second screen
- [ ] Rested and not cramming the morning of
- [ ] Strategy: answer all questions, flag uncertain ones, review flagged at end
- [ ] Time management: 72 seconds average per question; move on if stuck

**Final Readiness Score:**

- 18–20 correct: Ready — expect 85%+
- 15–17 correct: Borderline — review missed topics, consider 1 more day
- <15 correct: Not ready — identify patterns in missed questions, spend 1–2 days drilling

**Time Estimate:** 40 minutes drill + 20 minutes exam prep review

**Cross-Section Connections:** → This section synthesizes all 29 preceding sections. If any drill answer above is uncertain, return to the corresponding section for a 20-minute targeted review.

</details>

<summary>⏱️ Scenario 30-C: Mock Exam Scenarios with Time Constraints</summary>


**Objective:** Practice full mock exam scenarios under timed conditions to build exam readiness.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 30-B complete.

**Context:** Time management is critical on certification exams. Practicing under realistic time constraints builds speed and accuracy.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Set 120-minute timer for full mock exam
2. Complete 60 scenario-based questions (2 min per question target)
3. Track time spent per question
4. Review answers and identify timing issues
5. Complete second timed run to measure improvement

**Detailed Workflow Example (Mock Exam Simulation):**

```yaml
name: Timed Mock Exam
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
jobs:
  mock-exam-session:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Start exam timer
        id: timer
        run: |
          echo "🎓 GitHub Actions GH-200 Mock Exam"
          echo "Total time: 120 minutes"
          echo "Number of questions: 60"
          echo "Time per question target: 2 minutes"
          echo ""
          echo "Exam started at: $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)"
          START_TIME=$(date +%s)
          echo "start_time=$START_TIME" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

      - name: Sample exam questions (timed)
        continue-on-error: true
        run: |
          echo "Question 1 (Workflow triggers): Time limit 2 min"
          echo "  A. How do you trigger a workflow on pull request?"
          echo "  B. What is the difference between 'on: pull_request' and 'on: pull_request_target'?"
          echo "  C. How do you filter pull requests by file path?"
          echo "Estimated time: 1:45"
          echo ""
          echo "Question 2 (Matrix strategy): Time limit 2 min"
          echo "  A. Build matrix for 3 Node versions × 2 OS × 2 architectures"
          echo "  B. Calculate total job count"
          echo "  C. How do you use 'include' to add a special case?"
          echo "Estimated time: 1:30"
          echo ""
          echo "Question 3 (Secrets management): Time limit 2 min"
          echo "  A. Compare GITHUB_TOKEN vs repository secrets vs org secrets"
          echo "  B. When should you use OIDC token?"
          echo "  C. How do you rotate secrets safely?"
          echo "Estimated time: 2:00"
          echo ""
          echo "[Questions 4-60 continue...]"

      - name: Track question timing
        run: |
          echo "Question Timing Report:"
          echo "Question | Category | Time Allocated | Estimated | Over/Under"
          echo "---------|----------|-----------------|-----------|----------"
          echo "1        | Triggers | 2:00           | 1:45      | ✓ Under"
          echo "2        | Matrix   | 2:00           | 1:30      | ✓ Under"
          echo "3        | Secrets  | 2:00           | 2:00      | ✓ On Time"
          echo "[...]"
          echo "Total: 120:00 allocated, estimated 115:20 used"

      - name: End exam timer
        run: |
          END_TIME=$(date +%s)
          echo "Exam completed at: $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ)"
          echo "Total time used: 118 minutes"
          echo "Time remaining: 2 minutes"

      - name: Generate exam report
        run: |
          cat > exam-results.json <<'EOF'
          {
            "exam_type": "GH-200 Mock Exam",
            "duration_minutes": 120,
            "questions_total": 60,
            "questions_answered": 58,
            "score_estimate": "86%",
            "time_management": "Excellent",
            "timing_breakdown": {
              "quick_answers_under_1_30": 15,
              "standard_1_30_to_2_30": 38,
              "extended_over_2_30": 5
            }
          }
          EOF
          cat exam-results.json
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Complete 60 questions in 120 minutes
- [ ] Average 2 minutes per question
- [ ] Avoid rushing on final questions
- [ ] Review answers and identify time sinks
- [ ] Improve timing on second attempt

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Exam started: 2026-04-19T14:00:00Z
Total time used: 118 minutes
Time remaining: 2 minutes
Score estimate: 86%
Time management: Excellent
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Running out of time:** Practice faster question reading and decision-making
- **Unsure about answers:** Flag for review and move on; return if time permits
- **Second-guessing answers:** Build confidence by drilling weak areas

**Time Estimate:** 120 minutes (full exam)

**Cross-Section Connections:** → All sections for comprehensive exam coverage.

</details>

<summary>🔍 Scenario 30-D: Gap Analysis and Targeted Review Recommendations</summary>


**Objective:** Analyze mock exam results to identify knowledge gaps and recommend focused remediation.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 30-C complete (mock exam taken).

**Context:** Strategic review of weak areas maximizes study efficiency before real exam.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Score mock exam
2. Categorize incorrect answers by topic
3. Identify knowledge gaps
4. Recommend specific sections for review
5. Prioritize high-impact topics
6. Create targeted study plan

**Detailed Workflow Example:**

```yaml
name: Gap Analysis and Study Recommendations
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      mock_score:
        description: 'Mock exam score (0-100)'
        default: '86'
jobs:
  analyze-gaps:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Analyze mock exam results
        id: analysis
        run: |
          SCORE=${{ github.event.inputs.mock_score }}
          echo "Mock Exam Score: ${SCORE}%"
          echo ""
          echo "Performance by Category:"
          echo "  Fundamentals: 92% ✓ Strong"
          echo "  Triggers & Events: 88% ✓ Good"
          echo "  Jobs & Strategies: 78% ⚠️ Needs Review"
          echo "  Artifacts & Caching: 82% ✓ Acceptable"
          echo "  Debugging: 76% ⚠️ Needs Review"
          echo "  Security: 85% ✓ Acceptable"
          echo ""
          echo "Incorrect Questions Analysis:"
          echo "  Q15: Matrix edge cases (topic: matrix strategies)"
          echo "  Q32: Cache invalidation patterns (topic: caching)"
          echo "  Q41: Debugging workflow failures (topic: debugging)"
          echo "  Q48: Complex conditionals (topic: logic)"
          echo "  Q56: Action versioning (topic: actions)"

      - name: Identify knowledge gaps
        run: |
          echo "📊 Knowledge Gap Report:"
          echo ""
          echo "🔴 Critical Gaps (Score <75%):"
          echo "  - Section 10 (Matrix): Score 78% (14/20)"
          echo "  - Section 15 (Debugging): Score 76% (15/20)"
          echo ""
          echo "🟡 Areas for Improvement (75-85%):"
          echo "  - Section 13 (Caching): Score 82% (16/20)"
          echo "  - Section 9 (Conditional Logic): Score 80% (16/20)"
          echo ""
          echo "🟢 Strong Areas (>85%):"
          echo "  - Section 1-5 (Fundamentals): 90%+"
          echo "  - Section 8 (Secrets): 85%"

      - name: Generate study recommendations
        run: |
          cat > study-plan.md <<'EOF'
          # Targeted Study Plan for Score Improvement

          ## Priority 1: Critical Gaps (Expected +8% improvement)
          - **Section 10:** Review Scenario 10-C (Dynamic Matrix), 10-D (Matrix Bugs), 10-E (Distributed Testing)
          - **Section 15:** Review Scenario 15-C (Step Debugging), 15-D (Local Reproduction), 15-E (Log Aggregation)
          - **Estimated time:** 2-3 hours
          - **Expected score after review:** 88%

          ## Priority 2: Areas for Improvement (Expected +4% improvement)
          - **Section 13:** Review Scenario 13-C (Cache Invalidation), 13-D (Cache Debugging)
          - **Section 9:** Review Scenario 9-D (Conditional Debugging)
          - **Estimated time:** 1-2 hours
          - **Expected score after review:** 92%

          ## Priority 3: Reinforcement (Expected +3% improvement)
          - **Section 19:** Custom action edge cases
          - **Section 23:** Advanced security patterns
          - **Estimated time:** 1 hour
          - **Expected score after review:** 95%

          ## Quick Reference: Most Tested Topics
          1. Matrix strategies (appears in 8% of questions)
          2. Debugging workflows (appears in 6% of questions)
          3. Secrets management (appears in 5% of questions)
          4. Artifact handling (appears in 4% of questions)
          5. Custom actions (appears in 4% of questions)

          ## Recommended Study Schedule
          - **Today:** Complete Priority 1 (Critical Gaps) - 2-3 hours
          - **Tomorrow:** Complete Priority 2 (Improvements) - 1-2 hours
          - **Day 3:** Practice Priority 3 & take second mock exam - 2 hours
          - **Total study time:** 5-7 hours
          - **Expected final score:** 92-95%
          EOF
          cat study-plan.md

      - name: Create action items
        run: |
          echo "📋 Immediate Action Items:"
          echo "  ☐ Review Section 10 Scenarios C, D, E (2 hours)"
          echo "  ☐ Review Section 15 Scenarios C, D, E (1.5 hours)"
          echo "  ☐ Complete practice questions for matrix topics (30 min)"
          echo "  ☐ Complete practice questions for debugging (30 min)"
          echo "  ☐ Take second mock exam to verify improvement (2 hours)"
          echo ""
          echo "📈 Success Criteria:"
          echo "  ✓ Score improvement of at least 5% on second attempt"
          echo "  ✓ Confidence level 8/10 or higher"
          echo "  ✓ Ready to schedule certification exam"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Knowledge gaps identified by category
- [ ] Specific sections recommended for review
- [ ] Study time estimated for each gap
- [ ] Quick reference of high-frequency topics created
- [ ] Action items prioritized by impact

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Knowledge Gap Report:
🔴 Critical Gaps: Section 10 (78%), Section 15 (76%)
🟡 Areas for Improvement: Section 13 (82%), Section 9 (80%)
🟢 Strong Areas: Sections 1-5 (90%+)

Recommended study time: 5-7 hours
Expected final score: 92-95%
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Unsure which sections to review:** Focus on Critical Gaps first (red categories)
- **Time limited:** Prioritize sections that appear most frequently on exam
- **Still struggling after review:** Consider getting mentor guidance or taking extended study break

**Time Estimate:** 30–45 minutes (analysis), plus study time based on recommendations

**Cross-Section Connections:** → All sections for comprehensive reference.

</details>

<details>
<summary>🎓 Scenario 30-E: Real-World Certification Exam Patterns and Strategies</summary>


**Objective:** Learn exam strategies and patterns to maximize score on certification day.

**Prerequisites:** Scenario 30-D complete (gap analysis done).

**Context:** Exam success depends not just on knowledge but also on test-taking strategy.

**Detailed Steps:**

1. Study common question patterns on GH-200 exam
2. Learn question types: scenario-based, troubleshooting, best practices
3. Develop time allocation strategy
4. Practice eliminating wrong answers
5. Plan pre-exam day routine
6. Execute exam day protocol

**Detailed Workflow Example (Exam Strategy Guide):**

```yaml
name: Certification Exam Success Strategy
on:
  workflow_dispatch:
jobs:
  exam-patterns:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Learn common exam patterns
        run: |
          cat > exam-patterns.md <<'EOF'
          # GH-200 Certification Exam Patterns

          ## Question Type Distribution
          - Scenario-based (40%): Complex real-world situations
          - Troubleshooting (30%): Fix broken workflows
          - Best practices (20%): Choose optimal approach
          - Configuration (10%): YAML syntax and setup

          ## Scenario Pattern Example
          "You're asked to optimize a 15-minute workflow that tests 3 versions of Node.js across 2 OS platforms..."
          → Look for matrix optimization opportunities
          → Consider caching strategy
          → Evaluate parallel execution

          ## Troubleshooting Pattern Example
          "A workflow fails with 'permission denied' error..."
          → Check GITHUB_TOKEN permissions
          → Review branch protection rules
          → Verify environment protection rules

          ## Best Practices Pattern
          "What is the recommended approach for managing secrets in a monorepo?"
          → Organization-level secrets
          → Environment protection rules
          → OIDC token for external services
          EOF
          cat exam-patterns.md

      - name: Time allocation strategy
        run: |
          echo "⏱️ Exam Time Allocation Strategy:"
          echo ""
          echo "Total time: 120 minutes"
          echo "Total questions: 60"
          echo ""
          echo "Allocation:"
          echo "  📖 Reading questions: 1 min per question = 60 min"
          echo "  🤔 Thinking/deciding: 0.5 min per question = 30 min"
          echo "  ✏️ Answering: 0.5 min per question = 30 min"
          echo "  🔄 Review & revise: 10 min (for flagged questions)"
          echo ""
          echo "Strategy:"
          echo "  1. First pass: Answer all easy questions (1 min each)"
          echo "  2. Second pass: Answer medium questions (2 min each)"
          echo "  3. Third pass: Work on hard questions (3+ min each)"
          echo "  4. Final pass: Review flagged questions"

      - name: Answer elimination strategy
        run: |
          echo "❌ Wrong Answer Elimination Strategy:"
          echo ""
          echo "Example Question:"
          echo "  Q: 'How do you pass data between jobs?'"
          echo "  A. Using GITHUB_ENV globally"
          echo "  B. Using outputs and needs context"
          echo "  C. Using workflow_run event"
          echo "  D. Using git commits"
          echo ""
          echo "Elimination Process:"
          echo "  ❌ A: Incorrect - GITHUB_ENV is step-level only"
          echo "  ✓ B: Correct - This is the intended pattern"
          echo "  ❌ C: Incorrect - workflow_run is for triggering, not passing data"
          echo "  ❌ D: Incorrect - Not a data passing mechanism"
          echo ""
          echo "✅ Answer: B"

      - name: Pre-exam day checklist
        run: |
          cat > pre-exam-checklist.md <<'EOF'
          # Pre-Exam Day Preparation

          ## 1 Week Before
          - [ ] Review Sections 10, 15, 23 (highest-frequency topics)
          - [ ] Take full timed mock exam
          - [ ] Score >85% to confirm readiness
          - [ ] Review gap analysis results

          ## 1 Day Before
          - [ ] Light review of quick reference (30 min)
          - [ ] Prepare testing environment
          - [ ] Get good sleep (8+ hours)
          - [ ] Avoid heavy study (rest is important)

          ## Exam Day Morning
          - [ ] Eat healthy breakfast
          - [ ] Exercise lightly (30 min walk)
          - [ ] Arrive at testing center 15 min early
          - [ ] Use bathroom before starting
          - [ ] Deep breath - you're prepared!
          EOF
          cat pre-exam-checklist.md

      - name: Exam day protocol
        run: |
          echo "📋 Exam Day Protocol:"
          echo ""
          echo "First 5 minutes:"
          echo "  1. Read exam instructions carefully"
          echo "  2. Note time start and calculate time end"
          echo "  3. Plan breaks (2 min per break × 3 = 6 min total)"
          echo "  4. Scan all questions to identify easy ones"
          echo ""
          echo "During exam:"
          echo "  ✓ Answer easier questions first (build confidence)"
          echo "  ✓ Flag uncertain answers for review"
          echo "  ✓ Don't over-think - first instinct usually correct"
          echo "  ✓ Skip very difficult questions initially"
          echo "  ✓ Budget 2 min per question on average"
          echo ""
          echo "Last 10 minutes:"
          echo "  ✓ Review flagged questions"
          echo "  ✓ Don't change answers unless certain"
          echo "  ✓ Make sure all questions answered"
          echo "  ✓ Final review of reasoning"
          echo ""
          echo "Success mantra: 'I am prepared. I can do this.'"

      - name: Post-exam reflection
        run: |
          echo "🎓 You've completed the GH-200 certification exam!"
          echo ""
          echo "Next steps:"
          echo "  1. Note which questions felt difficult"
          echo "  2. Wait for results (usually within 24 hours)"
          echo "  3. If passed: Celebrate! Your GitHub Actions expertise is certified."
          echo "  4. If not passed: Identify gaps and schedule retake (60 day waiting period)"
          echo ""
          echo "Exam strategy effectiveness:"
          echo "  ✓ Time management: Allow adequate time per question"
          echo "  ✓ Answer elimination: Help narrow down correct answers"
          echo "  ✓ Knowledge gaps: Focus study on weak areas"
          echo "  ✓ Confidence: Build through practice and preparation"
```

**Success Criteria:**

- [ ] Understand common exam question patterns
- [ ] Time allocation strategy planned
- [ ] Answer elimination techniques practiced
- [ ] Pre-exam checklist completed
- [ ] Exam day protocol understood
- [ ] Post-exam plan established

**Expected Output:**

```bash
Exam Patterns Learned
Time Allocation: 60/30/30 strategy
Answer Elimination: Practice 5-10 questions using technique
Pre-exam day: All checklist items completed
Exam day protocol: Ready to execute
```

**Troubleshooting:**

- **Anxiety before exam:** Practice relaxation techniques and remember your preparation
- **Time management during exam:** Practice with mock exams to build speed
- **Second-guessing answers:** Trust your preparation; your first instinct is usually correct
- **Need to retake:** Identify specific weak topics and focus on targeted practice

**Time Estimate:** 30–45 minutes (strategy review); then 120+ minutes (exam day)

**Cross-Section Connections:** → All sections for comprehensive exam coverage.

</details>

## Study Strategy & Tips

### Daily Checklist

- [ ] Read/watch assigned section content
- [ ] Complete hands-on practical work
- [ ] Answer quiz questions related to section
- [ ] Review and consolidate notes

### Knowledge Retention

- **Spaced Repetition:** Review topics 1 day, 3 days, 1 week later
- **Active Recall:** Quiz yourself without looking at notes
- **Practice Application:** Build actual workflows, not just theoretical work
- **Teaching Others:** Explain concepts to solidify understanding

### Weak Area Focus

- After each section quiz, identify topics scoring <80%
- Spend additional 30 mins on weak areas
- Re-do practice questions for those topics
- Build practice workflows targeting weak concepts

### Time Management

- **Intensive Track (10 days):** 3 sections/day, study 6 hours/day
- **Balanced Track (20 days):** 1.5 sections/day, study 3 hours/day
- **Relaxed Track (30 days):** 1 section/day, study 2 hours/day

### Success Criteria

- **Minimum:** >71% on practice exams consistently
- **Target:** >80% on practice exams (indicates 85%+ on actual exam)
- **Excellent:** >85% on practice exams (indicates 90%+ on actual exam)
